1401 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. McCoy


No. 2003-K-1948


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2003-1948 (La.App. 4 Cir. 03/03/04); 869 So. 2d 918; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 621



March 3, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 30, 2004.
Writ denied by State v. McCoy, 883 So. 2d 1044, 2004 La. LEXIS 3120 (La., Oct. 15, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPLICATION FOR WRITS DIRECTED TO CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT. ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 307-425, SECTION "E". HONORABLE CALVIN JOHNSON, JUDGE.
State v. McCoy, 515 So. 2d 445, 1987 La. LEXIS 10698 (La., 1987)



DISPOSITION: WRIT GRANTED; AMENDED SENTENCE VACATED; & ORIGINAL SENTENCE REINSTATED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of possession with the intent to distribute heroin and was sentenced to life imprisonment. Defendant filed a pro se motion to amend, modify, reduce, or vacate his life sentence. The Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish, Louisiana, granted defendant's motion and resentenced him to serve 30 years at hard labor. In a writ application, the State sought review of the trial court's ruling.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted and sentenced in 1986. Defendant filed his motion in 2003. The State argued that the trial court erred in vacating the defendant's life sentence and imposing a 30 year sentence as the trial court was precluded from amending the defendant's sentence at this point. The appellate court agreed and noted that under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art 881, the trial court could not amend defendant's sentence, and under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 822, defendant's sentence could not be modified. The appellate court held that in order for the trial court to be able to amend defendant's sentence, defendant would have had to move for an amendment prior to the commencement of the execution of the sentence. Likewise, a motion to modify his sentence had to be filed within 30 days of the imposition of the sentence. Further, defendant's sentence was not excessive, and therefore, not subject to correction pursuant to La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 882. Defendant did have recourse however pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:574.22, in that the Louisiana Risk Review Board could review defendant's sentence to see he was eligible for parole or clemency.


OUTCOME: The ruling of the trial court was reversed, the 30 year amended sentence was vacated, and the original life sentence was reinstated.

 

1402 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Engles v. City of New Orleans


No. 2003-CA-0692


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2003 0692 (La.App. 4 Cir. 02/25/04); 872 So. 2d 1166; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 432; 12 A.L.R.6th 905



February 25, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Rehearing denied by Engles v. City of New Orleans, 2004 La. App. LEXIS 1471 (La.App. 4 Cir., May 28, 2004)
Writ denied by Engles v. City of New Orleans, 882 So. 2d 1141, 2004 La. LEXIS 2904 (La., Sept. 24, 2004)
Rehearing denied by Engles v. City of New Orleans, 2004 La. App. LEXIS 2408 (La.App. 4 Cir., Sept. 30, 2004)
Writ denied by Engles v. City of New Orleans, 891 So. 2d 697, 2005 La. LEXIS 80 (La., Jan. 7, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 98-21448, DIVISION "N-8". HONRABLE ETHEL SIMMS JULIEN, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART & REVERSED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a husband and wife, brought premises liability and negligence claims against defendants, the city and the city sewerage and water board, when the husband hit a depression in the street and fell off of his bicycle, resulting in permanent brain damage. The Civil District Court of Orleans Parish, Louisiana, awarded the husband and wife damages for lost wages, medical expenses, and loss of consortium. The city and the board appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the city and the board contended the trial court erred in finding they had previously received notice as to the road's condition and in the damages awards. The appellate court found that the record provided sufficient testimony upon which the trial court could have reasonably concluded that the city and the board had notice of the defect. However, the appellate court also found that the city, and not the board, was completely at fault for causing the unreasonable risk of harm that caused the accident and the husband's resulting injuries. As the city was liable for the husband's injuries, his recovery was limited to general damages in the amount of $ 500,000 for total bodily injury recovery in toto, as per La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:5106. Considering the trauma of the accident and the husband's physical and mental suffering, the award, reduced to $ 500,000 under the cap, did not shock the conscience. The trial court's award for future lost wages and earning capacity was not an abuse of discretion, as it was more probable than not that, but for the accident, the husband would have pursued his education to obtain additional advanced degrees resulting in higher salaries.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed as to the board's liability, and the board and the husband were found not to be at fault. The general damages award was amended and reduced, and the wife's award for loss of consortium was reversed. Otherwise, the judgment was affirmed.

 

1403 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Cheron v. LCS Corr. Serv.


2002 CW 1049 R2


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2002 1049 (La. App. 1 Cir. 2/23/04); 872 So. 2d 1094; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 334



February 23, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ granted by Cheron v. LCS Corr. Servs., 872 So. 2d 532, 2004 La. LEXIS 1682 (La., May 14, 2004)
Affirmed by Cheron v. LCS Corr. Servs., 891 So. 2d 1250, 2005 La. LEXIS 130 (La., Jan. 19, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM THE NENTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT (NUMBER 486,044 "H"), PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE STATE OF LOUISIANA. HONORABLE J. MICHAEL MCDONALD, JUDGE.
Cheron v. LCS Corr. Servs., 847 So. 2d 1246, 2003 La. LEXIS 1974 (La., June 20, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Writ Denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Louisiana Supreme Court remanded the writ application filed by defendant, the State of Louisiana, through the Department of Public Safety and Corrections (department) after plaintiff inmate filed a personal injury action. The appellate court had previously denied the department's writ.


OVERVIEW: The inmate filed a personal injury action against the department for injuries he sustained, including a potentially fatal kidney disease. The department filed a dilatory exception raising the objection of prematurity, asserting that the inmate failed to exhaust administrative remedies, as required by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 15:1172 and 15:1184. The trial court denied both exceptions, and the department filed a writ application. The merits of the application were denied by the appellate court, and the supreme court later remanded the matter to the appellate court. The appellate court once again denied the department's exceptions, holding that retroactive application of 2002 La. Acts 89 (Act 89) to the inmate's tort action would have unconstitutionally disturbed his vested rights. The inmate was not required to comply with the unconstitutional procedure that existed prior to Act 89. Thus, his tort action was not filed prematurely. Additionally, the inmate's petition was not vague or ambiguous because it did not provide an administrative procedure number.


OUTCOME: The court denied the writ application.

 

1404 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Dailey v. Travis


2002 CW 2051R


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2002 2051 (La.App. 1 Cir. 02/23/04); 872 So. 2d 1104; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 349



February 23, 2004, Date of Judgment


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ granted by Dailey v. Travis, 872 So. 2d 527, 2004 La. LEXIS 1683 (La., May 14, 2004)
Affirmed by Dailey v. Travis, 892 So. 2d 17, 2005 La. LEXIS 122 (La., Jan. 19, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE EIGHTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. (NUMBER 55628 "C"), PARISH OF IBERVILLE, STATE OF LOUISIANA. HONORABLE SHARAH HARRIS, JUDGE.
Dailey v. Travis, 847 So. 2d 1246, 2003 La. LEXIS 1973 (La., June 20, 2003)



DISPOSITION: WRIT DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Claiming that appellant department of corrections was negligent, appellee injured inmate sought to recover damages, including medical bills, future medical expenses, and general damages for pain and suffering. The department filed dilatory exceptions, raising the objection of prematurity. The 18th Judicial District Court, Parish of Iberville (Louisiana), denied the department's exceptions. The department appealed.


OVERVIEW: The Supreme Court of Louisiana remanded the matter to the appellate court for briefing, argument, and opinion. The department urged that the inmate failed to exhaust her administrative remedies as required by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:1172 of the Louisiana Corrections Administrative Remedy Procedure (CARP), La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:1171-1179, and La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 15:1184 and 15:1191 of the Louisiana Prison Litigation Reform Act (LPLRA), La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:1181-1191. The inmate claimed she was entitled to proceed with the trial court proceeding based on the holding of Pope v. State. The inmate initiated her request for an administrative remedy within 90 days of the alleged accident. The appellate court found that retroactive application of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:1172 was not permissible based on the facts of the instant case. The administrative regulations in place prior to the enactment of 2002 La. Acts 89 were unenforceable, because they implemented legislation that was found unconstitutional in Pope. Accordingly, the department had not sustained its burden of establishing an available administrative remedy. The trial court did not err in denying the exception.


OUTCOME: The writ was denied.

 

1405 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Pierre


No. 03-KA-1306


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


03-1306 (La.App. 5 Cir. 02/23/04); 869 So. 2d 206; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 306



February 23, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 16, 2004.
Writ denied by State v. Pierre, 2004 La. LEXIS 2747 (La., Oct. 1, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 01-5658, DIVISION "M". HONORABLE HENRY G. SULLIVAN, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was found guilty of distribution of heroin, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:966(A). The 24th Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, Division "M" (Louisiana) denied defendant's motion to exclude certain tape recorded conversations and denied his motions for new trial and post-verdict judgment of acquittal. Defendant was sentenced to life imprisonment without benefit of probation or suspension. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Inter alia, defendant argued that the evidence presented at trial was legally insufficient to support his conviction because the State failed to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that he acted with co-defendant to deliver the heroin to the informant. While defendant was not directly involved in the transaction, the evidence reflected that he facilitated the transaction and procured co-defendant to deliver the heroin. According to co-defendant, defendant described the precise location of the heroin and even described how it would be packaged. After speaking to defendant, co-defendant went to the location, picked up the heroin and delivered it to the informant in exchange for $ 350. Further, defendant was seen driving a vehicle near the building prior to and during the transaction. Although defendant contended that his co-defendant's testimony was not believable, the jury obviously found otherwise. The appellate court found that the evidence was sufficient for rational jurors, viewing the evidence in the light most favorable to the prosecution, to conclude beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant was a principal to distribution of heroin. The assignment of error was without merit.


OUTCOME: The conviction and sentence were affirmed.

 

1406 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Allen


No. 03-KA-1205


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


03-1205 (La.App. 5 Cir. 02/23/04); 868 So. 2d 877; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 326



February 23, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 16, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE FORTIETH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF ST. JOHN THE BAPTIST, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 02-194. HONORABLE MADELINE JASMINE, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to six counts of carnal knowledge of a juvenile under the age of 17, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:80. The Fortieth Judicial District Court for the Parish of St. John the Baptist, Louisiana, sentenced defendant to 10-years at hard labor on each of the six counts with each sentence to run concurrently. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The plea agreement did not contain an agreed-upon sentence, and only indicated defendant would be sentenced, with no sentencing cap, after a pre-sentence investigation report. Defendant admitted he had sexual intercourse with the 13-year-old victim on six separate occasions over a two-month period. Defendant argued that the imposed sentences were unconstitutionally excessive, and that the failure of trial counsel to file a motion to reconsider constituted ineffective assistance of counsel. Since defendant sought a review of his sentences solely for constitutional excessiveness, his trial counsel's failure to move for reconsideration was inconsequential and his ineffective assistance claim had no merit. Furthermore, there was no abuse of discretion in the sentences imposed. Defendant had a previous conviction for carnal knowledge of a juvenile, and was on probation for the same offense at the time he committed the present six offenses. Defendant, at the age of 22, had over 20 adult arrests ranging from simple robbery and simple assault to attempted armed robbery.


OUTCOME: Defendant's sentences were affirmed.

 

1407 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Boudreaux v. Braun Invs., L.L.C.


No. 03-CA-1070


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


03-1070 (La.App. 5 Cir. 02/23/04); 869 So. 2d 180; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 312



February 23, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 16, 2004.
Writ denied by Boudreaux v. Braun Invs., L.L.C., 872 So. 2d 1084, 2004 La. LEXIS 1640 (La., May 7, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-THIRD JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF ST. JAMES, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 28589, DIVISION "E". HONORABLE GUY HOLDRIDGE, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant homeowners brought a suit against appellee neighboring business and a town, claiming that the business blocked their right of way and that the correct procedures had not been followed in changing the zoning of the lot owned by the business. The 23rd Judicial District Court, Parish of St. James, Division "E" (Louisiana), prohibited the right-of-way from being blocked and dismissed the rest of the case. The landowners appealed.


OVERVIEW: The homeowners, inter alia, claimed that the trial court erred in finding that the town's zoning map and ordinance were properly enacted. They alleged that the published notices were deceptive and misleading, because the board of alderman voted immediately after the meeting to adopt the ordinance, rather than waiting three days for written comments, and because no notice of the agenda for the meeting was published. La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:4724 and the town's zoning plan required a public hearing be held prior to adoption or amendment of zoning regulations, and the meeting duly noticed. There was no requirement to hold open adoption of the amendments for three days, and the appellate court did not find that the notice so implied. There was evidence at the trial that receipt of any such comments in the three-day period could have brought the matter back before the board. There were no written comments or objections within the time frame allowed. Strict compliance with the zoning laws did not require the town to wait until the three day period had passed before adopting the ordinances. The town complied with the statutory law requiring notice and the opportunity for a public hearing.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed. The homeowners were taxed the costs of the appeal.

 

1408 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Faul


No. 2003 KA 1423


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2003 1423 (La.App. 1 Cir. 02/23/04); 873 So. 2d 690; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 342



February 23, 2004, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 17th Judicial District Court, In and for the Parish of Lafourche State of Louisiana. Trial Court No. 375851. Honorable Walter I. Lanier, III, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded guilty to sexual battery in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:43.1. The 17th Judicial District Court, in and for the Parish of Lafourche (Louisiana) sentenced defendant to five years at hard labor without the benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant claimed that his sentence was excessive. The State argued that review of defendant's assignment of error was barred by La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 881.2 A(2). The court agreed with the State that the existence of a plea agreement was set forth in the record at the time of defendant's plea. However, that plea agreement was not set forth in the record with any particularity. Without specific reference to an agreed-upon sentence in the record at the time of the plea, Art. 881.2 A(2) did not bar appellate review of the sentence imposed. After considering defendant's argument, the court affirmed. A review of the record revealed that the trial court adequately considered the criteria of La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 894.1 B(2) and did not manifestly abuse its discretion in imposing the sentence herein. The sentence imposed was not grossly disproportionate to the severity of the offense, given that defendant had sexual contact with a victim younger than 15 years of age and more than three years younger than defendant. Therefore, the sentence was not constitutionally excessive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

 

1409 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Capitol City Towing & Recovery Inc. v. State


No. 2003 CA 0647


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2003 0647 (La.App. 1 Cir. 2/23/04); 873 So. 2d 706; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 363



February 23, 2004, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Writ denied by Capitol City Towing & Recovery, Inc. v. State, 2004 La. LEXIS 1910 (La., June 4, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, In and For the Parish of East Baton Rouge, State of Louisiana. Trial Court No. 428,638. Honorable Kay Bates, Judge.
Capitol City Towing & Recovery, Inc. v. State, 842 So. 2d 321, 2003 La. LEXIS 834 (La., Mar. 21, 2003)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Nineteenth Judicial District Court, in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana, granted judgment in favor of appellee towing company owner, finding that numerous Louisiana statutes regulating the towing/storage industry, as well as regulations promulgated pursuant to those statutes, were preempted by federal law. Appellant State Police appealed.


OVERVIEW: The State argued that the rules and regulations attacked by the towing company were not preempted by 49 U.S.C.S. § 14501(c), but fell under Louisiana's safety regulatory authority and were thus saved from preemption. The appellate court found that the subject statutes and regulations found to be preempted by the trial court came within the safety exemption of § 14501(c). The ban on solicitation of towing business by tow truck operators, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 32:1714(2), was designed to protect the public from the safety hazards associated with wreck-chasing. The provision requiring that tow operators wear clothing sufficient to identify the towing company and driver was clearly related to the efficient administration of accident scenes and was designed to make the towing and removal of vehicles safer. Requiring oil-absorbent materials, such as sand or oil, to be protected from the elements, was clearly related to vehicle safety and was thus saved from preemption under the safety exemption.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded.

 

1410 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Acadia Parish Police Jury v. Town of Duson


03-944


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


03-944 (La.App. 3 Cir. 02/18/04); 874 So. 2d 178; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 251



February 18, 2004, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 19, 2004.
Writ denied by Acadia Parish Police Jury v. Town of Duson, 872 So. 2d 1083, 2004 La. LEXIS 1636 (La., May 7, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE FIFTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF ACADIA, DOCKET NO. 75,890. HONORABLE HERMAN CLAUSE, PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant police jury filed a petition in the Fifteenth Judicial District Court, Acadia Parish, Louisiana, for declaratory judgment seeking to prohibit appellee town from collecting video poker revenues generated by businesses located within the town's municipal boundaries. The trial court dismissed the police jury's petition. The police jury appealed.


OVERVIEW: The police jury had argued that the parish was entitled to the revenue derived from video poker machines located in Acadia Parish and also within the municipal limits of the town. The police jury argued that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:171 was unconstitutional because there was no rationale basis for distinguishing between municipalities located wholly within the physical boundaries of one parish and those municipalities whose boundaries encompassed more than one parish. The police jury asserted that it defeated the legislative purpose behind La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:171(B), which was to protect the integrity of the local option vote in each parish and prevent a municipality located wholly within a parish that voted to prohibit video poker from changing its eligibility to receive revenue through the annexation of portions of a parish that voted to allow video poker. The appellate court held that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:171(B) did not create any unreasonable classifications, and was a legitimate exercise of the legislature's constitutional power to except municipalities which were located in two parishes from the prohibition contained in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:171(B).


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

1411 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Duhon v. Duhon


03-898


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


03-898 (La.App. 3 Cir. 02/18/04); 867 So. 2d 830; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 254



February 18, 2004, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Duhon v. Duhon, 2004 La. App. LEXIS 743 (La.App. 3 Cir., Mar. 31, 2004)
Writ denied by Duhon v. Duhon, 2004 La. LEXIS 2061 (La., June 18, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE FIFTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF LAFAYETTE, NO. 98-1104. HONORABLE JULES D. EDWARDS, III, PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a legal malpractice case, the Fifteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Lafayette, Louisiana, denied plaintiffs', family members, motion for new trial after finding that defendants, law firm and lawyer, did not deviate from the standard of care in a meeting between the family members and defendant relatives. The family members appealed.


OVERVIEW: The family members attacked the constitutionality of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5605, arguing that its application prevented the jury from hearing the evidence that the law firm had been involved in representing the family in developing a real estate project from the beginning. The appellate court found that the members' legal malpractice case was premised on the lawyer's failure to document the tentative agreement reached at a meeting; however, this failure did not automatically require the jury to find that the lawyer had committed legal malpractice. The record in no way supported the allegation that the lawyer's failure to document the tentative agreement was a legal cause of the members' loss. One brother testified that he would not have signed the agreement that night without first checking with his wife, who was a co-owner with him in the business venture. His wife was adamant that the agreement would not be acceptable to her and her husband.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1412 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Gibson v. State


No. 03-CA-1112


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


03-1112 (La.App. 5 Cir. 02/10/04); 866 So. 2d 375; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 218



February 10, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 3, 2004.
Rehearing denied by Gibson v. State, 2004 La. App. LEXIS 575 (La.App. 5 Cir., Mar. 3, 2004)
Writ denied by Gibson v. State, 2005 La. LEXIS 1059 (La., Apr. 8, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-NINTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF ST. CHARLES, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 57,526, DIVISION "E". HONORABLE ROBERT A. CHAISSON, JUDGE PRESIDING.
Gibson v. Whitley, 1992 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 12818 (E.D. La., Aug. 17, 1992)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate filed a declaratory relief action against defendant district attorney and alleged that his arrests and convictions were void as the district attorney did not have the power to legally represent the State in the criminal matters against him. The Twenty-Ninth Judicial District Court, Parish of St. Charles, Louisiana, granted the district attorney's exceptions of no cause of action and no right of action. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate had been convicted of theft and forgery and was sentenced as a multiple offender to 32 years at hard labor. His conviction and sentence were affirmed on appeal. His application for post-conviction relief and his petition for habeas corpus were both denied. The inmate then filed this action and alleged that La. Const. art. V, § 26(B) and La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 16:1(B) were unconstitutional as they conflicted with the United States Constitution and that there was an unconstitutional delegation of power to the district attorney's office to prosecute cases on the State's behalf. The trial court granted the district attorney's exceptions of no cause of action and no right of action. The appellate court affirmed and held that there was no cause of action as the inmate's pleading presented no existing, actual and substantial dispute for which declaratory judgment would be appropriate. No resolution of a justiciable controversy could possibly be served by a declaratory judgment in the case. Further, the court held there was no right of action as there was no indication that the inmate was member of a class that had a legal interest in the subject matter of the litigation.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

1413 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Todd


KA 03-1230


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


03-1230 (La.App. 3 Cir. 02/04/04); 866 So. 2d 1040; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 152



February 4, 2004, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. Todd, 2004 La. LEXIS 2311 (La., July 2, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE THIRTY-THIRD JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF ALLEN, NO. CR2002-4819, HONORABLE JOEL GERARD DAVIS, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After being found guilty in the Thirty-Third Judicial District Court, Allen Parish (Louisiana), of distribution of a controlled dangerous substance, Schedule II, cocaine, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967(A)(1), defendant's motion for a new trial was denied. Defendant was sentenced to 25 years at hard labor. Defendant's motion to reconsider his sentence was denied. Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that: (1) the evidence was insufficient to support the verdict; and (2) his sentence was constitutionally excessive. Defendant could not complain of errors after the verdict unless he objected to the errors at the time of the ruling. A review of the trial transcript revealed that defendant did not object to the admission of the drugs or the video tapes showing the drug transaction. Thus, the instant court could not address the issue of whether the trial court improperly admitted into evidence the drugs, the video tapes of the drug transaction showing defendant exchanging two rocks of crack cocaine for $ 40, and the confidential informant's testimony. The evidence was sufficient to support the conviction. On the issue of excessiveness of the sentence, it was not whether another sentence would have been more appropriate, but whether the trial court abused its discretion. La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967(B)(1) provided for a term of imprisonment of not less than two years nor more than 30 years. Defendant failed to establish that the trial court abused its considerable discretion when it sentenced him to 25 years at hard labor.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence were affirmed.

 

1414 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Christiana v. Southern Baptist Hosp.


No. 2003-C-1880


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2003-1880 (La.App. 4 Cir. 02/04/04); 867 So. 2d 809; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 291



February 4, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 1, 2004.



DISPOSITION: WRIT GRANTED, JUDGMENT OF DISTRICT COURT VACATED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee couple asserted causes of action in strict liability as well as negligence and sought a judgment that the Blood Shield Statutes were not applicable to the couple's strict liability claims against appellant hospital for the distribution of alleged contaminated blood products received by the wife in 1984. The Judicial District Court (Louisiana) rendered a judgment granting their motion for partial summary judgment. The hospital appealed.


OVERVIEW: The parties agreed that the law in effect in 1984 when the blood transfusion took place was the law that governed the case. While there was no dispute that the hospital was a distributor of blood, the parties disagreed on whether the strict liability prohibition contained in the Blood Shield Statutes, former La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2797 and former La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 2322.1, in effect in 1984 applied to distributors of blood. The appellate court held that the 1982 statute did not expressly make a distinction between hospitals that actually provided blood from their own blood banks and hospitals that obtained blood from other hospital blood banks. Therefore, the district court erred in concluding that, as of 1984, when the wife's transfusion was received, strict liability applied. The language of the 1982 statute clearly showed the legislature's intention to shield, inter alia, hospitals and hospital blood banks from claims of strict liability or liability of any kind without negligence in the screening, processing, transfusion, or medical use of human blood and blood components resulting in transmission of viral disease undetectable by medical and scientific laboratory tests.


OUTCOME: The writ was granted, and the judgment of the trial court granting the motion for partial summary judgment in favor of the couple was vacated.

 

1415 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Byrnside Drilling Co. v. Armour


No. 38,073-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


38,073-CA (La.App. 2 Cir. 01/30/04); 865 So. 2d 310; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 108



January 30, 2004, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected February 3, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Webster, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 50,971. Honorable Dewey E. Burchett, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant drilling company "stacked" a drilling rig on property it believed belonged to a client, leaving it there for a year. The property actually belonged to appellee property owner, who after unsuccessful attempts to serve the drilling company, had the rig seized and sold at a sheriff's sale. In a declaratory action, the Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Webster, Louisiana, upheld the sale. The drilling company appealed.


OVERVIEW: A bank intervened as the holder of a chattel mortgage, asserting that its chattel mortgage was secured by the same drilling rig, and that the chattel mortgage was properly filed. The bank subsequently assigned its security interest to substituted intervenor petroleum company. The sole issue on appeal was the validity of the sheriff's sale. The trial court had held that the bank, knowing the mobile nature of the portable drilling rig, had a duty to take steps to have the mortgage filed in the parishes in which it was located in order to put third parties on notice. Since the bank did not take steps to record its mortgage in the parishes in which the rig was located, the trial court held that, as a mortgagee, the bank was not reasonably identifiable to third parties in other parishes, such as the property owner. The appellate court found that the equipment seized and sold at the sheriff's sale was substantially different from that listed in the chattel mortgage. Further, the location of the chattel as specified in the chattel mortgage was incorrect, precluding notice to third parties. Therefore the chattel mortgage could not be enforced against the property sold.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed. Costs were assessed to the drilling company and the petroleum company.

 

1416 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Clark v. State


No. 2002 CW 1936 R


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2002 1936 (La.App. 1 Cir. 01/28/04); 873 So. 2d 32; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 74



January 28, 2004, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 10, 2004.
Writ denied by Clark v. State, 870 So. 2d 300, 2004 La. LEXIS 1407 (La., Apr. 23, 2004)
Appeal after remand at Clark v. State, 2009 La. App. LEXIS 2188 (La.App. 1 Cir., Dec. 23, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the 19th Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 483,150. The Honorable Kay Bates, Judge Presiding.
Clark v. State, 842 So. 2d 388, 2003 La. LEXIS 1251 (La., Apr. 25, 2003)



DISPOSITION: WRIT GRANTED, JUDGMENT AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART, AND VACATED IN PART, AND CASE REMANDED AND STAYED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff electric cooperative customers filed a petition for refund of state sales taxes with the board of tax appeals against defendant department of revenue; the customers also filed a class action suit seeking virtually the same relief. The 19th Judicial District Court of East Baton Rouge Parish, Louisiana, denied the department's exceptions. On review, the department was granted writs, and the case was remanded to the trial court.


OVERVIEW: In its exceptions, the department characterized the customers' claims as being brought pursuant to the Louisiana Overpayment Refund procedure, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:1621 et seq. The customers' opposed the declinatory exception on the grounds that the trial court had original jurisdiction of all civil matters under La. Const. art. V, § 16(A). The instant court found that the law did not afford the customers a remedy under civil code theories of recovery; thus, the board's jurisdiction was not circumscribed by § 16(A) and the trial court's jurisdiction vis-a-vis the board was properly governed by La. Const. art. V, § 16(B). As such, the instant court held that the trial court lacked original jurisdiction to consider the merits of the customers' claims. The instant court could not properly consider the customers' constitutional issues until the trial court had definitively ruled on them, as the validity of the claim procedure and the merits of the department's prescription defense were intertwined with the issue of the constitutionality of the challenged statutes.


OUTCOME: That portion of the judgment denying the objection of lack of subject matter jurisdiction was reversed. That portion of the judgment denying the peremptory exception of prescription was vacated. The customers' cause of action for judicial review of their causes of action and claims for refund of the sales tax overpayments was remanded, but stayed pending the conclusion of the administrative proceeding before the department and the board.

In re Trahan


No. 03-CA-1002


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


03-1002 (La.App. 5 Cir. 01/27/04); 866 So. 2d 907; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 87



January 27, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 16, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 583-786, DIVISION "E". HONORABLE GREG G. GUIDRY, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT SET ASIDE; REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient appealed a judgment of the 24th Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, Louisiana, Division E, maintaining an exception of prescription in favor of defendant doctor.


OVERVIEW: The patient sued the doctor for misdiagnosing a mole as not being skin cancer. The doctor filed an exception of prescription, in which he alleged that the complaint was filed beyond the three year prescriptive period designated in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5628. The patient averred that the condition from which she suffered had a latency period of more than three years, and urged that the Louisiana Supreme Court noted in dicta that in such cases, the prescriptive period may be unconstitutional. As the instant court read the record, it was apparent that the trial court determined the constitutional issue presented by the patient at the trial on the exception of prescription, and, as it granted the exception, it effectively denied the request for declaratory judgment. While the patient did raise the issue in a motion, it was tried as an opposition, the attorney general was not notified as required by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:4448, and no hearing was had on the motion itself. The trial court thus erred in considering the claim of unconstitutionality, and to the extent that it determined the constitutional claim, its ruling, on that issue alone, was vacated.


OUTCOME: The judgment granting the doctor's exception of prescription was set aside. The matter was remanded to allow the patient an opportunity to properly litigate her constitutional challenge.

State v. Williams


No. 2003-KA-0091


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2003-0091 (La.App. 4 Cir. 01/14/04); 866 So. 2d 296; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 19



January 14, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 10, 2004.
Writ denied by State v. Williams, 876 So. 2d 831, 2004 La. LEXIS 2214 (La., June 25, 2004)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Williams v. Louisiana, 543 U.S. 1062, 125 S. Ct. 880, 160 L. Ed. 2d 790, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 16 (Jan. 10, 2005)
Post-conviction relief denied at State v. Williams, 2014 La. App. LEXIS 3220 (La.App. 4 Cir., July 28, 2014)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Williams v. Cain, 2017 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 129754 (E.D. La., May 12, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: COURT OF APPEAL FOURTH CIRCUIT STATE OF LOUISIANA APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH NO. 378-491, SECTION "B". Hon. Robert J. Burns, Judge Pro Tempore.
State v. Williams, 855 So. 2d 443, 2003 La. App. LEXIS 2900 (La.App. 4 Cir., Oct. 1, 2003)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was granted a rehearing to consider his appeal from the judgment of the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish, Section B, Louisiana, denying his second motion to quash the indictment, which challenged the constitutionality of the grand jury selection in Orleans Parish at the time of his indictment.


OVERVIEW: The Louisiana Supreme Court struck down as unconstitutional La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 412, 413(C) and 414(C), La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:114, and the introductory phrases of La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 413(B) and 414(B). The statute and codal provisions pertinent to the instant case were declared unconstitutional in the Louisiana Supreme Court decision solely because they were local laws in violation of La. Const. art. III, § 12(A). In the Orleans Parish, prior to the Louisiana Supreme Court decision, pursuant to former La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 413(C), the trial court selected the grand jury in the Orleans Parish, and the grand jury foreperson was selected from among members of that grand jury. The appellate court ruled that, although the trial court erred in denying defendant's motion to quash his grand jury indictment based on the unconstitutionality of the local laws at issue, there was no showing that the error affected his substantial rights, La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 921. The substantial rights of defendant were not affected per se solely because he was indicted by a grand jury selected pursuant to local laws passed by the Louisiana State Legislature.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence were affirmed.

 

1419 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Diefenthal v. Longue Vue Found.


No. 2002-CA-1470


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2002-1470 (La.App. 4 Cir. 01/7/04); 865 So. 2d 863; 2004 La. App. LEXIS 23



January 7, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 4, 2004.
Writ denied by Diefenthal v. Longue Vue Found., 869 So. 2d 883, 2004 La. LEXIS 1086 (La., Apr. 2, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 2000-6189, DIVISION "F". Honorable Yada Magee, Judge.
Diefenthal v. Longue Vue Management Corp., 561 So. 2d 44, 1990 La. LEXIS 1036 (La., 1990)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED IN PART; AFFIRMED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, foundation and corporation, sought review of the decision of the Civil District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), which granted summary judgment in favor of plaintiffs, residents, in an action seeking to enforce restrictive covenants prohibiting commercial use of properties. The district court also granted appellees, intervenors', motion to intervene.


OVERVIEW: The case involved an action for declaratory and injunctive relief seeking to enforce restrictive covenants prohibiting commercial use of the properties fronting one of the premiere residential neighborhoods in New Orleans. The residents fronting the area in question filed an action against the corporation, and the trial court granted summary judgment in favor of the residents. The trial court affirmed, stating that, based on the analysis of the three pertinent documents, the two contractual agreements, the 1931 Act and the 1977 Agreement, and the 1990 decision interpreting those agreements, the parties intended to create building restrictions, La. Civ. Code Ann. arts. 781 and 782. The court thus classified the restrictions as building restrictions. Because building restrictions constituted real property rights on property, the only way in which the restrictions could have been amended before the expiration of the fixed term of April 18, 2027, was with the consent of all of the landowners. The court reversed the granting of the intervention, because the restrictions were at the heart of the action and the intervenors were strangers to those restrictions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment granting the residents' motion for summary judgment and their request for injunctive relief. The court reversed the ruling granting the intervenor's intervention.

Messina v. St. Charles Parish Council


No. 03-CA-644


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


03-644 (La.App. 5 Cir. 12/30/03); 865 So. 2d 158; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 3655



December 30, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by Messina v. St. Charles Parish Council, 871 So. 2d 354, 2004 La. LEXIS 1042 (La., Mar. 26, 2004)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Messina v. Parish of St. Charles, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 4365 (U.S., May 31, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM THE 29TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF ST. CHARLES, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 50,029, DIVISION "D". HONORABLE KIRK R. GRANIER, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff reception hall and restaurant owner appealed from a summary judgment granted by the 29th Judicial District Court, Parish of St. Charles, Division "D" (Louisiana) to appellee parish in the restaurant owner's suit against the parish for denying the restaurant an outdoor liquor permit after he had already been in business for sometime.


OVERVIEW: The restaurant owner contended, inter alia, that he was denied his constitutional rights of due process of law and equal protection and was deprived of property without just compensation because the ordinance was amended without notice to him. Although the denial of the permit affected the scope of his business, the ordinance did not affect his right to conduct either a restaurant business or a reception business. His right to provide alcoholic beverages inside was not revoked by the ordinance. The ordinance was merely economic or social regulation, thus there needed only to have been a rational relationship to a legitimate governmental interest. The restriction on alcohol outdoors had a rational relationship to a legitimate governmental interest, which was to regulate noise nuisance. The council concluded that removing the exemption for restaurants was the best way to regulate the noise caused by loud music at outside parties. Since the ordinance did not: (1) affect a fundamental right; (2) constitute arbitrary and unreasonable action; and (3) was rationally related to a legitimate government interest, it did not violate the federal or the state's due process protections.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed. Costs of the appeal were to be paid by the restaurant owner.

State v. Triche


No. 03-KA-910


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


03-910 (La.App. 5 Cir. 12/30/03); 864 So. 2d 832; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 3684



December 30, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 01-2421, DIVISION "G". HONORABLE ROBERT A. PITRE, JR., JUDGE PRESIDING.
State v. Triche, 848 So. 2d 80, 2003 La. App. LEXIS 1613 (La.App. 5 Cir., May 28, 2003)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a second appeal following his conviction on a charge of possession with intent to distribute marijuana, defendant sought review of the habitual offender sentence imposed upon him by the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, Louisiana.


OVERVIEW: Defendant received an enhanced sentence after the trial court found that he had committed a prior felony. In reviewing the record in the first appeal, the court had recognized that an illegal sentence had been imposed. The sentence was vacated and the case was remanded. The trial court reduced the original enhanced sentence by five years and defendant again appealed. In the second appeal he asserted that the trial court erred in finding him to be a second-felony offender and that his new sentence was excessive. The sentence imposed was the mandatory minimum sentence for defendant's offense at the time it was committed. It was presumed to be constitutional. Defendant failed to present any evidence that the sentence was unconstitutional. The sentence was mandatory and defendant failed to show that it was grossly out of proportion to the severity of his crime.


OUTCOME: Defendant's habitual offender sentence was affirmed.

La. Pub. Facilities Auth. v. All Taxpayers


NUMBER 2003 CA 2738 Consolidated with NUMBER 2003 CA 2739

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, student and others (student) sought review of the decision of the Nineteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which found in favor of appellees, Board of Supervisors (board) of Louisiana State University Agricultural and Mechanical College (university) and the Louisiana Public Facilities Authority in an action involving the increase in the price of football tickets.

Accordingly, the price charged for admission to football games in the stadium did not constitute a "fee" for purposes of La. Const. art. VII, § 2.1.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1425 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Ross


03-0564


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


03-0564 (La.App. 3 Cir. 12/17/03); 861 So. 2d 888; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 3512



December 17, 2003, Opinions Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. Ross, 2004 La. LEXIS 2209 (La., June 25, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE NINTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF RAPIDES, NO. 260,431. HONORABLE HARRY F. RANDOW, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from decisions of the Ninth Judicial District Court, Parish of Rapides (Louisiana), which convicted defendant on a charge of aggravated rape and sentenced him to life imprisonment without the benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was accused of raping a seven-year old child. On appeal, his main contentions were that there was insufficient evidence of penile penetration and that his sentence was excessive. Defendant was 16 years old at the time of the rape. The court affirmed. While there were some conflicts in the evidence, it was sufficient to support defendant's conviction. The victim, testifying in terms she used to describe genitals and other body areas, testified that defendant attempted to stick his penis inside her. The victim made similar statements to doctors and a child advocate. Physical examinations by the doctors indicated penetration. And the victim testified that defendant was the only one who had touched her in an inappropriate manner. The life sentence was mandatory under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:42. Departure from the minimum sentence was available only in rare circumstances where a trial court felt the sentence would violate La. Const. art. I, § 20. Defendant failed to prove by clear and convincing evidence that circumstances existed that warranted a departure from the minimum sentence. Thus, the sentence was not constitutionally excessive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed both defendant's conviction and his sentence.

 

1426 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Fielding


No. 37,943-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


37,943 (La.App. 2 Cir. 12/10/03); 862 So. 2d 420; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 3353



December 10, 2003, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State ex rel. Fielding v. State, 889 So. 2d 256, 2005 La. LEXIS 195 (La., Jan. 14, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Appealed from the Second Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bienville, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 34-050. Honorable Jenifer Ward Clason, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After denying defendant's motion to suppress evidence, the Second Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bienville, Louisiana, convicted him of second-degree murder and sentenced him to the mandatory term of life imprisonment. Defendant's motion for mistrial based on the prosecutor's comments was denied. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended, inter alia, that the trial court erred in denying his motions to suppress and for mistrial. The appellate court found that the testimony and physical evidence were sufficient for a rational jury to find that defendant had the specific intent to kill or inflict great bodily harm when he fired his weapon at the victim's head. Although defendant's self-serving statement was that he shot the victim in self-defense, the jury chose to reject this version of the shooting, which it was entitled to do. As defendant had no right to an expectation of privacy in the abandoned house, and, as probable cause for the search existed, the search was not unlawful, and defendant's statement was not subject to suppression. While questions the prosecutor asked an expert regarding the gunshot wounds were improper, denial of defendant's motion to mistrial was proper, considering the trial court's strong admonition to disregard. Defendant's sentence was not unconstitutionally excessive, as it was statutorily required; defendant failed to articulate why his circumstances justified an exception to the imposition of the mandatory life sentence.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Cazes v. Pertuit


No. 03-CA-842


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


03-842 (La.App. 5 Cir. 12/09/03); 864 So. 2d 705; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 3364



December 9, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-THIRD JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF ST. JAMES, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 27886. HONORABLE RALPH TUREAU, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A restraining order required plaintiff individual's wife to leave the home. Defendants, two city police officers, escorted the wife to the home to retrieve personal items. The individual sued the officers, alleging they deprived him of his constitutional right to be free of unreasonable search and seizure. The Twenty-Third Judicial District Court, Parish of St. James, Louisiana, granted summary judgment for the officers. The individual appealed.


OVERVIEW: The individual and his wife were going through a divorce. La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 46:2135(C) provided that during the existence of a temporary restraining order, a party had the right to return to the family residence once, to recover his or her personal necessities, provided that the party was accompanied by a law enforcement officer. However, the individual asserted that under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, the alleged violation of his Fourth Amendment rights took place with the entry of one officer into his home without a warrant, and that there was a "seizure" of his person when the officer instructed him to sit on the sofa while his wife gathered her belongings. The appellate court agreed with the trial court's findings that nothing in the record indicated the officers threatened or touched the individual or removed anything from his house. The officers were on the premises for approximately 10 minutes, and were authorized by their department to provide the assistance rendered for defendant's wife for the limited purpose of obtaining her clothing and personal items. Thus, there was not an unconstitutional seizure on the individual.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Writ denied by State v. Pearson, 876 So. 2d 73, 2004 La. LEXIS 1896 (La., June 4, 2004)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Pearson v. La., 543 U.S. 1007, 125 S. Ct. 626, 160 L. Ed. 2d 471, 2004 U.S. LEXIS 7803 (U.S., Nov. 29, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 00-5403, DIVISION "F". HONORABLE PATRICK J. McCABE, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED ; MOTION TO WITHDRAW GRANTED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), which convicted him of possession of cocaine in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967(C) pursuant to a plea agreement. He was resentenced as a multiple offender to seven years at hard labor. Further, his counsel filed a motion to withdraw.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with possession of cocaine and he later pled guilty in connection with a plea agreement. His original sentence of five years at hard labor was vacated because he failed to appear and he was resentenced as a multiple offender to seven years at hard labor. He appeal, but the court affirmed, stating that defendant was sufficiently advised of his rights and made a knowing and intelligent waiver of those rights. Throughout the colloquy, the trial court asked defendant if he understood his rights and the fact that he was giving them up by pleading guilty to which defendant consistently responded, "Yes, sir." The trial court also specifically inquired into the waiver of rights form. Defendant acknowledged that he had read and signed the form, which specifically advised defendant of his three Boykin rights. The court further granted his counsel's motion to withdraw, holding that there were no errors or issues, which if raised, would have arguable supported an appeal. The court concluded that the record showed that the trial court fully complied with La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1(D)(1)(a) prior to accepting defendant's stipulation or plea to the multiple bill.


OUTCOME: The court granted counsel's motion to withdraw and affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

State v. Wallace


No. 2003-KA-0193


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2003-0193 (La.App. 4 Cir. 11/26/03); 862 So. 2d 286; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 3299



November 26, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 22, 2004.
Writ denied by State v. Wallace, 870 So. 2d 269, 2004 La. LEXIS 1293 (La., Apr. 8, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 356-168, SECTION "I". Honorable Raymond C. Bigelow, Judge.
State ex rel. Wallace v. State, 726 So. 2d 4, 1998 La. LEXIS 2831 (La., Sept. 25, 1998)



DISPOSITION: Conviction and sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), which convicted him of armed robbery, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:64. The Louisiana Supreme Court had granted defendant's writ application in part, remanding it to the trial court with an order to grant defendant an out-of-time appeal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of armed robbery in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:64 and he appealed both his conviction and sentence. The court affirmed however, stating that the evidence was not insufficient to convict him, because the convictions essentially rested on his identification by the victims in each case. In a case where there was no physical evidence to link a defendant to the crime charged, the testimony of one witness, if believed by the trier of fact, was sufficient support for a factual conclusion required for a verdict of guilty. Further, defendant was not prejudiced by the State's comments in its opening statement, because defendant did not allege or prove bad faith on the part of the prosecution, and the court found that there was no clear or substantial prejudice to him. There was sufficient evidence to connect defendant with the crime independent of any inference in the opening statement. Defendant had no constitutionally guaranteed right to the assistance of counsel at the physical lineup, because it was held prior to his indictment. Defendant was precluded from raising an appeal with regard to a juror, because he did not object prior.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1430 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Terrell


No. 37,762-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


37,762 (La.App. 2 Cir. 11/18/03); 858 So. 2d 1282; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 3158



November 18, 2003, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reversed by State v. Terrell, 2004 La. LEXIS 1862 (La., June 4, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 205,548. Honorable Charles R. Scott, Judge.



DISPOSITION: SENTENCE VACATED; REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury found defendant guilty as charged of one count of possession of cocaine, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967C. Defendant was adjudicated a fourth felony offender and given the mandatory sentence of life imprisonment at hard labor without benefits. After the First Judicial District Court, Parish of Caddo (Louisiana), denied defendant's motion to reconsider the sentence, defendant appealed his sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the term was disproportionate to the severity of the offense and excessive due to his disabilities and the non-violent nature of his prior offenses. The appellate court found that the trial court could have considered the legislative change in policy brought about by the 2001 amendment to the Habitual Offender Law, but rejected defendant's argument regarding the direct application of the new law to his sentencing. As defendant had only one 10-year drug offense, which was his oldest and not his latest offense, the leniency of the new law indicated that such an offender, after June 15, 2001, should have been sentenced under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1(A)(1)(c)(i) to a term ranging from 20 years at hard labor to life imprisonment. A trial court could take into consideration such leniency, as reflected in the legislature's new policy, and had the duty to reduce a sentence to one that would not have been excessive in view of the specific facts regarding the prior offenses and the fact that the legislature amended the Habitual Offender Law to provide more lenient punishment for drug offenders such as defendant who committed crimes after June 15, 2001.


OUTCOME: The sentence was vacated, and the case was remanded for resentencing.

 

1431 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


St. Romain v. State


2003 CA 0291


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2003 0291 (La.App. 1 Cir. 11/12/03); 863 So. 2d 577; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 3128



November 12, 2003, Date of Judgment


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 11, 2003.
Later proceeding at St. Romain v. State, 2003 La. App. LEXIS 3804 (La.App. 1 Cir., Dec. 11, 2003)
Writ of certiorari denied St. Romain v. State, 2004 La. LEXIS 1023 (La., Mar. 26, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. (NUMBER 477,803 "I-24"), PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE, STATE OF LOUISIANA. HONORABLE R. MICHAEL CALDWELL, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Nineteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), dismissed plaintiff probationary employee's state law claims for sexual discrimination as well as her sexual harassment claims against defendants, the Louisiana Department of Wildlife and Fisheries (DWF) and her immediate supervisor. The employee appealed.


OVERVIEW: The employee was hired by the DWF as a wildlife educator supervisor. She served as a wildlife educator supervisor under a probationary appointment. She was separated from employment when she failed to obtain permanent status after a 12-month probationary period. Subsequently, she filed claims of sexual discrimination and/or sexual harassment. The appellate court found that the alleged sexual discrimination and harassment claims alleged in the employee's petition were not included in the parameters of the jurisdiction afforded to the Louisiana Civil Service Commission. Thus, she properly filed her suit in district court. Additionally, the trial court improperly granted the DWF and the supervisor's motion for summary judgment because there was evidence that the supervisor engaged in sexual harassment because (1) the supervisor's rude behavior was directed much less frequently toward the men than toward the women at the DWF; (2) in a training session on handguns, all the females were singled out and excluded while the men were permitted to attend and participate; and (3) and the supervisor had a propensity to remark about the size and appearance of female employees.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

State v. Brown


No. 03-KA-581


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


03-581 (La.App. 5 Cir. 11/12/03); 861 So. 2d 644; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 3143



November 12, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 16, 2004.
Writ of certiorari denied State v. Brown, 2004 La. LEXIS 1158 (La., Apr. 2, 2004)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Brown v. State, 2004 La. LEXIS 1065 (La., Apr. 2, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 00-6036, DIVISION "K". HONORABLE MARTHA E. SASSONE, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), of possession of cocaine in excess of 400 grams and possession with intent to distribute marijuana. Defendant challenged his cocaine possession conviction and his marijuana distribution sentence.


OVERVIEW: Police officers learned that a package containing a controlled substance was being shipped to defendant's address. Defendant claimed that the package was shipped to his house for a friend and defendant did not know anything about the cocaine found inside the package. A search warrant was executed and drugs were found in defendant's house. Defendant was subsequently charged and convicted of drug offenses. The court affirmed on appeal. The evidence was sufficient to support defendant's possession of cocaine conviction in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967(F). The kilogram of cocaine was found inside a videocassette recorder in defendant's bathroom closet. The police also seized 29 bags of crack cocaine, a digital scale, and other drug-related items. The State established that the cocaine was subject to defendant's dominion and control. Defendant's guilt could have been inferred from the circumstances. Defendant's two 30-year concurrent sentences were not constitutionally excessive in violation of La. Const. art. I, § 20. The trial court properly considered the presentence investigation report and the facts. Defendant failed to show that he was entitled to a downward departure.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

1433 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Bridges v. X Communs., Inc.


No. 03-CA-441


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


03-441 (La.App. 5 Cir. 11/12/03); 861 So. 2d 592; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 3145



November 12, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 16, 2004.
Writ denied by Bridges v. X Communs., Inc., 866 So. 2d 830, 2004 La. LEXIS 715 (La., Feb. 20, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA, NO. 561-366, DIVISION "I," HONORABLE JO ELLEN GRANT, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; decision of Board of Tax Appeals reinstated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Louisiana Board of Tax Appeals vacated a portion of the additional sales tax assessment by defendant, the Louisiana Department of Revenue, set aside the penalty imposed, and ordered a refund of the payment made on that portion of the assessment. The Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, Division "I" (Louisiana), reversed the part of the Board's ruling that was in favor of plaintiff taxpayer. The taxpayer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The Department began a sales tax audit of the taxpayer. The controller of the taxpayer signed a Department-supplied form that waived prescription for the tax period January 1, 1993 through December 31, 1993. Subsequently, the chief executive officer (CEO) signed a waiver of prescription for 1994. The taxpayer filed a petition with the Board asserting that the waivers of prescription signed by the controller and the CEO were invalid because they were made without authorization by the board of directors. Although most of the facts were stipulated, there was no stipulation of fact as to the issues of the apparent authority of the controller and the CEO and the alleged ratification by the CEO of the controller's waiver. Because the controller was only an employee of the taxpayer and had no apparent authority to act for the taxpayer, the 1993 prescription waiver was not valid and the additional sales tax assessment for 1993 was improper. However, the CEO had apparent authority to act for the taxpayer; thus, the waiver of prescription of the 1994 taxes was effective. Finally, the Board did not exceed its authority in ordering a refund of the overpayment.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the district court's judgment and reinstated the Board's decision.

 

1434 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Plaisance v. Davis


2003 CA 0767


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2003 0767 (La.App. 1 Cir. 11/7/03); 868 So. 2d 711; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 3792



November 7, 2003, Date of Judgment


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by Plaisance v. Davis, 867 So. 2d 699, 2004 La. LEXIS 602 (La., Feb. 13, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. (NUMBER 503,890 "F" (22)), PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE. STATE OF LOUISIANA. HONORABLE TIMOTHY E. KELLEY, JUDGE.
Plaisance v. Davis, 857 So. 2d 38, 2003 La. App. LEXIS 3234 (La.App. 1 Cir., Nov. 7, 2003)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED; ANSWER TO APPEAL DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mayor and city failed to issue a paycheck to appellee newly-elected city court judge. The judge filed suit seeking an alternative writ of mandamus directing the mayor to issue the judge's paycheck. The 19th Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), ordered that the writ of mandamus be made peremptory and ordered that the mayor pay attorney fees. The mayor and city appealed.


OVERVIEW: The judge argued that his failure to sign the personnel action form would only have served as acquiescence to an incorrect salary. The appellate court held that the judge's cause of action arose when his first paycheck was withheld. The trial court properly overruled the exception raising the objection of prematurity. The primary issue was whether or not the trial court properly granted the extraordinary remedy of mandamus. As the chief executive officer of the city, the mayor had to execute the ordinances as passed by the city council. The appellate court concluded that the mayor was obligated to compensate the judge in accordance with the city ordinance. Because the mayor failed to comply with the terms of the city charter and with the mandate of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:2488.27 that the judge's salary was to be fixed by the council, the judge's only available avenue of relief in the case at bar was by mandamus proceeding. Thus, the appellate court found no error in the trial court's judgment ordering that the writ of mandamus be made peremptory. It necessarily followed that the mayor's dilatory exception to the unauthorized use of summary proceedings was without merit.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed. Appeal costs in the amount of $ 1,724 were assessed against the mayor.

State v. Wilturner


03-0719


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


03-0719 (La.App. 3 Cir. 11/05/03); 858 So. 2d 743; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 3007



November 5, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 1, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE SIXTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF IBERIA, NO. 98-1798. HONORABLE WILLIAM D. HUNTER, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with three counts of sexual battery and three counts of molestation of a juvenile and ultimately entered a guilty plea to one count of sexual battery. The Sixteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Iberia, Louisiana, sentenced him to serve five years at hard labor. Defendant appealed his sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was employed at a group home; the victim was a 12 year old resident of the home. Defendant performed oral sex on the child and attempted to sodomize him. At the sentencing hearing, defendant produced numerous letters from various persons in the community that attested to his good character and three members of the community testified on his behalf. Defendant argued that the trial court failed to adequately consider the mitigating circumstances listed in La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 894.1, which resulted the court's failure to sufficiently particularize the sentence. The appellate court affirmed the sentence and noted that aggravating factors relevant to the case included art. 894.1(B)(2), (B)(9), and (B)(13) in that the victim was particularly vulnerable or incapable of resistance due to his mental retardation, the offense resulted in a civil suit against defendant for damages which could not be recovered in a criminal matter, and defendant occupied a supervisory position to the victim. While defendant had no prior record, and the trial judge was impressed by defendant's witnesses, the five year sentence for the heinous acts was not excessive.


OUTCOME: The sentence imposed was affirmed.

 

1437 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Yen v. Avoyelles Parish Police Jury


03-603


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


03 603 (La.App. 3 Cir. 11/05/03);  858 So. 2d 786; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 3015



November 5, 2003, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 1, 2003.
Related proceeding at Yen v. Avoyelles Parish Police Jury, 2007 La. App. LEXIS 2203 (La.App. 3 Cir., Dec. 5, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE TWELFTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF AVOYELLES, NO. 2002-4312-A. HONORABLE MARK A. JEANSONNE, DISTRICT COURT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a medical malpractice claim filed by appellee heirs of a state prisoner after the prisoner died while incarcerated, the Twelfth Judicial District Court, Parish of Avoyelles (Louisiana), found that the heirs were not required to go through a medical review panel before filing their suit. The trial court then dismissed appellant State's exceptions of lack of subject matter jurisdiction and prematurity. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner died in state custody due to illness caused by sickle cell anemia. After his death, the heirs filed a wrongful death and survival action. The suit alleged that the State committed medical malpractice and, thus, caused the prisoner's death. The heirs did not go through a medical review panel before bringing their malpractice claim. The appellate court found that the wording of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.39.1(A)(1) of the Medical Liability for State Services Act was clear and unambiguous. The appellate court found that the statute excluded claims where the patient was a prisoner and claims by persons other than the prisoner himself. Specifically, the appellate court found that the phrase "other than claims wherein patients are prisoners" would exclude from the medical review panel process claims by patients who were prisoners and claims of a person that arose from the claim of the prison patient. Thus, the heirs were not required to go through a medical review panel because the specific wording of the statute excluded them from that process. Therefore, the trial court properly dismissed the State's exceptions of lack of subject matter jurisdiction and prematurity.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Related proceeding at Johnson v. Stalder, 2007 La. App. Unpub. LEXIS 24 (La.App. 1 Cir., Sept. 19, 2007)
Transferred by State ex rel. Johnson v. State, 993 So. 2d 1233, 2008 La. LEXIS 2308 (La., 2008)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Johnson v. State, 84 So. 3d 570, 2012 La. LEXIS 752 (La., 2012)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Johnson v. State, 90 So. 3d 455, 2012 La. LEXIS 1847 (La., 2012)

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 02-3243, DIVISION "L". HONORABLE CHARLES V. CUSIMANO, III, JUDGE PRESIDING.
State ex rel. Johnson v. State, 855 So. 2d 342, 2003 La. LEXIS 2988 (La., Oct. 10, 2003)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Twenty-fourth Judicial District Court, Jefferson Parish (Louisiana), which convicted him of armed robbery and sentenced him to 66 years at hard labor.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of armed robbery. As a third felony offender, he was sentenced to 66 years at hard labor. On appeal, the court found that the trial court did not improperly deny defendant's motion for a mistrial based on the absence of two police officers who were subpoenaed but failed to appear for trial. The mistrial statute, La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 775, did not apply to a missing witness under the particular facts of the case. The court further found that, based on the jurisprudence holding that double jeopardy protections did not apply to habitual offender proceedings, defendant's counsel was not ineffective for failing to file a motion to quash the bill of information on the basis of double jeopardy. Finally, the court found that defendant's 66-year enhanced sentence as a third felony offender was not constitutionally excessive. Defendant faced a sentencing range between 66 and 198 years of imprisonment at hard labor. The record revealed no patent errors in the case.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

State v. Lebreton

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by the court in the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), of three counts of aggravated kidnapping, three counts of aggravated rape, and two counts of aggravated crime against nature. Defendant was sentenced to concurrent life sentences on the kidnapping and rape counts and concurrent 15-year sentences on the crime against nature counts. CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Fourteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Calcasieu (Louisiana), which convicted him of the molestation of a juvenile in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:81.2 and sentenced him to eight years at hard labor with four years suspended.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of the molestation of a juvenile pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:81.2 and was sentenced to eight years at hard labor with four years suspended.
