State v. Berniard


No. 03-KA-484


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


03-484 (La.App. 5 Cir. 10/15/03); 860 So. 2d 66; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 2839



October 15, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 18, 2003.
Writ of certiorari denied State v. Berniard, 2004 La. LEXIS 1012 (La., Mar. 26, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 01-4929, DIVISION "P". HONORABLE MELVIN C. ZENO, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED; REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury for the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, State of Louisiana, Division "P," found defendant guilty of aggravated rape. Defendant was sentence of life imprisonment at hard labor, without the benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence, with credit for time served. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of raping his estranged wife. The wife's testimony that she fought unsuccessfully to repel defendant was supported by the other evidence. Defendant's torso was scratched in many places, the wife had marks and an abrasion on her face, and a spot of blood was on her shirt. Also, the wife was visibly upset when she described the events to the police and the doctor and her trial testimony was consistent with her interviews. Additionally, the law did not require that defendant, but only that such force was used that the victim could not dislodge defendant. The jury heard the testimony of the wife, the witnesses, defendant, and apparently believed the wife that the degree of force used by defendant to subdue her was such that a verdict of aggravated rape was warranted. Thus, the evidence was sufficient for a rational trier of fact to find defendant guilty of aggravated rape beyond a reasonable doubt. Also, the trial court did not err in rejecting defendant's request for a downward deviation of the mandatory sentence. Finally, defendant was not deprived of a fair trial by ineffective assistance of counsel.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence, but remanded the case to the trial judge so that the judge could inform defendant of the sex offender registration requirements.

Dan Rhodes Enters. v. City of Lake Charles


03-195


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


03-195 (La.App. 3 Cir. 10/08/03); 857 So. 2d 1256; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 2804



October 8, 2003, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] The Date of this Case was Corrected October 20, 2003.
Writ denied by Dan Rhodes Enters. v. City of Lake Charles, 2004 La. LEXIS 823 (La., Mar. 12, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Fourteenth Judicial District Court [Number 01-6308], for the Parish of Calcasieu, State of Louisiana; the Honorable Fred R. Godwin, District Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff company sued defendant city for lost profits after the city annexed certain immovable property into its city limits that prohibited the company from continuing fireworks sales on the annexed land that it had leased. The Fourteenth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Calcasieu, Louisiana, granted the city's summary judgment motion. The company appealed.


OVERVIEW: The company had leased the subject property to operate seasonal fireworks sales establishments. The city annexed the property into its corporate limits in 2000, such that the property became subject to the city's ordinance that prohibited the sale of fireworks within the corporate limits. The ordinance's application to the annexed property had the effect of preventing the company from continuing its fireworks sales on the leased property. The company filed suit to recover its lost profits from the city, asserting that the annexation constituted an unconstitutional taking of its property. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of the city. The appellate court affirmed the grant of summary judgment. The appellate court noted that, while a lessee could require the city to provide compensation for the expropriation of leased property, the property here was not taken or damaged by the annexation for purposes of eminent domain compensation. The court also held that there was no evidence that the company was led to believe that its business would not be affected by the ordinance or that the person from the city who made such a representation had the authority to do so.


OUTCOME: The grant of summary judgment was affirmed.

 

1444 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Van Dyke


03-437 consolidated with 03-438


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


03-437 (La.App. 3 Cir. 10/01/03);  856 So. 2d 187; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 2643



October 1, 2003, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. Van Dyke, 2004 La. LEXIS 552 (La., Feb. 13, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE FOURTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF CALCASIEU, NO. 17068-96. HONORABLE ALCIDE JOSEPH GRAY, DISTRICT JUDGE.
State v. Van Dyke, 856 So. 2d 203, 2003 La. App. LEXIS 2639 (La.App. 3 Cir., Oct. 1, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: An original charge against defendant in 1996, of first degree murder, was quashed by the trial court, and subsequently dismissed by the State. However, in 2002, based on the same underlying offense, a grand jury returned an indictment charging defendant with second degree murder. The Fourteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Calcasieu, Louisiana, quashed the latter indictment, and ordered defendant's release. The State sought review.


OVERVIEW: It was clear from the trial court's ruling that it calculated the time delay for commencement of trial, from the date of the original indictment. That was improper, because the dismissal of the first indictment was the result of that indictment being quashed. The State's re-indictment was not for the purpose of avoiding the time limitation established by La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 578. The State had two years from the filing of the second degree murder charge to bring defendant to trial. Thus, the trial court erred in quashing the second degree murder indictment. The remaining issue was whether defendant's constitutional right to a speedy trial was violated. The appellate court applied the four factors under Barker v. Wingo. Here, defendant had been incarcerated since his arrest in 1996, so prejudice could be presumed. However, the record established severe problems in obtaining, and retaining, and funding qualified counsel for defendant, and that the vast majority of the delays, continuances for trial, and for hearings on pretrial motions, were attributable to the defense. Defendant failed to proffer what a purported eyewitness, who had died, would have testified to.


OUTCOME: The appellate court held that as the 1996 indictment for first degree murder had already been dismissed, the trial court was incorrect in granting a motion to quash that indictment. The appellate court held defendant was not denied his statutory or constitutional right to speedy trial, and the trial court's order quashing the indictment for second degree murder was reversed. The matter was remanded for further proceedings.

 

1445 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Houston


No. 2003-KA-0854


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2003-0854 (La.App. 4 Cir. 10/01/03); 859 So. 2d 707; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 2864



October 1, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 3, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 417-430, SECTION "I". HONORABLE RAYMOND C. BIGELOW, JUDGE.
State v. Houston, 818 So. 2d 253, 2002 La. App. LEXIS 1524 (La.App. 4 Cir., Apr. 24, 2002)



DISPOSITION: SENTENCE VACATED; REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Upon remand for sentencing for attempted possession of cocaine, the Louisiana Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish, No. 417-430, Section I, sentenced defendant under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1A, before being amended by 2001 La. Acts 403, effective on June 15, 2001, as a multiple drug offender to life imprisonment at hard labor without the benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence. Defendant appealed the sentence.


OVERVIEW: The Louisiana Supreme Court had decided that the appeals court's prior decision was correct that the 2001 La. Acts 403 amendments to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1, which provided for a sentencing range of from 20 years to life was not applicable because defendant's attempted possession occurred before its June 15, 2001 effective date. However, even though the mandatory life sentence provided by § 15:529.1, before 2001 La. Acts 403, had been declared constitutional as a part of the entire Habitual Offender Law being declared constitutional, the imposition of a mandatory life sentence could still be unconstitutionally excessive under the facts of a particular case, such as defendant's case. The trial court, which had originally imposed a 30-year sentence, had apparently imposed the mandatory minimum life sentence on remand because it believed that sentence was its only alternative. The appeals court stated that, upon another remand, the trial court was to consider the Dorthey case to determine whether to impose a lesser sentence.


OUTCOME: The appeals court reversed the sentencing judgment and remanded the case for resentencing.

State v. Oliver


No. 03-KA-416


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


03 416 (La.App. 5 Cir. 10/01/03);  857 So. 2d 1227; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 2654



September 30, 2003, Decided

Post-conviction relief denied at State ex rel. Oliver v. State, 941 So. 2d 36, 2006 La. LEXIS 3183 (La., Nov. 9, 2006)
Post-conviction relief denied at State ex rel. Oliver v. State, 963 So. 2d 387, 2007 La. LEXIS 1894 (La., 2007)
Transferred by State ex rel. Oliver v. State, 994 So. 2d 5, 2008 La. LEXIS 2271 (La., 2008)
Post-conviction relief denied at State ex rel. Oliver v. State, 996 So. 2d 1087, 2008 La. LEXIS 2633 (La., 2008)
Writ denied by, As moot State ex rel. Oliver v. State, 6 So. 3d 790, 2009 La. LEXIS 320 (La., 2009)
Decision reached on appeal by, Writ denied by State v. Oliver, 30 So. 3d 946, 2009 La. App. LEXIS 2202 (La.App. 5 Cir., 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 01-0955, DIVISION "P". HONORABLE MELVIN C. ZENO, JUDGE PRESIDING.
State ex rel. Oliver v. State, 845 So. 2d 1063, 2003 La. LEXIS 1761 (La., May 30, 2003)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted with theft of goods. The State filed a multiple bill, alleging defendant to be a fourth felony offender. The trial court resentenced defendant as a fourth felony offender to imprisonment at hard labor for 20 years. The 24th District Court, Parish of Jefferson, Louisiana, denied defendant's motion for reconsideration. She appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was engaged in a scheme, wherein she stole large houseware items from local retailers. Although convicted twice before for theft, she continued to engage in this illegal activity. Upon her conviction for theft of goods in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:67.10, she was sentenced to 20 years imprisonment as a fourth felony offender. The appellate court upheld her sentence, because it was not unconstitutionally excessive given that the sentencing range for a fourth felony offender was between two and 20 years of imprisonment under the Habitual Offender Law, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1(A)(1)(c)(i).


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1447 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Town of Church Point v. Acadia Parish Police Jury


No. 03-1268


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


03-1268 (La.App. 3 Cir. 09/19/03);  865 So. 2d 755; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 2486



September 19, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE FIFTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF ACADIA, No.80,764. HONORABLE JULES D. EDWARDS, III, DISTRICT COURT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Fifteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Acadia (Louisiana), entered a judgment that found an election to create a mosquito control sales tax district was a constitutional exercise of appellee police jury's authority and sufficient to satisfy statutory law for that sales tax district to levy and collect sales and use tax, and/or to fund the tax proceeds into bonds. Appellants, a town and its mayor, appealed.


OVERVIEW: The police jury adopted an ordinance creating the mosquito control sales tax district. On that same date, the police jury, acting as the district's governing authority, adopted a resolution calling for a special election to place the proposition before the voters authorizing the district to levy and collect the tax. The electors cast more votes for the proposition than against it. Thereafter, the police jury passed a resolution declaring that the proposition was carried by a majority of the qualified voters, voting in the special election. The town and mayor filed suit, pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 18:1405(E), contesting the legality of the election and the tax authorized by the passing of the proposition. The trial court found that the constitutional and statutory law permitted the police jury to hold the election to create the district and levy taxes for the district. After the town and mayor appealed, the appellate court found that constitutional law allowed a police jury, as a local government subdivision, to have the authority to levy and collect sales taxes, while statutory law permitted it to create a special district to use the additional tax so authorized.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

1448 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Brooks


No. 03-KA-391


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


2003 391 (La.App. 5 Cir. 09/16/03);  858 So. 2d 74; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 2478



September 16, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State ex rel. Brooks v. State, 2005 La. LEXIS 2618 (La., Dec. 9, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-NINTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF ST. CHARLES, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 01-0011, DIVISION "D". HONORABLE KIRK A. GRANIER, JUDGE PRESIDING.
State v. Brooks, 817 So. 2d 222, 2002 La. App. LEXIS 999 (La.App. 5 Cir., Apr. 10, 2002)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of possession of a firearm by a convicted felon. Defendant's motions for post verdict judgment of acquittal, and a motion for new trial, were denied. Defendant's subsequent direct appeal was dismissed as untimely. The Twenty-Ninth Judicial District Court, Parish of St. Charles, Louisiana, then granted defendant's uniform application for post-conviction relief, seeking an out-of-time appeal.


OVERVIEW: The parties stipulated that defendant had a prior felony conviction for unauthorized entry of an inhabited dwelling. Defendant argued his 15-year sentence, the maximum punishment allowed under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:95.1, was unconstitutionally excessive, considering that he was offered a six-year sentence prior to trial as part of a plea agreement. However, the fact that a defendant did not accept a plea bargain was not a factor listed for consideration under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 894.1. Contrary to defendant's argument, the trial court did give an adequate explanation for the maximum sentence. Aggravating factors were that defendant deliberately shot the victim in the buttocks, and also put the safety of many other people in jeopardy. Defendant's argument that the victim was not a reliable witness, was rejected. The shooting did occur at night, and the victim did not actually testify that defendant "fired" the gun. But "firing" the gun was not a necessary element of the crime. Although there were inconsistencies in the victim's testimony regarding certain details, he consistently stated that defendant had a gun. Thus, the evidence supported defendant's conviction.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence were affirmed.

Wesco v. Columbia Lakeland Med. Ctr.


No. 2003-CA-0328


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2003-0328 (La.App. 4 Cir. 09/10/03); 862 So. 2d 997; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 2528



September 10, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Rehearing denied by Wesco v. Columbia Lakeland Med. Ctr., 2004 La. App. LEXIS 184 (La.App. 4 Cir., Jan. 30, 2004)
Writ denied by Wesco v. Columbia Lakeland Med. Ctr., 2004 La. LEXIS 1532 (La., Apr. 30, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 97-11597, DIVISION "G". HONORABLE ROBIN M. GIARRUSSO, JUDGE.
Wesco v. Columbia Lakeland Med. Ctr., 801 So. 2d 1187, 2001 La. App. LEXIS 2705 (La.App. 4 Cir., Nov. 14, 2001)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient sought review from a judgment of the Civil District Court, Orleans Parish, Division "G" (Louisiana), which granted appellee doctor an exception of prescription in the patient's negligence claim and dismissed the claim.


OVERVIEW: The patient filed a claim for a medical review panel, alleging negligence by defendants, a medical center and two doctors. The patient alleged that, due to their negligence, she had to undergo a second surgery to correct what her first surgery should have accomplished. The patient failed to comply with the procedural requirements of the Medical Malpractice Act (MMA), and her proceeding before the Patient's Compensation Fund was dismissed. However, prior thereto, the patient filed suit, although no defendants were served at that time. Thereafter, one doctor and the medical center were served. The served defendants were dismissed based on exceptions of prescription. Appellee was eventually served, and the trial court dismissed the claim based on an exception of prescription. On appeal therefrom, the court held that the trial court correctly found that the gross negligence alleged against appellee was covered by the MMA, even though it was a private claim. Further, it was found that the time for filing the claim had prescribed against the patient, pursuant to the limitations set out in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5628.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Desselle v. Lafleur


03-0562


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


2003 0562 (La.App. 3 Cir. 08/06/03); 853 So. 2d 692; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 2255



August 6, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 17, 2003.
Rehearing denied by Desselle v. Lafleur, 2003 La. App. LEXIS 2496 (La.App. 3 Cir., Sept. 17, 2003)
Subsequent appeal at Desselle v. LaFleur, 865 So. 2d 954, 2004 La. App. LEXIS 156 (La.App. 3 Cir., Feb. 4, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWELFTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF AVOYELLES, NO. 2001-2656. HONORABLE MARK A. JEANSONNE, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Motion to dismiss denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Twelfth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Avoyelles, Louisiana, awarded plaintiff, claimant, a judgment in the amount of $ 450,480, in her action to recover damages she sustained in an automobile accident. Defendants, individual and town, filed a motion for a suspensive appeal, and the claimant filed a motion seeking dismissal of the suspensive appeal as untimely perfected.


OVERVIEW: The claimant moved for a new trial, and on the same day, defendants filed a motion for suspensive appeal of the judgment. The trial court refused to sign the attached order granting the suspensive appeal, and denied it as premature, pending a ruling on the pleadings filed by the claimant. The trial court denied the claimant's motion for a new trial as untimely, and defendants filed a second motion for a suspensive appeal. Defendants argued that the claimant's motion to dismiss their appeal was untimely and should be dismissed. The appellate court ruled that the claimant's motion to dismiss the appeal was timely filed. The appellate court found that the subsequently filed motion for appeal was untimely, however, the untimely filing was not due to an error imputable to defendants. The appeal was perfected untimely because the trial court erroneously refused to sign the appeal order until a formal judgment denying the motion for a new trial had been signed. The failure of the trial court to promptly consider and sign the motion for a suspensive appeal was not an irregularity, error, or defect imputable to defendants, La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 2161.


OUTCOME: The motion to dismiss was denied.

State v. Bell


No. 2002-KA-2349


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2002-2349 (La.App. 4 Cir. 08/06/03); 854 So. 2d 429; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 2289



August 6, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 3, 2003.
Writ denied by State v. Bell, 2004 La. LEXIS 547 (La., Feb. 13, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 383-127, SECTION "C". Honorable Sharon K. Hunter, Judge.
State v. Bell, 748 So. 2d 458, 1999 La. LEXIS 2617 (La., Oct. 13, 1999)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), which convicted defendant of manslaughter.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty in a previous trial. The appellate court reversed the conviction because of the unavailability of a trial transcript and remanded for a new trial. Defendant was again found guilty and was sentenced to 40 years at hard labor. She contended on appeal that the trial court erred in denying her motion to quash the indictment, based on the expiration of the 1-year time limitation for a new trial in La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 582. The court found that the period of limitation had been interrupted, pursuant to La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 583, by defendant's filing of a motion to release her without bail on the ground of a statutory speedy trial violation and by her appeal from the denial of that motion. Consequently, defendant's retrial was timely. The court also found that defendant's sentence was not excessive under the standards of La. Const. art. I, § 20, because the killing was a vicious act. After strangling and stabbing the victim, defendant left the body for the victim's young son to find. The maximum sentence for manslaughter was not too severe under the circumstances.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction and sentence.

 

1452 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Babin v. Babin


No. 2002 CA 0396


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


854 So. 2d 403; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 2187



July 30, 2003, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Writ denied by Babin v. Babin, 854 So. 2d 338, 2003 La. LEXIS 2586 (La., Sept. 24, 2003)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Babin v. Darce, 158 L. Ed. 2d 86, 124 S. Ct. 1421, 2004 U.S. LEXIS 1108 (U.S., Feb. 23, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Family Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 126,676. Honorable Annette M. Lassalle, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff father appealed a judgment from the Family Court, East Baton Rouge Parish (Louisiana), which granted visitation to defendant grandmother.


OVERVIEW: The children's mother was deceased. The maternal grandmother sought visitation pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:344, which provided that a trial court had discretion to grant grandparent visitation when a parent was deceased and when such visitation rights would be in the best interest of the children. The trial court granted visitation for four hours every three weeks. The father challenged the constitutionality of § 9:344, arguing that the statute violated his constitutionally protected fundamental right of privacy. The court, in affirming, concluded that the limited visitation granted to the grandmother did not unduly burden the father's parental rights and was constitutional. The trial court reasonably determined that visitation with the grandmother was in the children's best interest. The court noted that a grandparent did not have to show extraordinary circumstances when seeking visitation under § 9:344.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of visitation rights to the grandmother.

State v. Billard


No. 03-KA-319


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


2003-319 (La.App. 5 Cir. 08/01/03); 852 So. 2d 1069; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 2217



July 29, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 15, 2003.
Writ denied by State v. Billard, 865 So. 2d 739, 2004 La. LEXIS 415 (La., Feb. 6, 2004)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Billard v. Warden, 2006 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 94978 (E.D. La., June 6, 2006)
Writ refused by, Transferred by State ex rel. Billard v. State, 994 So. 2d 42, 2008 La. LEXIS 2189 (La., 2008)
Subsequent civil proceeding at, Decision reached on appeal by Billard v. Rhonda Kling Record Analysis, 57 So. 3d 609, 2011 La. App. Unpub. LEXIS 82 (La.App. 1 Cir., 2011)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Billard v. Prince, 2013 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 99072 (E.D. La., May 16, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 00-1041, DIVISION "M". HONORABLE HENRY G. SULLIVAN, JR., JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was found guilty of 2 counts of armed robbery, violations of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:64. The State alleged defendant to be a second felony offender based on a prior armed robbery conviction. Defendant admitted the allegations in the multiple offender bill, and the 24th Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, Division "M" (Louisiana), imposed a sentence of 50 years at hard labor without benefit of probation. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the sufficiency of the evidence used to convict him. He pointed out that one of the victims could not identify him as the perpetrator and further that the testimony of the two victims was inconsistent with their prior statements to the police. He also argued that the state failed to prove the element of force or intimidation. Although the victim could not identify defendant from the photographic lineup, other evidence at the trial negated the reasonable probability of misidentification. Defendant placed himself at the scene of the crime with a companion and both victims positively identified defendant's companion from a photographic lineup. Additionally, the other victim identified defendant at trial as the gunman. One victim testified that defendant did not point the guns directly at him; however, the victim testified that he was afraid. The appellate court held that no verbal threat was required to satisfy that element of armed robbery. It was reasonable to infer that the victim was afraid, as he was on the passenger's side of the van looking through the van at defendant who was armed with two guns. Defendant created an atmosphere of intimidation.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions and sentences were affirmed.

 

1454 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Parker


No. 03-KA-288


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


2003-288 (La.App. 5 Cir. 08/01/03); 853 So. 2d 67; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 2220



July 29, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 15, 2003.
Magistrate's recommendation at, Subsequent civil proceeding at Parker v. Butler, 2008 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 117663 (E.D. La., Oct. 20, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 99-7171, DIVISION "O". HONORABLE ROSS P. LADART, JUDGE PRESIDING.
State v. Parker, 778 So. 2d 1167, 2001 La. App. LEXIS 36 (La.App. 5 Cir., Jan. 30, 2001)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of simple burglary, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:62. The State agreed that the use of defendant's prior violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:95.1 to enhance the sentence was erroneous. The 24th Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, Division "O" (Louisiana), resentenced defendant as a second felony offender to 12 years at hard labor. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court imposed an excessive multiple offender sentence. The appellate court held that defendant's failure to file a motion to reconsider sentence or to have stated specific grounds upon which the motion was based limited defendant to a bare review of the sentence for constitutional excessiveness. In the case at bar, the trial court mistakenly found defendant to have been a third felony offender. The trial court subsequently found defendant to have been a second felony offender, vacated the life sentence, and sentenced him to 12 years of imprisonment at hard labor. The appellate court held that the jurisprudence suggested that defendant's 12-year sentence was neither shocking nor grossly disproportionate to the severity of the crime committed. Defendant's 12-year sentence was at the lower end of the sentencing range, and the appellate court found that he could have received up to 24 years of imprisonment. Additionally, defendant had a prior conviction in 1986 for simple robbery. Under the circumstances of the case at bar, the appellate court found that the sentence was not excessive and that the trial judge had not abused his discretion.


OUTCOME: Defendant's adjudication as a second felony offender and defendant's sentence of 12 years imprisonment were affirmed.

1456 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Town of Church Point v. Acadia Parish Police Jury


No. 2003-890


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


2003-890 (La.App. 3 Cir. 07/15/2003);  849 So. 2d 87; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 2140



July 14, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Rehearing denied by Town of Church Point v. Acadia Parish Police Jury, 849 So. 2d 87, 2003 La. App. LEXIS 2894 (La.App. 3 Cir., July 15, 2003)
Writ dismissed by Town of Church Point v. Acadia Parish Police Jury, 849 So. 2d 534, 2003 La. LEXIS 2211 (La., July 29, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE FIFTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF ACADIA, No. 80,456. HONORABLE GLENNON P. EVERETT, DISTRICT COURT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Fifteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Acadia, Louisiana, denied plaintiff town's request to enjoin a special tax election. The town appealed, asserting defendant parish police jury, acting as the governing authority of the Mosquito Control Sales Tax District of the parish had no statutory or constitutional authority to adopt a resolution calling for the election to authorize the District to levy and collect a tax.


OVERVIEW: The town's suit objected to the calling of a special election. Pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 18:1405(G), such actions had to be instituted within 14 days after the calling of the election. The calling of the special election occurred on May 20, 2003, by resolution. Suit was not instituted until June 25, 2003, past the 14-day period. A precedent decision established that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 18:1405(A), which allowed a 10 day period for one to object to a candidate's qualifications for office, was a peremptive period. La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 18:1405(A) (B) and (G) contained the same operative language with respect to delays, all stating that actions "shall be instituted" within the time period set forth therein. Having failed to file their claim within the 14-day period, the town's action was lost. The town could not object to the calling of the special election. The town's remedy was therefore limited to challenging the legality of the election and tax, if authorized, pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 18:1405(E).


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court denying the town's request for an injunction was affirmed. Costs of the appeal were assessed against the town.

 

1457 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Azalea Lakes P'ship v. Parish of St. Tammany


2002 CA 0050


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2002 0050 (La.App. 1 Cir. 07/02/03); 859 So. 2d 57; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 1962



July 2, 2003, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by Azalea Lakes P'ship v. Parish of St. Tammany, 858 So. 2d 429, 2003 La. LEXIS 3410 (La., Nov. 14, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 22nd Judicial District Court. Parish of St. Tammany, Louisiana. Docket No. 97-11083, Division "I". Honorable Reginald T. Badeaux, III, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Intervenor homeowners association appealed a judgment by the 22nd Judicial District Court. Parish of St. Tammany, Louisiana, that granted summary judgment in favor of plaintiff partnerships and defendant parish that resulted in the dismissal of its complaint in intervention.


OVERVIEW: The homeowners association intervened in the action between the partnerships and the parish regarding an agreement between the partnerships and the parish to develop certain planned unit development (PUD). The partnerships sought specific performance of the agreements and damages. The homeowners association challenged the validity of the agreement as it claimed the authority under which the creation of the PUD was based was unconstitutional. The appellate court noted that the state supreme court had held that La. Const. of 1921, art. XIV, § 29, as amended, did not prohibit the establishment of other types of districts best suited to the needs of the local population. The appellate court held that a PUD qualified as an "other type of district" that was best suited to the needs of the population, and thus, the authority under which the PUD was planned was not unconstitutional. The appellate court also held that that it was within the parish's police power, delegated to it by the state, to enter into a development agreement with the partnerships.


OUTCOME: The dismissal of the homeowners association's complaint in intervention was affirmed.

State v. Echeverria


2002 KA 2592


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2002 2592 (La.App. 1 Cir. 06/27/03); 858 So. 2d 632; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 1906



June 27, 2003, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State ex rel. Echeverria v. State, 2004 La. LEXIS 2501 (La., Aug. 20, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 22nd Judicial District Court. Parish of St. Tammany, Louisiana. Docket No. 337238, Division B. Honorable Elaine W. DiMiceli, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION, HABITUAL OFFENDER ADJUDICATION, AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of one count of cruelty to the infirmed. The State filed a habitual offender bill of information against the defendant, alleging he was a fourth felony habitual offender. The 22nd Judicial District Court, St. Tammany Parish (Louisiana), sentenced defendant to seven years of imprisonment at hard labor and denied defendant's motion for a new trial and motion for reconsideration of the sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that the evidence was insufficient to support his conviction for cruelty to the infirmed. Defendant also argued that his sentence was constitutionally excessive. The appellate court rejected defendant's arguments. The defendant's shoving of the victim with both hands sufficiently established his general criminal intent to mistreat the victim, and the pain caused to the victim was not an inevitable consequence of care and treatment, and thus, was unjustifiable. Further, defendant, a third felony habitual offender, shoved his 84 year-old grandmother into kitchen furniture with both hands, thereby causing her unjustifiable pain and bruises. Thus, defendant's sentence of seven years at hard labor was not unconstitutionally excessive and not grossly disproportionate to the severity of the offense.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Mudd v. Christus Health N. La.


No. 37,133-CW, No. 37,145-CW


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


37,133 (La.App. 2 Cir. 06/25/03); 850 So. 2d 911; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 1858



June 25, 2003, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected September 26, 2003.
Writ granted by, Remanded by Mudd v. Christus Health N. 857 So. 2d 507, 2003 La. LEXIS 3252 (La., Nov. 7, 2003)
Writ granted by, Remanded by Mudd v. Christus Health Northern 857 So. 2d 508, 2003 La. LEXIS 3253 (La., Nov. 7, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Application for Writs from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court Nos. 444,381 & 449,018. Honorable Scott J. Crichton, Judge.



DISPOSITION: WRIT RECALLED; JUDGMENT AFFIRMED; CASE REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On application for writs from the First Judicial District Court, Parish of Caddo (Louisiana), defendants, a hospital and a blood center, sought review of an interlocutory ruling that denied their exceptions of prescription. The appellate court initially granted a writ to examine the record more closely.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff patient underwent a hysterectomy at the hospital in early 1980. In a deposition, she stated that she received at least 10 units of blood supplied to the hospital by the blood center. She alleged that she was diagnosed with Hepatitis C in late 1998 and had no other risk factors for the disease. The trial court noted that her first doctor's records were full of modifications and that he did not give her enough information to excite her suspicion as to diagnosis and cause. Specifically, the doctor did not consider the condition serious enough to warrant further tests or treatment, so he did not put her on notice. By contrast, a second doctor made it clear to the patient in late 1998 that she had Hepatitis C and probably contracted it from the blood transfusions. The appellate court found that the trial court was not plainly wrong to find that the patient did not have actual or constructive knowledge of her condition or its cause from her first doctor and that she only received actual knowledge of those matters from the second doctor. Thus, her petition for a medical review panel, filed in June 1999, was timely. Also, the claim against the blood center was also timely.


OUTCOME: The appellate court recalled its writ, affirmed the trial court's judgment denying the hospital's and the blood center's exceptions of prescription, and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

State v. Rogers


No. 2003-KA-276


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


2003-276 (La.App. 5 Cir. 06/19/03); 850 So. 2d 838; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 1803



June 19, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. Rogers, 865 So. 2d 73, 2004 La. LEXIS 298 (La., Jan. 30, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 02-2294, DIVISION "H". HONORABLE KERNAN A. HAND, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of distribution of cocaine in the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, Louisiana. Defendant was sentenced as a third felony offender, with prior convictions for distribution of cocaine, and possession of cocaine. Defendant's motion to reconsider sentence was denied. Defendant appealed, asserting there was insufficient to support his conviction, and that he was entrapped into committing the offense.


OVERVIEW: The evidence established that an agent stopped his vehicle, rolled down the window, and asked defendant where he could get "two 20s." Two $ 20s was street slang for 2 rocks of crack cocaine. Defendant entered the passenger's side of the detective's vehicle and gave the detective directions to a house. The detective gave defendant $ 40, and defendant returned with 2 rocks of cocaine. Videotaped and audiotaped recordings of the events were entered into evidence. Defendant asserted several fairly minor contradictions between the officer's testimony, the police report, and what actually transpired. However, the appellate court found that a rational trier of fact could have found defendant's guilt beyond a reasonable doubt. As to entrapment, defendant failed to establish that the detective induced him to distribute cocaine. The evidence indicated that the detective merely furnished an opportunity for defendant to distribute crack cocaine, and there was considerable evidence that defendant was predisposed to sell cocaine. Finally, defendant signed a habitual offender bill of information, pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1, and was precluded from challenging his sentence.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed. However, the matter was remanded for the trial court to advise defendant of the prescriptive period for filing post-conviction relief.

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 401-203, SECTION "F". Honorable Dennis J. Waldron, Judge.

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.

State v. Pierre

COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT

June 11, 2003, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. Pierre, 864 So. 2d 626, 2004 La. LEXIS 189 (La., Jan. 16, 2004)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Pierre v. Leger, 2011 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 72071 (W.D. La., May 16, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE FIFTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF LAFAYETTE, NO. 79-255, HONORABLE HERMAN C. CLAUSE, DISTRICT JUDGE.
State v. Pierre, 842 So. 2d 321, 2003 La. LEXIS 727 (La., Mar. 28, 2003)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A trial court found defendant guilty of second-degree murder and attempted second-degree murder. Defendant appealed, and the intermediate appellate court reversed her conviction and sentence, finding no proper waiver a jury trial. The Supreme Court of Louisiana granted the State's writ application, reinstated the conviction and sentence, and remanded the matter for consideration of defendant's remaining claims.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of the attempted murder of her estranged husband and for the murder of her three-year-old son, after she shot both of them and then shot herself. After it was found that she voluntarily waived a jury trial, on remand the court reviewed the rest of her claims and affirmed the conviction and sentence. Her mother admitted to telling police that defendant pointed the gun at the child. Moreover, two witnesses testified that defendant made threats regarding the husband and the child. The court affirmed the mandatory sentence for second-degree murder and the mandatory minimum sentence for attempted second-degree murder, to be served consecutively. Defendant failed to show that she was exceptional under the circumstances.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentences. The court further directed the trial court to inform defendant of the two-year time limit for filing post conviction relief and to file written proof that defendant received the notice in the record of the proceedings.

Vincent v. State


2002 CW 2444


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2002 2444 (La.App. 1 Cir. 06/06/03); 858 So. 2d 494; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 1710



June 6, 2003, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON A SUPERVISORY WRIT OF REVIEW FROM THE TWENTIETH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF WEST FELICIANA, STATE OF LOUISIANA. DOCKET NUMBER 17,559-A. HONORABLE GEORGE H. WARE, JR., JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Application for supervisory writs denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate sued defendant state to recover lost property. The state responded by filing a declinatory exception of improper venue and a dilatory exception of prematurity. The exception to venue was granted, and the 20th Judicial District Court, Louisiana, transferred the matter. The inmate filed a writ application.


OVERVIEW: When the inmate was transferred in the prison system, he alleged that his personal property was lost. On appeal, the issue was whether the lost property claims were controlled by the Corrections Administrative Remedy Procedure and, therefore, subject to judicial review of the record under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:1177 or were the property claims tort claims and thereby under the district court's original jurisdiction? The appellate court concluded that lost property claims were classic matters of prison administration or conditions of confinement. Moreover, the inmate was not raising a claim of unconstitutional deprivation of a vested property right. Thus, the grant of the motion to transfer venue was proper, as the district court had appellate jurisdiction over claims brought pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:1171, et seq.


OUTCOME: The appellate court denied the application for supervisory writs.

State v. Brown


No. 2002-KA-1217


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2002-1217 (La.App. 4 Cir. 05/28/03); 853 So. 2d 8; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 1701



May 28, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 9, 2003.
Rehearing denied by State v. Brown, 2003 La. App. LEXIS 2463 (La.App. 4 Cir., Sept. 9, 2003)
Writ of certiorari denied State v. Brown, 865 So. 2d 72, 2004 La. LEXIS 297 (La., Jan. 30, 2004)
Affirmed in part and remanded in part by State v. Brown, 879 So. 2d 1276, 2004 La. LEXIS 2220 (La., July 6, 2004)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Brown v. Louisiana, 2004 U.S. LEXIS 5758 (U.S., Oct. 4, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 406-890, SECTION "H". Honorable Camille Buras, Judge.
State v. Brown, 791 So. 2d 630, 2001 La. LEXIS 2164 (La., June 29, 2001)



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED; SENTENCE REVERSED; REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), of armed robbery. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred by sentencing him to 198 years at hard labor based on a prior juvenile conviction in which he had not been afforded the right to a trial by jury. The court of appeal agreed. The juvenile matter was heard by a judge, not a jury. The juvenile court, however, did employ the requisite beyond-a-reasonable-doubt standard. The defense asserted that the circumstances of that conviction (for attempted second degree murder) demonstrated the problem with considering a juvenile conviction as an Apprendi exception. A statement from defendant at the age of 14 indicated that there was no evidence that that he participated in the crime resulting in the girl's death. In fact, the statement indicated instead that he tried to help the victim. Yet, he was adjudicated guilty of attempted second degree murder. To use such a defective juvenile adjudication to constitute a "prior conviction" for purposes of the Apprendi exception, and allow such prior conviction to be used to enhance the statutory penalty for the instant offense was constitutionally improper.


OUTCOME: The conviction was affirmed. The sentence was reversed and the case was remanded for resentencing.

Writ denied by Bd. of Dirs. of the Indus. Dev. Bd. of New Orleans, 855 So. 2d 287, 2003 La. LEXIS 2725 (La., Oct. 1, 2003)
Writ denied by Bd. of Dirs. of the Indus. Dev. Bd. of New Orleans, 855 So. 2d 288, 2003 La. LEXIS 2727 (La., Oct. 1, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 2003-3309, DIVISION "C-6". HONORABLE ROLAND L. BELSOME, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED; MOTION TO REMAND DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee city board of directors of the industrial development board sought a judicial declaration of the validity and legality of a development project and the bonds issued to finance the project. The Civil District Court of Orleans Parish, Louisiana, declared that the bonds, the proceedings held, and the actions of the board were valid and binding on appellants, citizens, taxpayers, and property owners (citizens). The citizens appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the citizens contended, inter alia, that the trial court erred in denying their motion to compel more complete answers to discovery, the state bond commission's rules and regulations governing the filing of bonds were violated by the board, and the bond issuance in question was contrary to law. The appellate court found that the citizens filed their motion to compel less than two days before the hearing and that most of the requested records were a matter of public record and not beyond the reach of the citizens. Their requests for admissions were adequately answered by the board and the trial court did not abuse its discretion in so finding. Further, the board's filing of the amended resolution to its previously approved bond application did not constitute a substantial defect, or material error or omission. As the alleged "donation" of public funds was the exemption from payment of ad valorem taxes for the lessee of the property in question, no governmental entity was actually giving up anything of value, insofar as the property owned by the board would not be subject to ad valorem taxes. Thus, no improper donation of public funds to a private entity existed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed and the citizens' motion to remand was denied.

 

1467 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Allen


No. 2003-KA-0192


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2003-0192 (La.App. 4 Cir. 06/06/03); 849 So. 2d 82; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 1708



May 28, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 23, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 430-332, SECTION "I". HONORABLE RAYMOND C. BIGELOW, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Defendant's conviction affirmed; sentence affirmed as amended.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of distribution of heroin, the lesser included offense of attempted possession of heroin with intent to distribute, in the Criminal District Court of Orleans Parish, Louisiana. Defendant was sentenced to serve five years on each count, with the sentences to run concurrently. Defendant appealed, asserting the trial court erred in imposing his sentence without the benefit of parole. The State conceded error.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended the imposition of his sentence under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:966(B)(1), for the distribution of heroin without the benefit of parole, was error. The appellate court agreed. La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:966(B)(1) did not provide that the sentence for distribution was restricted as to "parole." A major issue however, was a discrepancy in the statutory sentencing provisions. La. Rev. Stat. Ann. 40:979(B), provided that the sentence for "attempt to distribute heroin or certain narcotics" would be imprisonment for not less than "eight years." However, the sentence for the greater offense of actual distribution of heroin or certain narcotics under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:966(B)(1), was not less than "five years." Thus, the minimum sentence for the lesser-included offense was more severe than the minimum sentence for the greater offense. The appellate court concluded that under La. Const. art. I, § 20, a more stringent sentence for the attempted crime, than for the actual crime, was an excessive sentence. Thus, defendant's sentence on the attempt crime was left at five years. For the same reason, defendant's sentence on the attempt crime was amended to allow for parole.


OUTCOME: Defendant's five-year sentence for his conviction on one count of distribution of heroin was amended to exclude any restriction on parole. Defendant's sentence for the lesser-included offense of attempt to distribute heroin, was left at five years, because correction to the statutory minimum of eight years would have been constitutionally excessive. For the same reason, the attempted crime was amended to exclude any restrictions on parole.

Reaux v. La. Bd. of Med. Exam'rs


No. 2002-CA-0906


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2002-0906 (La.App. 4 Cir. 05/21/03); 850 So. 2d 723; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 1626



May 21, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 18, 2003.
Rehearing denied by Reaux v. La. Bd. of Med. Examiners, 2003 La. App. LEXIS 2332 (La.App. 4 Cir., Aug. 15, 2003)
Writ of certiorari denied Reaux v. 860 So. 2d 1138, 2003 La. LEXIS 3582 (La., Nov. 26, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 2001-5328, DIVISION "B". Honorable Rosemary Ledet, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: An administrative complaint was filed against respondent doctor. The Louisiana State Board of Medical Examiners (board) held a hearing. The board revoked the doctor's license to practice medicine. The Civil District Court, New Orleans Parish, Division "B" (Louisiana), affirmed, but clarified the board's decision to reflect that fewer patients were involved than might have been suggested by the board's opinion. The doctor appealed.


OVERVIEW: The crux of the complaint against the doctor was that he prescribed narcotics and other controlled substance drugs to patients without performing physical examinations and without legitimate medical purpose in exchange for payments by those patients. The doctor claimed that expert testimony was needed to explain the meaning of the statutes involved. Unlike a jury of laypersons, the board was made up of physicians and was able to evaluate medical issues without the assistance of expert testimony. As to the argument that the statutes and regulations were unconstitutionally vague in the absence of expert testimony as to their meaning, the appellate court found dispositive the board's findings of fact that the doctor knew what the statutes and regulations meant and that any properly educated physician would have known what they meant. The doctor failed to take advantage of the second La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 49:961 961(c) meeting offered him, by insisting, improperly, that the meeting be transcribed by a court reporter. Further, he failed to preserve any right he had to another meeting by voluntarily going forward with discovery, and he thus waived the 961(c) meeting.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

1469 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Combs


No. 2002-KA-1920


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2002-1920 (La.App. 4 Cir. 05/21/03); 848 So. 2d 672; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 1634



May 21, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 16, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT. ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 393-663, SECTION "C". HONORABLE SHARON K. HUNTER, JUDGE.
State v. Combs, 793 So. 2d 570, 2001 La. App. LEXIS 1266 (La.App. 4 Cir., Mar. 14, 2001)



DISPOSITION: SENTENCE ON DISTRIBUTION CHARGE AFFIRMED; LIFE SENTENCE VACATED; CASE REMANDED FOR RESENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), denied defendant's motion to suppress and convicted him of possession of cocaine with intent to distribute and distribution of cocaine. The State filed a multiple bill, and, after hearing, the trial court found him to be a third felony offender. He was sentenced as such to life imprisonment at hard labor without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested after he sold crack cocaine to an undercover officer. Defendant was sentenced to life imprisonment for possession of cocaine with intent to distribute and seven and one-half years on the distribution conviction. Defendant appealed stating that the life sentence was excessive. The appellate court found that there was substantial evidence to rebut the presumption that the mandated life sentence was constitutional because (1) defendant had a supportive family who wanted to help him; (2) he was not in possession of a weapon when arrested, had no money in his possession, and was only a petty street drug pusher and not a major drug dealer; (3) he was a non-violent offender; (4) he admitted to his addiction; and (5) he was employed prior to his incarceration. Furthermore, because of a change in the Habitual Offender Law since his conviction, he would not qualify for a life term under the current law. Thus, the life sentence imposed was not proportionate to the crimes for which he was convicted and the sentence made no measurable contribution to the acceptable goals of punishment.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed defendant's seven and one-half year sentence on the distribution conviction. The appellate court vacated defendant's life sentence as a multiple offender on the possession of cocaine with intent to distribute conviction and remanded the case to the trial court for resentencing.

McConnico v. Red Oak Timber Co.


No. 36,985-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


36,985 (La.App. 2 Cir. 05/16/03); 847 So. 2d 191; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 1392



May 16, 2003, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 450,017. Honorable Frank H. Thaxton, III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Amended, and as amended, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant timber owner brought a suit against appellee timber company and timber co-owner three years after the timber had been cut. The First Judicial District Court, Parish of Caddo (Louisiana), found in favor of the owner under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 3:4278.1, the "timber piracy" statute. It found that the company and the co-owner acted in good faith, but ordered the pay damages and attorney fees to the owner. The parties appealed.


OVERVIEW: The timber company alleged that the trial court erred when it applied § 3:4278.1, as it cut and removed the timber from the property in question "in accordance with specific terms of a legal contract or agreement" with the co-owner. The Court of Appeal of Louisiana, Second Circuit, held that § 3:4278.1(A) allowed a timber buyer to escape the imposition of treble damages, if the buyer cut and removed timber with "the consent of" or at "the direction of" or with "a legal contract or agreement" with "the owner or legal possessor," where "the owner" was defined, in co-ownership situations, as at least 80 percent of the ownership interest in the land. The court's opinion relied heavily on the public policy describing the company's failure to identify and consult all co-owners as presumptive timber theft. The statute altered any implication of La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 798 suggesting that a single co-owner could produce a fruit or product of the immovable and owe only an accounting to a co-owner. The company's actions of cutting and removing the timber from the land without the consent of the owner constituted a violation of § 3:4278.1(A) and (C), and it was liable for treble damages.


OUTCOME: The damages awarded by the trial court were amended and increased to $ 22,500, and the attorney fees awarded were increased to $ 3,523. In all other respects the judgment was affirmed at the timber company's costs.

 

1471 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Holloway


No. 37,021-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


37,021 (La.App. 2 Cir. 05/16/03); 847 So. 2d 200; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 1396



May 16, 2003, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied State v. Holloway, 2003 La. LEXIS 3722 (La., Dec. 19, 2003)
Writ denied by State v. Holloway, 2003 La. LEXIS 3728 (La., Dec. 19, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 206,267. Honorable Charles R. Scott, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Conviction and adjudication affirmed; sentence affirmed as amended.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury for the First Judicial District Court, Parish of Caddo (Louisiana), found defendant guilty of attempted possession of cocaine. Defendant was adjudicated a habitual offender and sentenced to 20 years at hard labor, without benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The police conducted a sweep of a block in response to citizens' complaints about drug activity there. An officer saw defendant toss a plastic baggie on the ground. The baggie containing two rocks that appeared to be crack cocaine was recovered. Defendant was placed under arrest, advised of his Miranda rights, and escorted to the police car. Defendant offered to help the officers, but then recanted his statement and stated that he did not want to help the officers. The appellate court found that any rational jury could have concluded that the State established the essential elements of the crime of attempted possession of cocaine beyond a reasonable doubt. Also, the appellate court found that defendant's statement to the officers was voluntary, as it was not made in response to inducements by the officers. Additionally, when defendant tossed away the baggie, which contained suspected cocaine, the officers had probable cause to arrest defendant. Further, defendant's prior convictions were valid for habitual offender purposes, and his 20-year sentence was not excessive; however, the trial court erred in imposing the sentence without the benefit of parole.


OUTCOME: The appellate court amended defendant's sentence to remove the restriction on parole eligibility and, as amended, it affirmed defendant's conviction for attempted possession of cocaine and his adjudication as a fourth offender.

 

1472 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Moore


3003-0016


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


2003-0016 (La.App. 3 Cir. 05/14/03); 847 So. 2d 53; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 1376



May 14, 2003, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE FOURTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF CALCASIEU NO. 19562-02 HONORABLE FRED R. GODWIN, PRESIDING.
Moore v. Avoyelles Corr. Ctr., 253 F.3d 870, 2001 U.S. App. LEXIS 14172 (5th Cir. La., 2001)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was given a suspended sentence conditioned on sex offender registration after he pleaded guilty to one count of indecent behavior with a juvenile. His probation was revoked for failure to register. He failed to register after completing his prison sentence. The Fourteenth Judicial District Court Parish of Calcasieu (Louisiana) granted his motion to quash an indictment for violating La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:542(F)(1). The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's sentence for a sex crime included a requirement that he register as a sex offender pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:540 et seq. In his pro se motion to quash his indictment for failure to register defendant claimed that the completion of his sentence entitled him to a first offender pardon under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:572 and La. Const. art. IV, § 5(E)(1). The court disagreed. The court held that the first offender pardon statutory and constitutional provisions did not apply until defendant had completed his sentence and that an essential element of defendant's sentence was registration as a sex offender. The court noted that the purpose of the sex offender registration statute was to protect the public and aid in police investigations. The court also noted that a first offender pardon did not equate a full gubernatorial pardon, the former only reinstating basic citizenship rights, and further held that the pardon addressed in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:542.1(H)(1) was a full gubernatorial pardon. The court held that the issue of any mistake of law claim by defendant was not properly before it and remanded the case to the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court and remand the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

State Civ. Serv. Comm'n v. Dir. of the Dep't of Pub. Safety


NUMBER 2002 CA 1901


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2002 1901 (La.App. 1 Cir. 05/09/03); 849 So. 2d 602; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 1329



May 9, 2003, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by State Civ. Serv. Comm'n v. Dep't of Pub. Safety Dir., 2004 La. LEXIS 1254 (La., Apr. 14, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court In and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge. State of Louisiana Suit Number 488,160. Honorable Curtis A. Calloway, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Louisiana State Civil Service Commission filed suit against appellees, harbor police and Director of Louisiana Department of Public Safety, and sought injunctive and declaratory relief. The Nineteenth Judicial District Court, East Baton Rouge Parish, Louisiana, held La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33.22182. was constitutional and denied the Commission's request for injunctive relief. The Commission appealed.


OVERVIEW: The legislature enacted La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33.2218.2(A)(2)(a), which required each sworn, commissioned law enforcement officer employed on a full-time basis by a bona fide police agency of the state or its political subdivisions, headquartered in a municipality with a population in excess 450,000 and who served the welfare of the public in the capacity of a police officer to be paid an additional $ 300 per month. The Commission argued that § 33.2218.2(A)(2)(a) was unconstitutional, as it was in derogation of the authority granted to the Commission in La. Const. art. XI, §10(A)(1) to regulate the compensation of employees in state classified service. The appellate court agreed and reversed the trial court's ruling that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33.2218.2(A)(2)(a) was constitutional. The appellate court held that § 33.2218.2(A)(2)(a) was unconstitutional, as it was clearly in derogation of the uniform pay plan for employees in classified service established by the Commission. Further the legislature's enactment of § 33.2218.2(A)(2)(a) was not a constitutional exercise of the legislature's plenary power to enact legislation under La. Const. art. VI, § 14, the "minimum wage" law.


OUTCOME: The decision of the trial court was reversed, and the Commission was granted the injunctive relief it requested.

Breaux v. Lafourche Parish Council


2002 CA 1422


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2002 1422 (La. App. 1 Cir. 05/09/03); 851 So. 2d 1173; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 1337



May 9, 2003, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Costs and fees proceeding at Lafourche Parish Council v. Breaux, 845 So. 2d 645, 2003 La. App. LEXIS 1345 (La.App. 1 Cir., May 9, 2003)
Rehearing denied by Breaux v. Lafourche Parish Council, 2003 La. App. LEXIS 2383 (La.App. 1 Cir., Aug. 25, 2003)
Writ denied by Breaux v. Lafourche Parish Council, 2003 La. LEXIS 3666 (La., Dec. 12, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal From The 17th Judicial District Court In And For The Parish Of Lafourche, State of Louisiana. Docket No. 91285 "A". Honorable Judge John E. LeBlane.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee parish president filed suit for injunctive and declaratory relief against appellant parish council on the grounds that the council had circumvented provisions of the parish charter to enter contracts. The 17th Judicial District Court in and for the Parish Of Lafourche, Louisiana, granted the request and imposed limits on the council's ability to enter contracts by resolution. The council appealed.


OVERVIEW: The parish president sought injunctive relief to limit the parish council's ability to enter contracts by resolution. The trial court limited the council's ability to enter contracts by resolution, but held that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 42:263 was constitutional as it was applied to the parish. The appellate court reversed the trial court's limitation of the council's ability to enter contracts by resolution as it held that under the Lafourche Parish Home Rule Charter the council could approve a contract by resolution and could also authorize a person to sign or execute a on behalf of the council a contract that had been approved by resolution. The appellate court affirmed the trial court's determination that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 42:263 was constitutional as applied to the parish council as the statute did not impinge or abridge the council's structure or organization or distribution of powers and functions.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed to the extent it limited the parish council's ability to enter into and approve contracts by resolution, but affirmed as to the ruling that the statutory provision was constitutional as it applied to the parish.

Lafourche Parish Council v. Breaux


2002 CA 1565


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2002 1565 (La. App. 1 Cir. 05/09/03); 845 So. 2d 645; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 1345

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal From The 17th Judicial District Court In And For The Parish Of Lafourche, State of Louisiana. Docket No. 93404 "A". Honorable Judge John E. LeBlanc.
Breaux v. Lafourche Parish Council, 851 So. 2d 1173, 2003 La. App. LEXIS 1337 (La.App. 1 Cir., May 9, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and rendered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: At a preliminary injunction hearing, the 17th Judicial District Court, Lafourche Parish (Louisiana), denied appellant parish council's request for injunctive relief requesting that appellee parish president be enjoined from unilaterally awarding contracts for road construction without the council's approval and ordered the council to pay the attorney for the parish president. The council appealed.


OVERVIEW: The parish president filed a petition for declaratory judgment and injunctive relief against the council asserting that the council circumvented the provisions of the parish's home rule charter by improperly utilizing resolutions and/or motions, where ordinances would have been required. A temporary restraining order was issued. The parish president additionally asked that a preliminary and then permanent injunction issue prohibiting the council and the council members from interfering in administrative functions that were the responsibility of the parish president. The council filed an ex parte petition for injunctive relief requesting that the parish president be enjoined from unilaterally awarding contracts for road construction without its approval. Considering that the trial court specifically stated that the issue of sanctions was not before it, La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 863 was inapplicable, and attorney fees would be improper under that provision. Also, because La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 42:261(E) was declared unconstitutional, attorney fees were not appropriate under that statute. Thus, the order that the council pay the parish president's attorney was improper.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the trial court's judgment and rendered judgment in favor of the council.

State v. Jerome


No. 2003-KA-126


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


2003-126 (La.App. 5 Cir. 04/29/03); 845 So. 2d 1194; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 1220



April 29, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 01-1909, DIVISION "J". HONORABLE STEPHEN J. WINDHORST, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of four counts of distribution of cocaine, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967(A). The State filed a multiple offender bill of information, charging defendant as a third felony offender. The 24th Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, Division "J" (Louisiana), sentenced defendant to life imprisonment at hard labor without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Inter alia, defendant argued that the trial court erred in failing to properly arraign him on the habitual offender bill and additionally erred in failing to properly advise him of his right to remain silent and of the right to have a formal hearing prior to his stipulation to the multiple bill. At the multiple offender hearing, defense counsel informed the court that his client wished to stipulate to the allegations contained in the multiple bill. The trial judge additionally advised defendant that the district attorney would have to prove: (1) that he had a prior felony; (2) the appropriate time period between felonies; and (3) that he was properly advised of his rights at those proceedings. The court advised that, if he were to have a trial on the instant matter, he would have the right to remain silent, the right to cross-examine all witnesses against him, and the right to call his own witnesses. The appellate court held that defendant was properly advised of his rights and that he knowingly and intelligently waived his rights, particularly his right to a formal hearing and his right to remain silent, prior to stipulating to the multiple offender bill of information.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence were affirmed.

State v. Raiford


No. 2003-K-0098


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2003-0098 (La.App. 4 Cir. 04/23/03); 846 So. 2d 913; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 1253



April 23, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 18, 2003.
Writ of error denied State v. Raiford, 847 So. 2d 1217, 2003 La. LEXIS 1968 (La., June 18, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPLICATION FOR WRITS DIRECTED TO CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT. ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 391-156, SECTION "E". HONORABLE CALVIN JOHNSON, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: WRIT GRANTED; RELIEF DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant and co-defendant were indicted for first-degree murder. Defendant moved to suppress his confession, then a motion for a lunacy hearing was filed. Testimony on the competency issue was heard, and the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish, Section "E" (Louisiana), found that defendant was competent to proceed to trial, but granted the motion to suppress his confession. The State objected and sought writs.


OVERVIEW: The State argued that the trial court erred in suppressing defendant's confession on the grounds that his mental retardation precluded him from making a knowing and voluntary waiver of his rights. Defendant's statement, reflected that he was arrested for a carjacking, but he also told the officers that he had been with two others when they were involved in a shooting. Defendant's aunt was with him when he made his statement, but she stated that she was upset and just cried. A police sergeant testified that defendant completed the waiver of rights form prior to giving a taped statement; in fact he testified that defendant's completion of the form was reflected in the taped statement, even though the statement showed that defendant said he could not read or write well, so the sergeant read the form to defendant. The expert testimony overwhelmingly indicated that defendant was not able to understand and intelligently waive his rights as given to him at the time he made his statement. The extrinsic evidence that would have mitigated against the experts' opinions was minimal. The appellate court could not say the trial court had been manifestly erroneous in suppressing the confession.


OUTCOME: The State's writ was granted, but the trial court's ruling suppressing defendant's statement was affirmed.

State v. Fleming


No. 2002-KA-1700


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2002-1700 (La.App. 4 Cir. 04/16/03); 846 So. 2d 114; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 1178



April 16, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. Fleming, 2003 La. LEXIS 3564 (La., Nov. 26, 2003)
Writ denied by State v. Fleming, 2003 La. LEXIS 3565 (La., Nov. 26, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 401-182, SECTION "K". Honorable Arthur Hunter, Judge.
State v. Fleming, 820 So. 2d 467, 2002 La. LEXIS 2153 (La., June 21, 2002)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A grand jury indicted defendants for first-degree murder. The Orleans Parish criminal district court granted defendants' motion to quash their indictments based on equal protection and due process violations in the selection of the grand jury foreperson in Orleans Parish from 1987 to 2000. The State appealed directly to the Louisiana Supreme Court, which transferred the matter to the court to be treated as an appeal by the parties.


OVERVIEW: The district court quashed defendants' indictment, finding that they presented a prima facie case of discrimination in the selection of the jury forepersons in violation of the Equal Protection and Due Process Clauses of the federal Constitution and that former La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 413(C) was an unconstitutional local or special law. The State claimed that defendants failed to show a prima facie case of discrimination in the selection of grand jury forepersons between 1987 and 2000. The court agreed. Defendants failed to make a statistical showing of substantial under-representation of African Americans and women over a substantial period of time. The judge who selected the grand jury testified that he attempted to seat a grand jury representative of the parish's demographics. Such did not address selection of the forepersons. Moreover, defendants' statistical evidence was drawn from incomplete data, and the selecting judge's race and gender, relied on in defendants' analyses, were irrelevant. There was also no proof of a due process violation, especially given that the foreperson's role was ministerial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the district court's decision quashing the indictments and remanded the case to the district court for further proceedings.
