State v. Umezulike


2002-1165


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


2002-1165 (La.App. 3 Cir. 04/09/03); 843 So. 2d 614; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 1041



April 9, 2003, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 14, 2003.
Rehearing denied by State v. Umezulike, 2003 La. App. LEXIS 1435 (La.App. 3 Cir., May 14, 2003)
Writ granted by State v. Umezulike, 852 So. 2d 1017, 2003 La. LEXIS 2337 (La., Sept. 5, 2003)
Reversed by, Remanded by State v. Ifiany Obrinna Umezulike, 2004 La. LEXIS 616 (La., Feb. 25, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE FIFTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF LAFAYETTE, NO. 2000MD87871. HONORABLE THOMAS R. DUPLANTIER, DISTRICT COURT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A commissioner of the Fifteenth Judicial District issued a search warrant. Subsequently, defendant was charged with possession of marijuana and possession of drug paraphernalia, both misdemeanors. The 15th Judicial District Court, Lafayette Parish (Louisiana), denied defendant's motion to suppress, which challenged the constitutional propriety of a court-appointed commissioner issuing a search warrant. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the constitutionality of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:716(B)(1), which authorized the commissioner to sign search warrants. A judge testified and explained that the judges recommended that the commissioner post be created by the legislature in order to reduce their workload and improve court efficiency by having the commissioner handle as many minor matters as possible so that the judges could devote more time to jury trials. The judge acknowledged that judges discussed the possible constitutional problems with delegating judicial authority to a commissioner who was appointed, not elected. The Court of Appeal of Louisiana, Third Circuit, concluded that § 13:716(B)(1) was unconstitutional. Defendant's constitutional due process rights were impaired by the legislature's grant of authority to appointed commissioners. The commissioner's finding of probable cause for the issuance of a search warrant was a final determination that was not reviewed by an elected judge who was vested with judicial power by the state constitution. However, the appellate court held that the portion of section (B)(1) of § 13:716 pertaining to search warrants was severable.


OUTCOME: The decision of the trial court was reversed, and defendant's motion to suppress the seized evidence was granted.

State v. Willis


No. 36,759-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


36,759-KA (La.App. 2 Cir. 04/09/03); 843 So. 2d 592; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 1029



April 9, 2003, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State ex rel. Willis v. State, 897 So. 2d 593, 2005 La. LEXIS 967 (La., Apr. 1, 2005)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Willis v. State, 897 So. 2d 598, 2005 La. LEXIS 986 (La., Apr. 1, 2005)
Post-conviction relief denied at State ex rel. Willis v. State, 2015 La. LEXIS 46 (La., Jan. 16, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Third Judicial District Court for the Parish of Lincoln, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 47644. Honorable Cynthia T. Woodard, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Convictions affirmed. Sentences affirmed as amended.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Third Judicial District Court, Parish of Lincoln, Louisiana, convicted defendant of possession of marijuana with intent to distribute and possession of a firearm by a convicted felon. He was adjudicated to be a second felony habitual offender and his sentences were to run consecutively without benefit. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant challenged the sufficiency of the evidence to convict him of the offenses and contended the trial court erred by allowing the State to mention in front of the jury the name and nature of his prior convictions. The appellate court found that the marijuana was in the motel in which defendant was staying. His actual possession was established by the testimony of a co-defendant, who stated that the marijuana belonged to defendant and that he was selling marijuana out of his van. As there was no internal contradiction or irreconcilable conflict with the physical evidence, this accomplice's testimony, which was not uncorroborated, was sufficient support for a requisite factual conclusion. Further, the officers' testimony clearly proved that the firearm was subject to defendant's dominion and control, as it was located under the covers in close proximity to defendant's hand. The use of the prior felonies was appropriate to prove defendant was a convicted felon. Denial of defendant's motion to suppress was proper, as the law enforcement officers were lawfully at the door of the motel room where the presence of the marijuana was in plain view.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were affirmed; his sentence for possession of marijuana was amended, deleting the requirement that the first five years of the sentence be served without benefit. As amended, the sentences were affirmed.

City of Kenner v. Kyle


No. 2002-CA-1262


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


2002-1262 (La.App. 5 Cir. 04/08/03); 846 So. 2d 34; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 1017



April 8, 2003, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 577-846, DIVISION "O". HONORABLE ROSS P. LaDART, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; VACATED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff city instituted a petition for declaratory judgment, naming as defendant, the Legislative Auditor of the State of Louisiana. The city sought a judgment declaring that a city ordinance granting a temporary abatement of municipal ad valorem taxes did not violate La. Const. art. VII, § 20(A)(3). The Twenty-Fourth judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), granted partial summary judgment for the city. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court declared that the legislative auditor did not have power and/or authority to determine the constitutionality vel non of ordinances adopted by the city. The trial court also declared that the taxes levied by the city were "special taxes" that were subject to the homestead exemption, as provided in La. Const. art. VII, § 20(A)(1). The legislative auditor contended that he was not attempting to challenge the constitutionality of a municipal ordinance, but was merely attempting to adhere to his obligation to approve of the ad valorem property taxes collected by the tax recipient agency. The appellate court held the legislative auditor was required to abide by the provisions of the city ordinances, and he was without legal power or authority to withhold approval of the ad valorem property taxes of the city, absent a judicial determination, that the application of the homestead exemption to those taxes was unconstitutional. Thus, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in rendering a declaratory judgment declaring that the legislative auditor did not have the power or authority to challenge the constitutionality of the city ordinances.


OUTCOME: Because the trial court reached the merits of the constitutional challenge to the city ordinances prematurely, the appellate court vacated and set aside, in part, the summary judgment granted insofar as it declared that the subject ordinances were special ad valorem taxes that were subject to the homestead exemption pursuant to constitutional provisions. In all other respects, the judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

1482 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


EnerQuest Oil & Gas, LLC v. Asprodites


No. 2002 CA 0822


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2002 0822 (La.App. 1 Cir. 04/02/03); 843 So. 2d 535; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 811; 159 Oil & Gas Rep. 1078



April 2, 2003, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Rehearing denied by Enerquest Oil & Gas, LLC v. Asprodites, 2003 La. App. LEXIS 1574 (La.App. 1 Cir., May 13, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the 19th Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 483,395. The Honorable J. Michael McDonald, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, an oil and gas company, opposed another operator's request for administrative approval of an operator change for certain wells and units. After a hearing, appellee, the conservation commissioner and assistant secretary of state natural resources, granted the requested change. The decision was upheld by judgment of the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, East Baton Rouge Parish, Louisiana. The company appealed.


OVERVIEW: Appellant company was the designated operator of two wells that were not operating. It apparently had no intentions of conducting production operations. It had a .49 percent working interest in one unit and a 6.25 percent working interest in another. The other operator, which the commissioner designated as the new operator of record, and which intervened in the proceedings and supported the commissioner's order, had 63.53 and 87.85 percent working interests in the two wells. The appellate court found that it was realistic to assume that the party with the greater interest had more incentive to rework the wells. The company argued that the commissioner did not have authority to determine the validity of the mineral leases. However, the appellate court found that the commissioner merely took into consideration which party had a majority interest in the two units. The commissioner's authority in the instant matter was derived from La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 30:4. The commissioner was charged with preventing waste. The non-operation of the wells was wasteful to the other interested owners. Ownership issues in relation to wellbores and casing were not before the appellate court.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1483 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lee


No. 2002-KA-1793


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2002-1793 (La.App. 4 Cir. 04/02/03); 844 So. 2d 970; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 1065



April 2, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. Lee, 855 So. 2d 330, 2003 La. LEXIS 2929 (La., Oct. 10, 2003)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Lee v. Michael, 2011 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 79330 (E.D. La., May 2, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 414-519, SECTION "K". Honorable Arthur Hunter, Judge.
State v. Lee, 787 So. 2d 1020, 2001 La. App. LEXIS 1187 (La.App. 4 Cir., Apr. 6, 2001)



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AFFIRMED; SENTENCES AFFIRMED IN PART, VACATED AND REMANDED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After three mistrials, a jury for the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish, Section "K" (Louisiana), found defendant guilty of five counts of forcible rape and three counts of second degree kidnapping. Defendant was sentenced for each count, and the trial court sentenced defendant to two years for possessing a firearm at the time he committed at least one of the crimes. All sentences were to run concurrently. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a former police officer who was accused of raping several victims. A review of the record revealed an error patent, as La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 893.3(A) only provided for a two-year mandatory minimum sentence for the offense in which defendant possessed a firearm and did not provide for a separate sentence. Thus, defendant's separate two-year sentence, pursuant to art. 893.3(A), was improper and had to be vacated. But, the evidence was sufficient to establish that defendant possessed a firearm during the commission of one of the crimes, and a mandatory minimum sentence of two years for that crime would be appropriate. Additionally, it was not a gross abuse of discretion for the trial court to deny defendant's motion to quash his indictment or to bar his fourth trial, and double jeopardy did not bar his retrial. Furthermore, the evidence was sufficient to convict defendant of the forcible rapes and second-degree kidnappings of the victims. In addition, the trial court did not admit inadmissible evidence of defendant's bad character and other bad acts into evidence. However, even if it was error to admit any of the objectionable evidence, the errors were harmless.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed defendant's convictions for forcible rape and second-degree kidnapping. The appellate court vacated in part defendant's separate two-year sentence for possession of a firearm during the commission of one of the crimes and remanded that portion of the judgment to the trial court for a factual finding and appropriate resentencing. The appellate court affirmed the remainder of defendant's sentences.

 

1484 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Williams v. City of Baton Rouge


2002 CA 0682


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2002 0682 (La. App. 1 Cir. 03/28/03); 844 So. 2d 360; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 763



March 28, 2003, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 19th Judicial District Court. Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana. Docket No. 406,622, Division "I". Honorable R. Michael Caldwell, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AMENDED AND AFFIRMED AS AMENDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, an injured person and her minor daughter, filed an action against defendant City of Baton Rouge/Parish of East Baton Rouge to recover for injuries received in a fall on a broken sidewalk. The City/Parish appealed from the judgment of the 19th Judicial District Court, Division I, Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana, in favor of plaintiffs. The injured person answered the appeal, seeking increased general damages and other relief.


OVERVIEW: The injured person sustained a severe back injury when she tripped on a broken sidewalk that was partially covered by vegetation. She filed an action to recover damages from the City/Parish, which was within the latter's right-of-way and its responsibility regarding care and maintenance. The City/Parish appealed from a judgment awarding damages to plaintiffs. Plaintiffs answered the appeal, seeking an increase in general damages, court costs, and a reversal of the finding that the injured person was 40 percent at fault. The court held that there was no manifest error in the conclusion that the depression in the sidewalk, which was at least partially obscured by plant material, constituted a defect that presented an unreasonable risk of danger to the ordinary, prudent pedestrian; hence, the City/Parish was properly found liable under La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 2317. The court also found no legal error or manifest error in the allocation of fault to the injured person under La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 2323(A), given that she had a four-foot-wide sidewalk, but walked exactly where the depression was, but held that she was entitled to court costs under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:5112.


OUTCOME: The court amended the judgment by awarding additional court costs to plaintiffs to be paid by the City/Parish. As amended, the court affirmed the judgment. Costs of the appeal were assessed against the City/Parish.

 

1485 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Farhood


No. 2002-KA-490


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


2002-490 (La.App. 5 Cir. 03/25/03); 844 So. 2d 217; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 711



March 25, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 20, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE 24TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 00-1072, DIVISION "F". HONORABLE PATRICK J. MCCABE, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the 24th Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), of attempted manslaughter. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred by imposing the maximum sentence. The court of appeals disagreed. The trial court complied with the requirements of the sentencing guidelines by taking into account both mitigating and aggravating circumstances. It listened to the numerous witnesses presented by defendant in mitigation. The trial court specifically mentioned that defendant had indicated some sense of remorse. However, it was aware of the severe injuries suffered by the victim, including temporary blindness and brain damage, at the hands of defendant, her husband, who was twice her size. The trial court was particularly impressed with defendant's callousness in beating the victim nearly to death and leaving her alone to die. For those reasons, the seriousness and callousness of the crime, in the trial court's opinion, warranted a serious sentence. A lesser sentence would have deprecated the seriousness of the offense. Therefore, the trial court did not err.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Gaddis


No. 36,661-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


36,661 (La.App. 2 Cir. 03/14/03); 839 So. 2d 1258; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 662



March 14, 2003, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State ex rel. Gaddis v. State, 872 So. 2d 519, 2004 La. LEXIS 1701 (La., May 14, 2004)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Gaddis v. Louisiana, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 2542 (U.S., Mar. 21, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 209,037. Honorable John Mosely, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: By grand jury indictment, defendant was charged with second-degree murder. After a jury trial, the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana, entered judgment convicting him of the responsive verdict of manslaughter and sentenced him to life imprisonment without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence after his adjudication as a fourth-felony offender. Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for shooting a woman after an altercation. The court found sufficient evidence in the record to support the manslaughter conviction under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:31 and the jury's rejection of defendant's self-defense claim. A witness testified that defendant shot the woman while she was seated and unarmed, expert testimony corroborated that the wound was inflicted from a standing position while the victim was seated, and no gun was found at the scene to corroborate defendant's claim that the victim was armed. The court also found that self-defense instruction, while erroneous, was not a basis for reversal. The instruction improperly put the burden of proving self-defense on defendant, but in light of all other instructions, in which the burden was properly put on the State to prove all elements of the crime and in which the jury was to determine the credibility of witnesses, the court found no prejudice. The court also affirmed the enhanced sentence under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1(A)(1)(c)(ii). Defendant failed to show that he was an exceptional defendant for which downward departure from the mandatory minimum sentence was required.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction and sentence.

State v. Williams


No. 2002-KA-0260


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2002-0260 (La.App. 4 Cir. 03/25/03); 842 So. 2d 1143; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 697



March 12, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 8, 2003.
Writ denied by State v. Williams, 864 So. 2d 625, 2004 La. LEXIS 187 (La., Jan. 16, 2004)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Williams v. State, 2007 La. LEXIS 716 (La., Mar. 23, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH NO. 417-851, SECTION "L" Honorable Terry Alarcon, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Criminal District Court of the Orleans Parish, Section L, Louisiana, convicting him of second degree kidnapping, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:44.1, and sentencing him to 20 years at hard labor with the first two years to be served without benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence.


OVERVIEW: The evidence showed defendant forcibly detained the victim, his wife, inside the residence. During the encounter when she tried to escape, defendant threatened her with a shovel, forcing her to go back inside the residence. In addition, the victim testified defendant beat her while they were inside the residence. The appellate court determined that the evidence was sufficient to support a conviction under either La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:44.1A(3) or A(5) and B(3). Defendant asserted that the evidence was insufficient to support his conviction. The appellate court determined that the issue was whether defendant's conviction could be upheld based upon La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:44.1B(3), even though the subsection alleged in the bill of information was La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:44.1B(1). The appellate court ruled that defendant's conviction need not be reversed where the evidence was insufficient to support a conviction under one subsection of the statute, when the evidence was sufficient to convict defendant under another subsection of that statute. Furthermore, there was no merit to defendant's assertion that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:44.1 was unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1488 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Morgan


No. 2002-KA-1489


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2002-1489 (La.App. 4 Cir. 03/12/03); 842 So. 2d 1126; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 699



March 12, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 8, 2003.
Writ denied by State v. Morgan, 2003 La. LEXIS 3037 (La., Oct. 17, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH NO. 416-861, SECTION "L" Honorable Terry Alarcon, Judge.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED; SENTENCE AMENDED AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED AS AMENDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish No. 416-861, Section L (Louisiana), of possession with intent to distribute heroin. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred by denying his motion to suppress evidence, as the police lacked probable cause to conduct a warrantless search of his car's gas cap. The court of appeals disagreed. When police went to execute a search warrant, they conducted a brief surveillance from an area near defendant's residence. An officer testified that he spotted defendant four blocks from his residence standing next to a gray Buick Le Sabre. He then saw a red truck pull up next to the Le Sabre and a man exit the truck. Defendant and the truck driver then engaged in a brief conversation. The truck driver then reached into his pocket, pulled out an unknown amount of money, and handed it to defendant. Defendant walked to the gas cap compartment, pulled out a white package containing a plastic bag, and handed it to the truck driver. The truck driver then got back into the red truck and departed. Therefore, the police had probable cause to search defendant's gas cap, and the trial court did not err by denying defendant's motion to suppress.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed. The sentence was amended to delete the prohibition against parole.

 

1489 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Bentley


No. 2002-KA-1564


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2002-1564 (La.App. 4 Cir. 03/12/03); 844 So. 2d 149; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 700



March 12, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 8, 2003.
Writ denied by State v. Bentley, 2003 La. LEXIS 3381 (La., Nov. 14, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH NO. 422-802, SECTION "L" HONORABLE TERRY ALARCON, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a jury trial, defendant was convicted as charged by amended bill of information with distribution of cocaine. He was subsequently charged and found guilty of being a multiple offender, and the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish, Section L (Louisiana), sentenced him to 20 years in the custody of the department of corrections. Defendant's motions to reconsider and to quash the multiple bill were denied. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed from his conviction for distribution of cocaine and his sentence imposed for being a multiple offender. On appeal the court affirmed the conviction, holding that defendant's motion for a mistrial in reference to the prosecutor's comments during closing argument was properly denied. Although La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 770(2) barred the prosecutor from referencing other crimes in the closing, the court found that there was overwhelming evidence of defendant's guilt to make any error harmless beyond a reasonable doubt. Moreover, the prosecutor's subsequent statement immediately following his reference to other crimes was not an additional reference to other crimes but was a reference to an earlier statement made by the defense. The court also held that the 20-year sentence was not excessive. It was the minimum required under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15;529.1A(1)(b)(ii), and defendant's drug addiction and non-violent criminal history were not exceptional circumstances warranting a downward deviation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

State v. Bolton


No. 2002-KA-1034


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


2002-1034 (La.App. 5 Cir. 03/11/03); 844 So. 2d 135; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 643



March 11, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 20, 2003.
Writ denied by State v. Bolton, 858 So. 2d 417, 2003 La. LEXIS 3384 (La., Nov. 14, 2003)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Bolton v. Cooper, 2007 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 99177 (E.D. La., Aug. 13, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 99-6389, DIVISION "G". HONORABLE ROBERT A. PITRE, JR., JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED; REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was found guilty in the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, Louisiana, of distribution of marijuana. The State filed an amended multiple offender bill of information to allege defendant was a second felony offender. Defendant admitted to being a second felony offender and was sentenced to 15 years of imprisonment at hard labor without benefit of probation or suspension of sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was observed by the police holding a brown bag with a clear plastic bag inside. As the police approached, they saw defendant receiving money from a man while simultaneously passing a clear plastic bag with green vegetable matter to the man. Both defendant and the man he was selling the drugs to were arrested. The man who bought the marijuana testified on behalf of the defense that the marijuana was his, but the jury apparently discounted that testimony and believed the testimony of the police instead. The appellate court held that: (1) sufficient evidence existed to convict defendant, as the physical evidence supported the version presented by the police, and the jury's finding that the police were more credible would not be re-weighed on appeal; (2) evidence of the marijuana and scales did not have to be suppressed, as the police had reasonable suspicion of criminal activity based on what they observed and the location where the sale took place; and (3) defendant's sentence was not excessive, as he offered no evidence other than that he was a hardworking husband to rebut the constitutionality of the mandatory minimum sentence that was imposed.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence were affirmed, but the case was remanded for the trial court to properly advise defendant of the prescription period for filing post-conviction relief.

State v. Harris


No. 2002-KA-2099


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2002-2099 (La.App. 4 Cir. 03/05/03); 842 So. 2d 432; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 649



March 5, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected April 8, 2003. Released for Publication May 2, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 428-718, SECTION "I". HONORABLE RAYMOND C. BIGELOW, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Criminal District Court of Orleans Parish (Louisiana), which convicted her of second-degree battery and imposed a sentence of two years in prison.


OVERVIEW: Defendant got into an argument with a co-worker about her work assignment. As a result of the argument, defendant threw hot grease on the co-worker. Defendant contended that she acted in self-defense. After she was convicted of second-degree battery, defendant sought review. In affirming, the court determined that there was sufficient evidence to support defendant's conviction. The evidence demonstrated that defendant intended to inflict serious bodily harm when she threw the hot grease. Moreover, the State negated defendant's claim of self-defense by the co-worker's testimony. The court was not permitted to overturn the jury's evaluation of defendant's credibility. In addition, defendant failed to object to the jury instructions given. Therefore, the court declined to consider the issue on review. Finally, the court determined that the sentence imposed did not amount to cruel and unusual punishment. The sentence imposed was less than the maximum permitted in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:34.1. The court also noted that defendant caused severe, disabling injuries when she threw the hot grease.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

Aymond Plumbing & Heating, Inc. v. Harris


2002-1381


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


2002-1381 (La.App. 3 Cir. 03/05/03); 839 So. 2d 1145; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 599; Unemployment Ins. Rep. (CCH) P8673



March 5, 2003, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 5, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE NINTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF RAPIDES, NO. 204,581. HONORABLE GEORGE C. METOYER, JR.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Ninth Judicial District Court, Parish of Rapides, Louisiana, dismissed appellant employer's request for review of a ruling made by an administrative law judge in connection with an award of unemployment compensation benefits to appellee, its former employee. The employer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The employer argued that the trial court erred in dismissing its petition to the decision of the Department of Labor in the unemployment compensation claim. The appellate court found that the employer properly instituted its action to challenge the validity of the Louisiana Department of Labor Board of Review Rule 113 in the parish which was the domicile of the employee. La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1634(A) provided in part that the administrator, or any party to the proceedings before the board of review, could obtain judicial review thereof by filing in the district court of the claimant a petition for review of the decision, and in such proceeding any other party to the proceeding before the board of review should be made a party defendant. A challenge to the validity of an administrative rule was a civil matter falling under the original jurisdiction of the district courts.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded.

He was adjudged a second felony offender, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1(A)(2)(a), and further ordered to pay restitution to the victim. Bourgeois v. A.P. Green Indus.


No. 2002-CA-713


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


2002-713 (La.App. 5 Cir. 02/25/03); 841 So. 2d 902; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 466



February 25, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected April 22, 2003. Released for Publication April 22, 2003.
Writ denied by Bourgeois v. A. P. Green Indus., 877 So. 2d 991, 2004 La. LEXIS 2366 (La., July 16, 2004)
Related proceeding at Bourgeois v. A. P. Green Indus., 2006 La. App. LEXIS 1609 (La.App. 5 Cir., July 28, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROMTHE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA, NO. 488-642, DIVISION "Y,". HONORABLE ROBERT J. BURNS, JUDGE PRESIDING.
Bourgeois v. A.P. Green Indus., Inc., 783 So. 2d 1251, 2001 La. LEXIS 1026 (La., Apr. 3, 2001)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employees filed a class action suit against defendants, employer, executive officers, manufacturers, distributors, and insurers, due to their exposure to asbestos. The trial court denied defendants' exception of no cause of action. The Louisiana Supreme Court held that 1999 La. Acts 989 could not retroactively bar the employees claims and remanded the action to determine if the claims were barred by the workers' compensation statutes.


OVERVIEW: The employees were a class of former and current employees of the employer. The employees sought establishment of a judicially-administered medical monitoring fund and counseling program. The state supreme court previously held that medical monitoring was a compensable item of damage and that 1999 La. Acts 989 could not be applied retroactively to bar the employees' claims. The appellate court held that the employees' claims against the executive officers were not barred by the 1976 amendment to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1032, as long as the employees had significant exposure to asbestos before 1976. Finally, the appellate court noted that the employees could pursue their claims under either a state compensation scheme or the Longshore and Harbor Workers' Compensation Act (LHWCA). 33 U.S.C.S. § 901 et seq. As the employees sought compensation under the state scheme, they could sue executive officers in tort under the pre-amendment La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1032, even though that remedy was not available under the LHWCA.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Council of New Orleans v. All Taxpayers


No. 2003-CA-0189


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2003-0189 (La.App. 4 Cir. 02/21/03); 841 So. 2d 72; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 602



February 21, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Writ of certiorari denied Council of New Orleans v. All Taxpayers, 840 So. 2d 1221, 2003 La. LEXIS 1012 (La., Apr. 4, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 2002-18357, DIVISION "N-8". Honorable Ethel Simms Julien, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff city council sought a judicial declaration that a proposed bond issue was valid prior to the marketing of the bonds. Defendant citizens, a group of taxpayers, property owners, and residents of the city, filed an answer, reconventional demand, and exceptions of prematurity, vagueness, and failure to state a cause of action. The Civil District Court, Orleans Parish, Louisiana, declared that the bonds were valid. The citizens appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the citizens contended, inter alia, that the council's failure to produce a development agreement and other project documents should have precluded the trial court from validating the bonds. The appellate court disagreed, finding that the documents in the record sufficiently described the project, the source of funds, and all other material issues relevant to the bonds; the fact that subsidiary documents detailing certain aspects of the project had yet to be created did not preclude judicial validation of the bonds. Having determined that the documents were sufficient to establish the legality of the bonds, the trial court's decision that no further discovery was necessary or appropriate was not an abuse of discretion. The citizens failed to show that the dedication of the designated sales tax increments to finance the bonds either impaired any existing obligation of the city or included tax revenues previously dedicated for a special purpose, within the meaning of the TIF statute, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:9033.3. The citizens also failed to meet their burden of proving that the TIF statute was unconstitutionally vague or that the project lacked a public purpose.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Bel v. State Farm Mut. Auto. Ins. Co.


NUMBER 2002 CA 0360


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2002 0360 (La.App. 1 Cir. 02/14/03); 845 So. 2d 459; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 328



February 14, 2003, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Subsequent appeal at Bel v. State Farm Mut. Auto. Ins. Co., 845 So. 2d 377, 2003 La. App. LEXIS 336 (La.App. 1 Cir., Feb. 14, 2003)
Writ of error denied Bel v. State Farm Mut. Auto. Ins. Co., 845 So. 2d 1058, 2003 La. LEXIS 1784 (La., May 30, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Twenty-Second Judicial District Court In and for the Parish of St. Tammany, State of Louisiana. Suit Number 98-11637. Honorable Martin E. Coady, Judge.
Bel v. State Farm Mut. Auto. Ins. Co., 785 So. 2d 821, 2001 La. LEXIS 574 (La., Feb. 9, 2001)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff insured, individually and on behalf of the estate of her husband, and plaintiff individuals, sued defendant insurer and others for damages arising out of an automobile accident. The insurer moved for summary judgment, which was granted by the Twenty-Second Judicial District Court for the Parish of St. Tammany (Louisiana). The insured and individuals appealed.


OVERVIEW: The insured's deceased husband signed a waiver rejecting underinsured/uninsured (UM) motorist coverage under the insured's personal liability umbrella policy (PLUP). The appellate court found that: (1) La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22:1406(D)(1)(a)(i), (ii) clearly allowed any insured named in the policy to reject UM coverage, the insured's husband was a named insured, and he had the authority under the statute to execute a valid waiver of UM coverage under the PLUP; (2) under La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 2346 each spouse acting alone was authorized to manage, control, or dispose of community property and because the community property laws governed the insured's husband's ability to reject UM coverage under the PLUP despite the language in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22:1406(D)(1)(a)(i), the appellant court did not reach the issue of the constitutionality of § 22:1406(D)(1)(a)(i); and (3) the insurance rejection form complied with applicable state law in that it gave the insured a clear, meaningful choice between the three legal options available, and no legal option was foreclosed.


OUTCOME: The district court's judgment was affirmed.

 

1498 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Booker


2002 KA 1269


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2002 1269 (La.App. 1 Cir. 02/14/03) 839 So. 2d 455; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 349



February 14, 2003, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Rehearing denied by State v. Booker, 2003 La. App. LEXIS 772 (La.App. 1 Cir., Mar. 24, 2003)
Writ of certiorari denied State v. Booker, 2003 La. LEXIS 3185 (La., Oct. 31, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-SECOND JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT (NUMBER 329035), PARISH OF ST. TAMMANY, STATE OF LOUISIANA. HONORABLE PETER J. GARCIA, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Conviction and sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Twenty-Second Judicial District Court, St. Tammany Parish (Louisiana), of second-degree murder. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the evidence was insufficient to sustain his conviction. The court of appeal disagreed. The evidence clearly established that the child was severely abused and neglected throughout her life. The four-year-old child was bound, beaten, and deprived of food. Although the immediate cause of the child's death was listed as hypothermia, the secondary causes listed were battered child syndrome and malnourishment. Medical testimony at trial clearly indicated that the child's weakened physical condition, which was due to malnourishment and battered child syndrome, hastened her death. The medical testimony presented at trial, particularly the testimony indicating the existence of fresh or recent abusive wounds, some of which were only hours old, reasonably supports the conclusion that the child was beaten severely, possibly rendered unconscious, tied up, and left in an unheated room prior to her death. Viewing that evidence, together with defendant's admission that he intentionally struck the child and restrained her, any rational trier of fact could have concluded beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant was engaged in cruelty to a juvenile.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1499 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Foster


No. 2002 KA 1259


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2002-1259 (La.App. 1 Cir. 02/14/03); 845 So. 2d 393; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 350



February 14, 2003, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied State v. Foster, 2003 La. LEXIS 2776 (La., Oct. 3, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the 19th Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 1-01-635. The Honorable Bonnie Jackson, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged by grand jury indictment with conspiracy to commit malfeasance, and conspiracy to commit money laundering. Defendant filed a pre-trial motion to quash the indictment that the 19th Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana, granted. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: A grand jury investigated a state government official, who was indicted for malfeasance, maintaining false public records, and conspiracy to commit money laundering. Defendant was indicted for complicity in the same scheme that was the subject of his immunized testimony before the grand jury. The trial court held a Kastigar hearing. Defendant called upon the State to affirmatively demonstrate that his indictment and any evidence to be used against him did not emanate directly or indirectly from his compelled grand jury testimony. The State called no witnesses. On appeal, the State contended the trial court erred in holding the Kastigar hearing. The State cited no authority that stood for the proposition that the trial court could not hold the hearing contemplated by Kastigar prior to trial when defendant asserted a Kastigar violation in a pre-trial motion. The appellate court was unswayed by the argument of the State that defendant was obligated to point to some particular piece of allegedly tainted evidence in order to be entitled to a Kastigar hearing. Finally, the trial court did not err in quashing the indictment as a remedy.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

1500 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Millien


2002 KA 1006


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2002 1006 (La.App. 1 Cir. 02/14/03); 845 So. 2d 506; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 364



February 14, 2003, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-THIRD JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. (NUMBER 11,764), PARISH OF ASCENSION, STATE OF LOUISIANA. HONORABLE RALPH TUREAU, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION REVERSED AND MODIFIED; SENTENCE VACATED; REMANDED FOR RESENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a jury trial, defendant was convicted of theft of property having a value of $ 500 or more in the Twenty-Third Judicial District Court, Parish of Ascension (Louisiana). Defendant's motions for a mistrial, and for a new trial were denied. Defendant appealed, asserting the evidence was insufficient to support the verdict of guilty for felony theft, and that the trial court erred in allowing the admission of other crimes evidence.


OVERVIEW: The State established defendant's fingerprints were discovered upon three of the 13 fraudulent checks. Numerous witnesses testified that their initials were on the subject checks, and some witnesses recognized defendant as having been at their establishments. However, most witnesses could not definitively identify defendant as the person who presented the subject checks. The appellate court was not convinced the evidence proved beyond a reasonable doubt, all of the elements of the offense of theft of property having a value of $ 500 or more, and defendant's identity as the perpetrator. The State's evidence established the taking of the aggregate amount of $ 304, and defendant's identity as the perpetrator of those takings. That amount included three checks which witnesses testified defendant presented, and the three checks that had defendant's fingerprints on them. No direct evidence established defendant's identity as the person who presented the other checks. Finally, the appellate court rejected defendant's argument that the testimony of two witnesses, who observed defendant at two establishments attempting to pass checks, constituted inadmissible other crimes evidence.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for theft of property having a value of $ 500 or more was reversed, and modified to a conviction of theft of property having a value of $ 100 or more, but less than $ 500. Defendant's sentence was vacated, and the matter was remanded to the trial court for resentencing on the modified judgment of conviction.

 

1501 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lam


No. 36,862-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


36,862 (La.App. 2 Cir. 02/11/03); 837 So. 2d 749; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 288



February 11, 2003, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected April 11, 2003.
Writ of certiorari denied State v. Lam, 2003 La. LEXIS 2778 (La., Oct. 3, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 207,052. Honorable Eugene W. Bryson, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED. SENTENCE MODIFIED, AND AS MODIFIED, AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the First Judicial District Court, Parish of Caddo (Louisiana), of illegal use of a weapon. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the evidence was insufficient to sustain his conviction. The court of appeals disagreed. The evidence was clearly sufficient to conclude beyond a reasonable doubt that the defendant utilized a dangerous weapon in the latter stages of a melee. Defendant intentionally or negligently struck the head of an infant victim with a baseball bat, which foreseeably caused a serious head injury to the infant victim. The fact that a serious closed head injury was sustained by the infant victim was not contested at trial. Also, uncontested was that the bat admitted into evidence caused the infant's head injury. At least two eyewitnesses testified that defendant ran toward the mother and the infant victim wielding the bat. Those witnesses saw defendant swing the bat and strike the victim. That scenario was partially corroborated by several witnesses, including two eyewitnesses who were uninvolved in the altercation. Therefore, the evidence was sufficient to sustain defendant's conviction.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence were affirmed, but the probationary condition ordering restitution to the victim was vacated.

 

1502 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Day


2002-1039


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


2002-1039 (La.App. 3 Cir. 02/05/03); 838 So. 2d 74; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 216



February 5, 2003, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 5, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE FOURTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT PARISH OF CALCASIEU, NUMBER 20989-00. HONORABLE DAVID KENT SAVOIE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to cultivation of marijuana, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:966(A)(1), and was sentenced to serve five years at hard labor without benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence, with credit for time served. He appealed and claimed that his sentence was excessive and the 14th Judicial District Court, Parish of Calcasieu, Louisiana, erred in not applying the amendments to La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 893.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the amendments to art. 893 applied to persons convicted after June 15, 2001, and thus, the trial court erred when it applied the law in effect at the time of the offense when sentencing him. The State asserted that the sentencing provisions of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:966(A) and La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 893, in effect prior to the most recent amendments applied to defendant, which precluded him from receiving benefits. The appellate court held that defendant overlooked the clear reading of the act itself: 2001 La. Acts 403, § 6 provided that it would only have prospective effect. It was clear the legislature intended the newly amended provision of La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 893 to apply to only those defendants whose crimes were committed after June 15, 2001; the fact that the new provision became effective before defendant's conviction did not extinguish his liability for the offense committed under the prior statute. Therefore, the penalty provision under the prior law was applicable to the case at bar. The appellate court also held that the five-year sentence was not so grossly disproportionate as to shock the court's sense of justice.


OUTCOME: The conviction and sentence were affirmed.

 

1503 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Darby v. Gilbert Richard


NUMBER 2002-1154


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


2002-1154 (La.App. 3 Cir. 02/05/03); 838 So. 2d 141; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 224



February 5, 2003, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 5, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE OFFICE OF WORKERS' COMPENSATION, DISTRICT 9, PARISH OF IBERIA, NO. 01-8386, HONORABLE GLYNN F. VOISIN, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee challenged a decision of the Office of Workers' Compensation (OWC), District 9, Parish of Iberia (Louisiana), which found that: (1) the employee failed to prove that he had an accident at work resulting in an injury; and (2) his testimony was based on misrepresentations, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1208. The trial court ordered full restitution to appellee employer and fined the employee.


OVERVIEW: The employee was involved in a motor vehicle accident while working. After he was fired for unrelated reasons one week later, the employee sought workers' compensation benefits. The OWC ruled against him, and the court affirmed. The OWC did not commit legal error in failing to find that the employee's injury was caused by an on-the-job accident. The employee never mentioned his alleged back injury until after he was fired, and the treating physicians believed that any such injury would have manifested itself before the employee was fired. Furthermore, the employer introduced a videotape that showed the employee performing various activities without any restriction of movement, contrary to the employee's contentions. The employee failed to meet his burden of proof. The OWC properly found a willful misrepresentation on the employee's part that justified a forfeiture of benefits, pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1208. While the employee argued that the constitutionality of § 23:1208 should have been considered, and while the judge writing the opinion for the court argued against the statute's constitutionality, the majority found that the issue was not properly before the court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision.

State v. Alvey


No. 2002-KA-1741


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 27, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 426-536, SECTION "F". HONORABLE DENNIS J. WALDRON, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Conviction affirmed; sentence vacated; case remanded for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged by bill of information with theft, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §. 14:67(B)(1). Defendant pleaded guilty to theft, and to being a second-felony habitual offender. He was sentenced to 18 months at hard labor by the Criminal District Court of Orleans Parish, Louisiana. Defendant appealed the conviction and sentence.


OVERVIEW: The victim informed the officer that parts to his truck were at defendant's residence. Defendant advised officers that he had taken a truck bed cover off an abandoned truck. Defendant took the officers into his backyard and showed them the truck cover. They arrested him for possession of stolen property. On appeal, defendant framed his argument as one directed to intent. Viewing all of the evidence in a light most favorable to the prosecution, any rational trier of fact could have found beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant took the bed cover, valued at $ 300 or more, but less than $ 500, that he knew it belonged to another, without the other's consent, with an intent to permanently deprive the other person of the bed cover. As to defendant's sentence, the trial court only learned after imposing the sentence that defendant had been undergoing chemotherapy, and that he needed to be tested periodically to determine if leukemia was still in remission. Defendant had a valid argument that placing defendant in prison for one and one half years might be disproportionate to his actions.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the conviction, and the sentence was vacated.

January 28, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 25, 2003.
Appeal after remand at State v. Hernandez, 2003 La. App. LEXIS 2849 (La.App. 5 Cir., Oct. 15, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE 24TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 00-392, DIVISION "C". HONORABLE ALAN J. GREEN, JUDGE PRESIDING.
State v. Hernandez, 815 So. 2d 126, 2002 La. App. LEXIS 769 (La.App. 5 Cir., Mar. 13, 2002)



DISPOSITION: SENTENCE VACATED; CASE REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to armed robbery and agreed to a five year sentence, even though La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:64 provided for a minimum 10 year sentence. The State appealed and the plea agreement was vacated. Defendant pled guilty and the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, Louisiana, sentenced defendant to five years at hard labor, without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was 16 when he committed the crime. The trial court stated that it was deviating from the minimum mandatory sentence due to defendant's age, that this was his first conviction, and that he had a great deal of support from his family. The State argued that the trial court abused its discretion in imposing a sentence of five years' incarceration at hard labor for the crime of armed robbery where the mandatory minimum sentence was 10 years' incarceration at hard labor. The State contended that the facts of the case did not support the imposition of a sentence below the 10 year minimum penalty provided in La. Rev. Stat. § 14:64, and that the trial court failed to provide a sufficient basis for the downward departure. The instant court agreed and noted that the absence of violent offenses and defendant's age could not be the basis for a downward departure from the minimum sentence. As the State was not part of the sentencing agreement, defendant could withdraw his guilty plea.


OUTCOME: Defendant's sentence was vacated. The case was remanded to the trial court for further proceeding, reserving to defendant the right to withdraw his guilty plea.

State v. Wilson


No. 2002-KA-0776


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2002-0776 (La.App. 4 Cir. 01/22/03); 839 So. 2d 206; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 105



January 22, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 20, 2003.
Writ denied by State v. Wilson, 2003 La. LEXIS 3027 (La., Oct. 17, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 418-605, SECTION "L". Honorable Terry Alarcon, Judge.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED; SENTENCE VACATED AND REMANDED FOR RESENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish, Section L (Louisiana), which entered a conviction against him for possession of crack cocaine and which sentenced him to life imprisonment as a multiple offender.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of possession of crack cocaine and sentenced to two years' imprisonment. Thereafter, the State filed a multiple bill charging defendant as a fourth felony offender under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1 and he was sentenced to life imprisonment without the trial court having first vacated the previously imposed term. Defendant's motions to reconsider the sentence and to quash the multiple bill were denied, and on appeal, the court affirmed defendant's conviction. The trial court's denial of defendant's motion to suppress was proper because he was not seized when he was approached by police. When he dropped a bag with drugs in it, it was an abandonment thereof. Accordingly, suppression was not necessary. However, the court vacated his sentence, finding that there may have been extenuating circumstances which warranted a lesser sentence. Although § 15:529.1(A)(1)(c)(ii) mandated life imprisonment, the court found that the trial court still had discretion to make a downward modification thereof in the event that such sentencing was constitutionally excessive. The failure to have vacated the prior sentence did not affect defendant's substantial rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction, but vacated the sentence and remanded for resentencing.

Lanthier v. Family Dollar Store


2002-0429


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


2002-0429 (La.App. 3 Cir. 01/08/03); 848 So. 2d 605; 2003 La. App. LEXIS 5



January 8, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Costs and fees proceeding at Lanthier v. Family Dollar Store, 2006 La. App. LEXIS 2371 (La.App. 3 Cir., Nov. 2, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON REMAND FROM THE LOUISIANA SUPREME COURT OFFICE OF WORKERS' COMPENSATION, DISTRICT 02. PARISH OF RAPIDES, NO. 01-06757. ANTHONY PALERMO, WORKERS' COMPENSATION JUDGE.
Lanthier v. Family Dollar Store, 827 So. 2d 547, 2002 La. App. LEXIS 2986 (La.App. 3 Cir., Oct. 2, 2002)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant claimant filed an additional disputed claim against appellee employer. The workers' compensation judge granted a sua sponte exception of lack of subject matter jurisdiction. Claimant appealed. The Louisiana Supreme Court Office of Workers' Compensation, District 02, Parish of Rapides, vacated the decision of the instant court, holding that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1208 was unconstitutional, and remanded the matter to the instant court.


OVERVIEW: In the instant appeal, the claimant alleged the hearing officer erred in finding that the Louisiana Office of Workers' Compensation had no jurisdiction to hear a claim under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1208. The claimant asserted that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1208(D) was applicable to the facts, as to alleged false statements by the employer, and that the workers' compensation judge was the proper authority to assess a penalty under § 23:1208(D). The appellate court held the identification of the workers' compensation judge as the appropriate authority to impose the penalties under § 23:1208(D) was the type of legislative intent required by La. Const. art. V, § 16. Section 16 described the district court's jurisdiction being that other than those provided by law for administrative agency determinations in workers' compensation matters. Insofar as La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1208(D) was concerned, subject matter jurisdiction was specifically assigned to the Louisiana Office of Workers' Compensation. Thus, the workers' compensation judge's erred in granting the exception of subject matter jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The decision of the workers' compensation judge, granting the exception of subject matter jurisdiction, was reversed, and the matter was remanded for consideration under the applicable statute.

Kenny v. Kenneth Hoschar & Colonial Lloyds Ins. Co.


No. 2002-CA-1169


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2002-CA-1169 (La.App. 4 Cir. 01/08/03); 2003 La. App. LEXIS 7



January 8, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Released for Publication February 27, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 89-23895, DIVISION "A-5". HONORABLE CAROLYN GILL-JEFFERSON, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff injured motorist brought an action against defendants, a tortfeasor, his insurer, and the motorist's uninsured/underinsured carrier, for damages relating to a car accident. After the insurer was declared insolvent, the motorist sought insurance benefits from defendant Louisiana Insurance Guaranty Association (LIGA). The Civil District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), dismissed the motorist's claims against LIGA. The motorist appealed.


OVERVIEW: The motorist's vehicle was hit in the rear by the tortfeasor. The motorist settled with her carrier for an amount less than the policy limits. The parties stipulated that the motorist's damages did not exceed those policy limits, and they further stipulated the amount to which the motorist was entitled in the event she was rendered a judgment against LIGA. The trial court ruled in favor of LIGA and found that it was constitutionally permissible to apply La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22:1386 (amended 1992) to the case at hand. On appeal, the motorist challenged the constitutionality of the statute's retroactive application. The court affirmed the ruling. The court noted that a previous opinion held that the statute could be constitutionally retroactively applied. In light of that case, the court made the same conclusion. Thus, the statute was applicable in this case. The motorist was only entitled to recover from LIGA to the extent that her damages exceeded the policy limits of other insurance. Because the motorist failed to exhaust her rights under the limits of her policy with her carrier, the trial court properly found in LIGA's favor.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision.

Sandi's II v. Assumption Parish Police Jury


No. 2001 CA 2819


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2001 2819 (La.App. 1 Cir. 12/31/02); 837 So. 2d 124; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 4022



December 31, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Twenty-Third Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of Assumption, State of Louisiana. Trial Court No. 25,070. Honorable Guy Holdridge, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After denial of plaintiff lounge's application for a liquor license, the lounge filed an action seeking a writ of mandamus against defendant police jury. After a trial, the Twenty-Third Judicial District Court, Parish of Assumption (Louisiana), granted the police jury's exception of prescription and motion for partial summary judgment, and dismissed all of the lounge's claims. The lounge appealed.


OVERVIEW: The police jury met on January 13, 1999, and it amended its existing liquor ordinance to prohibit a barroom within 500 feet of a church. On January 27, 1999, the police jury denied the lounge's application for a liquor license. The lounge's owners were present at the January 27, 1999, meeting. The lounge filed suit on March 29, 1999, contending that the police jury violated provisions of the Open Meetings Law, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 42:4.1 et seq., and that the amended ordinance was unconstitutional. The appellate court found that: (1) the lounge's challenge of the police jury's finding that they could not issue a liquor license under the amended ordinance was untimely, as the lounge owner's were present at the meeting, they had notice on January 27, 1999, that the license was denied, and they failed to file the lounge's action within 10 days after the denial under the provisions of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 26:106; and (2) the lounge lost the right to attack the amended ordinance on the ground that it violated the Open Meetings Law, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 42:4.1 et seq., by failing to file suit within 60 days of January 13, 1999, as required by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 42.9.


OUTCOME: The district court's judgment was affirmed.
