State v. Lott


No. 2002-KA-702


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


2002-702 (La.App. 5 Cir. 12/30/02); 836 So. 2d 584; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 4059



December 30, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 18, 2003.
Writ denied by State ex rel. Lott v. State, 852 So. 2d 1030, 2003 La. LEXIS 2364 (La., Sept. 5, 2003)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Lott v. State, 855 So. 2d 300, 2003 La. LEXIS 2755 (La., Oct. 3, 2003)
Writ denied by State v. Lott, 855 So. 2d 755, 2003 La. LEXIS 3021 (La., Oct. 17, 2003)
Post-conviction relief denied at State ex rel. Lott v. State, 952 So. 2d 693, 2007 La. LEXIS 666 (La., Mar. 16, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE 24TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 97-0229, DIVISION "I" FROM "S". HONORABLE WALTER E. KOLLIN, M. JOSEPH TIEMANN, AND JO ELLEN GRANT, JUDGES PRESIDING.
State v. Lott, 796 So. 2d 941, 2001 La. App. LEXIS 1528 (La.App. 5 Cir., May 30, 2001)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of two counts of distribution of cocaine, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967A. He was subsequently found to have been a third felony offender and was sentenced under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1 to 25 years. The 24th Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, Division "I" from "S" (Louisiana), denied defendant's appeal. Defendant appealed and claimed his enhanced sentence was unconstitutionally excessive.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued his 25-year enhanced sentence was excessive, because, in the 5 years that he was in prison prior to his resentencing, he rehabilitated himself through the various courses offered in prison. He pointed to several substance abuse, life-saving, and religious courses he completed while in prison. He also noted that he was currently enrolled in a GED program. Defendant was a third felony offender. His prior convictions included possession of cocaine and possession of stolen property. In his most recent conviction, defendant's level of crime progressed to distribution of cocaine. The appellate court found that an adequate factual basis for the trial court's imposition of a 25-year sentence existed. Defendant argued 25 years was excessive in light of his non-violent record. However, a defendant's record of non-violent offenses was not the sole reason or even the major reason for declaring a sentence excessive. Violent offenses had already been taken into account under the Habitual Offender Law for third and fourth offenders, which punished third and fourth offenders with a history of violent offenses more severely than those with a history of non-violent offenses.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

1512 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Fortino


No. 2002-KA-708


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


2002-708 (La.App. 5 Cir. 12/30/02); 837 So. 2d 684; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 4142



December 30, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 18, 2003.
Writ denied by State v. Fortino, 843 So. 2d 395, 2003 La. LEXIS 1546 (La., May 9, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 01-4444, DIVISION "G". HONORABLE ROBERT A. PITRE, JUDGE PRESIDING.
State v. Fortino, 807 So. 2d 827, 2002 La. LEXIS 442 (La., Jan. 28, 2002)



DISPOSITION: Conviction and sentence affirmed. Case remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with second degree battery on his estranged wife, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:34.1. He pled not guilty. A six-person jury in the 24th Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, Division "G" (Louisiana), found defendant guilty as charged, and he was sentenced to four years imprisonment at hard labor. Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence and asserted, inter alia, that the evidence was insufficient.


OVERVIEW: Defendant also asserted that the trial judge erred in admitting Prieur evidence and that the sentence was excessive. Defendant contended that the state failed to prove that his estranged wife's injuries were sufficient to constitute "serious bodily injury," as intended by the second-degree battery statute. However, inter alia, defendant choked her, shoved her across the bed, and kicked her. She could not breathe and thought she was going to die. As defendant continued to choke her, she felt her neck "crackle," she "blacked out," and she was in jeopardy of losing her life. When defendant finally released her, she still had difficulty breathing. He then beat her about the head and face. Defendant's actions left marks on her neck that were observed by a deputy the following day. Those injuries were sufficiently serious to have risen to the level of second degree battery. The trial judge had not abused his discretion in admitting the evidence of other crimes. The record supported the sentence imposed. Defendant was a chronic abuser who did not think his actions were aberrant. He testified that he attended an anger management class, but only after being ordered by a judge to do so.


OUTCOME: The conviction and sentence were affirmed, and the case was remanded so that the trial judge could, within 10 days of the rendering of the appellate opinion, send written notice of the prescriptive period for post-conviction relief to defendant, and then to file written proof in the record that defendant received the notice.

 

1513 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Ruffin


No. 2002-KA-798


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


2002-798 (La.App. 5 Cir. 12/30/02); 836 So. 2d 625; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 4144



December 30, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 18, 2003.
Post-conviction relief denied at State ex rel. Ruffin v. State, 888 So. 2d 831, 2004 La. LEXIS 3740 (La., Dec. 10, 2004)
Post-conviction relief denied at State ex rel. Ruffin v. State, 949 So. 2d 410, 2007 La. LEXIS 456 (La., Feb. 16, 2007)
Post-conviction relief denied at State ex rel. Ruffin v. State, 992 So. 2d 981, 2008 La. LEXIS 1906 (La., 2008)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Transferred by State ex rel. Ruffin v. State, 994 So. 2d 5, 2008 La. LEXIS 2241 (La., 2008)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Ruffin v. State, 90 So. 3d 454, 2012 La. LEXIS 1864 (La., 2012)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Ruffin v. Cain, 2013 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 140941 (E.D. La., July 26, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 00-5965, DIVISION "C". HONORABLE ALAN J. GREEN, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded..


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence for distribution of cocaine within 1000 feet of an elementary school, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:981.3. The 24th Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, Division "C" (Louisiana), found him to be a second felony offender. The court vacated the original sentence and sentenced defendant under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1 to imprisonment at hard labor for 60 years.


OVERVIEW: Defendant raised issues on appeal, inter alia, regarding sufficiency of the evidence, erroneous admission of evidence, and his sentence. He argued that his counsel was ineffective for failing to timely file a motion for post verdict judgment of acquittal, where the evidence was insufficient to support a conviction. He argued that the state failed to prove he knowingly or intentionally distributed cocaine. The state produced the testimony of a police officer, which proved that defendant voluntarily delivered or physically transferred the cocaine when he handed the drugs to an undercover officer. Guilty knowledge of the cocaine at the time of transfer was shown when defendant handed two crack cocaine rocks to the officer. The exact identity of the cocaine had been stipulated to. The drug transaction was videotaped and played for the judge. The undercover officer identified defendant in a photographic lineup and testified that the transaction occurred one block away from the school. The appellate court held that the state proved beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant knowingly or intentionally distributed cocaine within 1000 feet of a school.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed, and the case was remanded for a ruling on the motion to reconsider the sentence, for the trial court to send the appropriate written notice to defendant regarding the prescriptive period for post-conviction relief, and to file written proof in the record that he received the notice.

 

1514 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Jordan


No. 2002-KA-820


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


2002-820 (La.App. 5 Cir. 12/30/02); 836 So. 2d 609; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 4167



December 30, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 18, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE 24TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 00-6586, DIVISION "M". HONORABLE HENRY G. SULLIVAN, JR., JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted before the 24th Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, Louisiana, on a charge of distribution of cocaine within 1000 feet of the playground, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:981.3. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: A narcotics agent was driving an unmarked patrol car near a playground. A woman came to the car, and the agent asked the woman if she could purchase some drugs. The woman told the officer to drive around the block, but, before the officer could, defendant asked the officer what she wanted. Defendant gave the woman cocaine, which she handed to the officer in exchange for money. The transaction took place approximately 250 feet from the playground. On appeal, defendant contended that the trial judge improperly denied his motion to quash and motion for new trial because the State failed to establish that the playground was school property as defined by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:981.3(C)(2). Nevertheless, defendant never raised this issue before the trial court. The appellate court found that defendant's chief complaint was that the evidence was insufficient. At trial, the officer described the drug-free zone sign, and this testimony was uncontested. Finally, in its patent error review, the appellate court determined that it would not correct the illegally lenient sentence.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1515 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Dupre v. Dupre


2002-0902


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


2002-0902 (La.App. 3 Cir. 12/30/02); 834 So. 2d 1272; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 4196



December 30, 2002, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE FIFTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT PARISH OF LAFAYETTE, NUMBER 20006328. HONORABLE RONALD D. COX.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant father appealed a judgment from the Fifteenth Judicial District, Parish of Lafayette (Louisiana), which changed the visitation schedule between the father and plaintiff mother regarding their child and the mother's daughter from a previous marriage from "seven and seven" physical sharing to every other weekend. The father claimed error in awarding visitation rights for the daughter to her biological paternal grandmother and her husband.


OVERVIEW: The court found no manifest error in modifying the physical custody schedule from a "seven and seven" schedule to every other weekend visitations. The "seven and seven" physical custody schedule was not intended to be a permanent custody arrangement and due to continuances, the plan was in effect much longer than originally intended. Previously the physical custody schedule in effect was a more traditional every other weekend arrangement with additional visitation in the middle of the week. The language of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:344(B) showed a clear preference by the legislature to ensure a child's contact with biological family members, regardless of the marital status of the child's parents. Therefore, the father's contention that the daughter was not a child of the marriage between the mother and her first husband was without merit, and La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:344 was the applicable statute. In light of the grandmother's past contact with the granddaughter, as well as her substantial economic support for the past several years, there was no error in the determination that it was in the granddaughter's best interest to ensure her continued contact with the grandmother.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1516 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Kenny v. Hoschar


No. 2002-CA-1169


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2002-CA-1169 (La.App. 4 Cir. 12/30/02); 837 So. 2d 113; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 4240



December 30, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 89-23895, DIVISION "A-5". HONORABLE CAROLYN GILL-JEFFERSON, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff injured motorist brought an action against defendants, a tortfeasor, his insurer, and the motorist's uninsured/underinsured carrier, for damages relating to a car accident. After the insurer was declared insolvent, the motorist sought insurance benefits from defendant Louisiana Insurance Guaranty Association (LIGA). The Civil District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), dismissed the motorist's claims against LIGA. The motorist appealed.


OVERVIEW: The motorist's vehicle was hit in the rear by the tortfeasor. The motorist settled with her carrier for an amount less than the policy limits. The parties stipulated that the motorist's damages did not exceed those policy limits, and they further stipulated the amount to which the motorist was entitled in the event she was rendered a judgment against LIGA. The trial court ruled in favor of LIGA and found that it was constitutionally permissible to apply La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22:1386 (amended 1992) to the case at hand. On appeal, the motorist challenged the constitutionality of the statute's retroactive application. The court affirmed the ruling. The court noted that a previous opinion held that the statute could be constitutionally retroactively applied. In light of that case, the court made the same conclusion. Thus, the statute was applicable in this case. The motorist was only entitled to recover from LIGA to the extent that her damages exceeded the policy limits of other insurance. Because the motorist failed to exhaust her rights under the limits of her policy with her carrier, the trial court properly found in LIGA's favor.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision.

 

1517 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Kirsch


No. 2002 KA 0993


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2002 0993 (La. App. 1 Cir. 12/20/02); 836 So. 2d 390; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 3992



December 20, 2002, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. Kirsch, 2003 La. LEXIS 2388 (La., Sept. 5, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the 22nd Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of St. Tammany, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 312,236. The Honorable Reginald T. Badeaux, III.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged by bill of information with indecent behavior with juveniles, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:81. He pled not guilty and was found guilty as charged. The 22nd Judicial District Court, Parish of St. Tammany (Louisiana), imposed a sentence of seven years imprisonment at hard labor, but suspended three years of the sentence. Defendant's motion to reconsider his sentence was denied, and he appealed.


OVERVIEW: In his first assignment of error, defendant argued that the trial court erred in denying him the right to present evidence of the victim's accusation and subsequent denial of prior sexual activity with her biological brother. Defendant further submitted that the trial court's failure to allow him to present such evidence was not harmless error. Defendant attempted to present evidence to show that the victim made prior false statements concerning sexual activity between herself and her biological brother. The appellate court held that two requirements had to be satisfied before evidence of prior sexual activity could be admitted for impeachment purposes, assuming the evidence was otherwise admissible. First, the activity had to have been of a sexual nature. Second, there had to have been evidence the statement was false. The appellate court found that the trial court properly applied State v. Smith and did not err in ruling the evidence concerning sexual behavior between the victim and her brother inadmissible. Furthermore, the trial court did not err in ruling that there was insufficient admissible evidence that the victim made false allegations regarding sexual activities.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

1518 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Avants v. Kennedy


NUMBER 2002 CA 0830


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2002 0830 (La.App. 1 Cir. 12/20/02); 837 So. 2d 647; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 3993



December 20, 2002, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of error denied Avants v. Kennedy, 840 So. 2d 1215, 2003 La. LEXIS 993 (La., Apr. 4, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana. Docket Number 434,575, Division "D". Honorable Janice Clark, Judge Presiding.
Avants v. Kennedy, 752 So. 2d 150, 2000 La. LEXIS 501 (La., Feb. 2, 2000)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant department of revenue challenged the award by the 19th Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), of attorney fees to appellee attorneys who represented plaintiffs. The award was based upon the "fund doctrine" or "common fund doctrine." The attorneys in turn requested 35 percent of the common fund, rather than the 28 percent award ordered by the trial court.


OVERVIEW: The attorneys' claim for an attorney fee award was properly raised and properly considered by the trial court. The assignment of error lacked merit. The appellate court held that the fund doctrine was applicable under the facts and circumstances of the case at bar. The efforts of the attorneys clearly resulted in the creation, preservation, protection, and increase in the settlement fund for the benefit of all taxpayer beneficiaries. But for the actions of the attorneys, no fund would have been created for the non-party beneficiaries to receive a refund of state sales taxes paid on manufactured and mobile home purchases. Accordingly, the appellate court found no error by the trial court in its conclusion that the fund doctrine was applicable and entitled the attorneys to a fee from the fund. Given the vast amount of work performed by the attorneys over the course of six years as well as the skill, ingenuity, and diligence resulting in the creation, preservation, and increase of the fund, the appellate court was unable to say the trial court abused its discretion in awarding a fee of 28 percent of the Settlement Fund. The appellate court, however, declined to change that award.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed. Costs of the appeal were assessed against the state through the department.

 

1519 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


St. Mary Anesthesia Assocs. v. Hosp. Serv. Dist. No. 2


No. 2001 CA 2852


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2001 2852 (La.App. 1 Cir. 12/20/02); 836 So. 2d 379; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 3995



December 20, 2002, Judgement Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by St. Mary Anesthesia Assocs. v. Hosp. Servs. Dist. No. 2, 840 So. 2d 577, 2003 La. LEXIS 917 (La., Mar. 28, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the 16th Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of St. Mary, Louisiana. Civil Docket No. 107,891. The Honorable William D. Hunter, Judge Presiding.
Joseph v. Hosp. Serv. Dist. No. 2, 805 So. 2d 400, 2001 La. App. LEXIS 3151 (La.App. 1 Cir., Dec. 28, 2001)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff complainant challenged a declaratory judgment from the 16th Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of St. Mary, Louisiana, which upheld the constitutionality of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 46:1071, 46:1072, and 46:1073, dismissing the complainant's challenge to the statutes as being overly broad and therefore violative of La. Const. art. XII, § 3.


OVERVIEW: The complainant and others sued defendant hospital and its chief executive officer for alleged violations of the Open Meetings Law, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 42:4.1 et seq., and other claims. They argued the hospital had used the Enhanced Ability to Compete Act to improperly conduct closed executive sessions. Reversing the trial court's judgment, the court held that the hospital had not violated the Open Meetings Law. The complainant then instituted an action seeking a declaration that the core provisions of the Enhanced Ability to Compete Act violated La. Const. art. XII, § 3. The trial court held that the Act was constitutional. On appeal, the court affirmed. The right to observe the deliberations of public bodies and examine public documents was not an inalienable individual right. The Legislature could exempt from disclosure any information it wished. The Act was a permissible exercise of legislative power. Because the right was not a fundamental, inalienable constitutional right, the substantial overbreadth doctrine was not applicable. The complainant failed to rebut the strong presumption in favor of the Act's constitutionality. The Act did not violate the complainant's rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the constitutionality of the statutes that exempted the hospital's closed executive sessions from the Open Meetings Law.

 

1520 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Robertson v. Caddo Parish


No. 36,540-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


36,540-CA (La.App. 2 Cir. 833 So. 2d 1139; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 3839



December 11, 2002, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by Robertson v. Caddo Parish, 2004 La. LEXIS 1365 (La., Apr. 23, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 444,263. Honorable Frank H. Thaxton, III, Judge.
Robertson v. Ieyoub, 799 So. 2d 863, 2001 La. App. LEXIS 2696 (La.App. 2 Cir., Nov. 16, 2001)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant citizen filed a declaratory judgment action in the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana, arguing the former La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 413(B) was unconstitutional. The trial court granted appellee parish's exceptions of no cause and no right of action. The citizen appealed.


OVERVIEW: The citizen had previously been convicted for aggravated rape and burglary. He filed his declaratory action, arguing under the former version of La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 413(B) in effect at the time of his conviction called for the trial court to select one person from the grand jury venire to serve as the foreman of the grand jury. The citizen contended the statute was unconstitutional due to the alleged racially discriminatory method of selecting grand jury foremen. The appellate court initially noted although couched in terms of a prayer for declaratory relief, the citizen's request was nothing more than an effort to obtain a reversal of his conviction based upon the alleged illegality of the previous La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 413(B). The appellate court admonished declaratory judgment was unavailable to test the constitutionality of a repealed criminal statute and a resulting conviction. The appellate court held the citizen waived his right to complain because he failed to assert an equal protection claim regarding the composition of grand juries in a pre-trial motion to quash at his trial.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

1521 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Paddio


2002-722


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


2002-0722 (La.App. 3 Cir. 12/11/02);  832 So. 2d 1120; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 3737



December 11, 2002, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 11, 2002.
Writ denied by State ex rel. Paddio v. State, 2004 La. LEXIS 531 (La., Feb. 13, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE FIFTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF LAFAYETTE, NUMBER 85011, HONORABLE MARILYN CARR CASTLE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Fifteenth Judicial District Court, Paris of Lafayette (Louisiana), after she was tried by a jury and found guilty of second degree murder; a sentence of life imprisonment at hard labor was imposed, without the benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence; and her motion to reconsider sentence was denied.


OVERVIEW: Upon arrival to investigate a domestic disturbance, police found the victim lying dead on the bedroom floor, with a substantial amount of blood on his shoulder and a large knife lying nearby. Defendant admitted that she stabbed the victim, and gave a videotaped statement, during which she conflicting accounts of the events leading up to the crime. The appellate court held that: (1) the State submitted sufficient evidence to prove that defendant did not act in self-defense, as the murder scene did not show any signs of a violent physical confrontation, defendant had physically the victim on several prior occasions, and it was unnecessary to kill the victim under any of the scenarios offered by defendant; (2) based on the evidence, the jury did not err in rejecting defendant's claim that she acted in the heat of passion; (3) prosecution of defendant, following a mistrial, did not violate double jeopardy, because prosecutorial error was unintentional and defendant suffered no prejudice; and (4) the record contained no evidence which the trial court could have reviewed to determine that the mandatory life sentence was constitutionally excessive.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1522 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Expunged Record No. 249,044


2002-589


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


2002-589 (La.App. 3 Cir. 12/11/02); 833 So. 2d 553; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 3740



December 11, 2002, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 11, 2002.
Appeal after remand at State v. Expunged Record 249,044, 2004 La. LEXIS 2103 (La., July 2, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE NINTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF RAPIDES, NO. 249,044, HONORABLE GEORGE C. METOYER, JR., DISTRICT JUDGE.
State v. Expunged Record No. 249,044, 826 So. 2d 661, 2002 La. App. LEXIS 2341 (La.App. 3 Cir., July 10, 2002)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Movant had been arrested for obstruction of justice and false personation of a peace officer. He filed a motion in the Ninth Judicial District Court, Rapides Parish (Louisiana), in which he prayed that his felony arrest records be expunged and destroyed. The State did not oppose the request for expungement but opposed the destruction request. The trial court ultimately ordered the expungement and destruction of the records. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court first noted that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 44:9 provided for the expungement of felony arrest records in particularized instances, but it did not provide for the destruction of felony arrest records. The appellate court then quoted La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 44:9(G) in finding that expungement meant removal of a record from public access but did not mean destruction of the record. The appellate court held that the trial court's grant of movant's request for destruction of his felony arrest records was a misapplication of the law. Movant alternatively sought a judgment declaring that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 44:9's provision for the destruction of misdemeanor arrest records, but not felony arrest records, was unconstitutional. In his rule to modify judgment on rule or, alternatively, petition for declaratory judgment, he requested service on the Louisiana Attorney General, but there was no evidence in the record that service was made. Without proof of notice of service on the attorney general, the issue of the constitutionality of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 44:9 was not properly before the appellate court.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court ordering the destruction of movant's felony arrest records was reversed. The issue of service on the Louisiana Attorney General regarding movant's challenge to the constitutionality of the expungement statute was remanded to the trial court.

 

1523 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Cedars


KA2002-861


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


2002-0861 (La.App. 3 Cir. 12/11/02);  832 So. 2d 1191; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 3755



December 11, 2002, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 11, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF NATCHITOCHES, NUMBER C 2699, DIV. A HONORABLE ERIC R. HARRINGTON, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Convictions affirmed; sentences affirmed in part, vacated and remanded in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Tenth Judicial District Court, Parish of Natchitoches (Louisiana), which convicted him of vehicular homicide, pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:32.1 and sentenced him to 15 years at hard labor, and convicted him of vehicular negligent injuring, pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:39.1 and sentenced him to 6 months in the detention center.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted and sentenced for vehicular homicide and vehicular negligent injuring. He appealed, and the court affirmed both of his convictions, but vacated his sentence for vehicular homicide, finding that it was indeterminate. The trial court imposed an indeterminate sentence when it ordered that "at least" five years of defendant's sentence for vehicular homicide be served without benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence. The sentencing provision for vehicular homicide required that at least one year of the sentence be served without probation, parole, or suspension of sentence. Thus, the trial court could order all or a portion, but at least one year, of the sentence to be served without benefits, but it must have specified the term. Further, in addition to being indeterminate, the sentence for vehicular homicide was illegally lenient. The failure to access defendant with a fine and order him into a court-approved program provided additional grounds for vacating the sentence. Defendant's ineffective assistance of counsel argument failed, because it should be relegated to post-conviction relief.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and his sentence for vehicular negligent injuring. The court vacated his sentence for vehicular homicide and remanded for resentencing.

 

1524 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Ashmore v. Hilton


2002-816


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


2002-0816 (La.App. 3 Cir. 12/11/02); 834 So. 2d 1131; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 3789



December 11, 2002, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Ashmore v. Hilton, 2003 La. App. LEXIS 355 (La.App. 3 Cir., Feb. 12, 2003)
Rehearing denied by Ashmore v. Hilton, 2003 La. App. LEXIS 356 (La.App. 3 Cir., Feb. 12, 2003)
Writ of error denied Ashmore v. Hilton, 2003 La. LEXIS 1564 (La., May 9, 2003)
Writ of error denied Ashmore v. Hilton, 2003 La. LEXIS 1566 (La., May 9, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE NINTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF RAPIDES, NUMBER 189,486. HONORABLE HARRY FRED RANDOW.



DISPOSITION: MODIFIED IN PART; AFFIRMED IN PART; AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Ninth Judicial District Court, Parish of Rapides (Louisiana), found defendant city liable to plaintiff injured party, who alleged that she was raped by a trustee, a prison inmate, while working for the city doing community service work. The city appealed. The injured party answered the city's appeal seeking an increase in the award of damages and claiming that the trial court erred in dismissing her 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claim.


OVERVIEW: The injured party was sentenced to perform community service. While performing community service, the injured party was raped by a trustee who was incarcerated at a parish detention center. The city and the parish detention center had entered into an agreement for the use of inmates outside of the detention facility. In the agreement, the city agreed to supervise a trustee when a trustee was working for the city. The trial court found that the injured party was raped and that the city was responsible for her resulting injuries and awarded her special and general damages. The appellate court found that had the city simply never allowed the trustee and the injured party to be alone together, the rape would never have occurred. Therefore, the city was 70 percent at fault and the trustee was 30 percent at fault. Also, the city's actions were grossly negligent. Thus, the city was responsible for any general damages in addition to medical expenses. Additionally, the trial court's award of damages was appropriate. However, the injured party failed to prove a claim for damages under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and her claim was properly dismissed.


OUTCOME: The appellate court modified the trial court's judgment insofar as it failed to allocate fault to the trustee who raped the injured party and reduced fault as to the city based on the allocation of fault to the trustee. In all other respects, the judgment of the trial court was affirmed. Costs of the appeal were assessed to the city.

 

1525 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Peterson v. Austin


No. 36,365-CA (Consolidated Cases) No. 36,582-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


36,365 (La.App. 2 Cir. 12/11/02); 836 So. 2d 235; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 3794



December 11, 2002, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Amended February 25, 2003.
Writ of certiorari denied Peterson v. Austin, 2004 La. LEXIS 291 (La., Jan. 30, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Second Judicial District Court for the Parish of Claiborne, Louisiana Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 35,148, Trial Court No. 463628. Honorable Jenifer Ward Clason, Judge, Honorable Frank H. Thaxton, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate filed two separate actions against prison employees and the department of corrections for injuries he received from conditions of discipline or confinement. The Second Judicial District Court for the Parish of Claiborne (Louisiana) and the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo (Louisiana) dismissed the inmate's suits on the basis of prematurity and lack of subject matter jurisdiction. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate alleged that a corrections officer retaliated against him because of administrative grievances that he filed against the officer. In a separate action, the inmate alleged that a prison nurse improperly denied his request to be seen by a mental health professional and retaliated against him for complaining by accusing him of malingering. The matters were consolidated on appeal. The appellate court found that: (1) the inmate's "tort" claims arose directly from the disciplinary and administrative remedy proceedings of the department of corrections and not from an independent accident; (2) the corrections administrative remedy procedure was not unconstitutional when applied to injuries from prison confinement; (3) LA. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:1177(A) required the inmate to seek judicial review of any adverse administrative remedy decision in the nineteenth judicial district court within 30 days of receipt of the adverse decision; and (4) both of the district courts properly sustained the exceptions of prematurity and lack of subject matter jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The district courts' judgments were affirmed.

 

1526 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Sanders


No. 2002-KA-568


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


2002-568 (La.App. 5 Cir. 12/11/02); 836 So. 2d 263; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 3867



December 11, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 18, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 99-1270, DIVISION "A". HONORABLE JOAN S. BENGE, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Twenty Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, Division A, Louisiana, convicting her of unauthorized use of an access device with the intent to defraud, former La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:70.4, and sentencing her, pursuant to a multiple offender adjudication, to a term of five years.


OVERVIEW: The trial court advised defendant that her two-year sentence pursuant to her guilty plea would be vacated and a five-year sentence would be imposed, if a multiple bill was filed and she agreed to the allegations of the multiple bill. Defendant admitted the allegations, the two year sentence was vacated, and the five year sentence was imposed. Defendant argued that her guilty plea should have been set aside, because she was erroneously advised that she was pleading guilty to a felony, and she was later advised that an amendment to the statute under which she was charged made the offense a misdemeanor. The appellate court ruled that defendant's contention that her conviction and multiple offender adjudication and sentence should be set aside because they resulted from involuntary guilty plea was unfounded. Defendant admitted culpability to access device fraud in exchange for a two-year sentence. The sentence was legal within the language of former La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:70.4 (E), as that statute existed at the time of defendant's offense. Also, as defendant's charged offense was a felony at the time of its commission, the multiple bill adjudication was also legal.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1527 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Everidge


No. 2002-KA-0309


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2002-0309 (La.App. 4 Cir. 12/11/02); 834 So. 2d 1197; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 3914



December 11, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 7, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT. ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 417-740, SECTION "L". Honorable Terry Alarcon, Judge.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTIONS AFFIRMED; SENTENCE VACATED; REMANDED FOR RESENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish, Section "L" (Louisiana), after he was convicted, following a mistrial, of possession of cocaine in an amount 28 grams or more, but less than 200 grams, and was adjudicated a second-felony habitual offender and sentenced to 30 years at hard labor.


OVERVIEW: Two police officers arrested defendant after they saw him engage in a hand-to-hand transaction with another individual near a store. On appeal, defendant argued that the evidence was insufficient to support the conviction, and that his sentence was constitutionally excessive. The appellate court held that any rational trier of fact could have found beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant was a seller of crack cocaine, as defendant offered no evidence that the substance was not cocaine to rebut the State's evidence, and the record contained evidence that two police officers observed defendant engage in a hand-to-hand transaction and one officer observed the individual hand defendant currency and defendant hand a white object to the individual. However, the trial court erred regarding sentencing insofar as it believed that it was barred by law from considering the dramatic reductions in sentences for drug offenses effected by 2001 La. Acts 403, § 4, as a palliative factor when assessing the reasonableness of defendant's sentence under the Dorthey standard. To the contrary, the legislature's subsequent changes in criminal statutes were relevant sentencing considerations.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed defendant's conviction and adjudication as a second-felony habitual offender, vacated his sentence, and remanded the case for resentencing in accordance with the views expressed in the opinion.

Anthony Crane Rental, L.P. v. Fruge


2002-0635


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


2002-0635 (La.App. 3 Cir. 12/11/02); 833 So. 2d 1070; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 3783



December 11, 2002, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 11, 2002.
Review granted by Anthony Crane Rental, L.P. v. Fruge, 842 So. 2d 1082, 2003 La. LEXIS 741 (La., Mar. 28, 2003)
Reversed by, Remanded by Anthony Crane Rental, L.P. v. Fruge, 859 So. 2d 631, 2003 La. LEXIS 2870 (La., Oct. 21, 2003)
Writ denied by Anthony Crane Rental, L.P. v. Fruge, 2004 La. LEXIS 180 (La., Jan. 16, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE FOURTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. PARISH OF CALCASIEU, NUMBER 2000-1828, Division "H" HONORABLE DAVID PAINTER.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART; AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a sales tax assessment case, the Fourteenth Judicial District, Parish of Calcasieu, Division "H" (Louisiana), denied plaintiff rental company's motion for summary judgment and granted the motion for summary judgment in favor of defendant, the Director of Calcasieu Parish Sales and Use Tax Department (Louisiana). The trial court subsequently reduced the penalty percentage owed by the rental company. Both parties appealed.


OVERVIEW: The rental company was audited by the Department and was assessed sales and use taxes for its leased cranes. The rental company protested the assessment, but it was denied. The rental company paid, under protest, the Department's final assessment, but filed a petition for refund to recover the amounts, essentially arguing that the cranes were excluded from taxation. The rental company appealed the trial court's denial of its motion for summary judgment and motion for new trial regarding the impropriety of the taxation. The Department appealed that portion of the motion for new trial which was granted by the trial court reducing the penalty percentage owed by the rental company. The appellate court held that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:301(10)(a)(iii) and (18)(a)(iii) were constitutional. Thus, the Department properly assessed the rental company with its local use tax. Also, the appellate court had to reverse the trial court's judgment regarding the imposition of attorney's fees since the amount awarded would cause the combined interest, penalty, and attorney's fees to exceed the 15 percent penalty permitted by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:2746.


OUTCOME: The summary judgment granted in favor of the Director finding that the rental company was subject to a sales and use tax and was not entitled to a credit was affirmed. The trial court's judgment was reversed regarding the amount of penalties. On remand, the combined interest, penalty, and attorney's fee award could not to exceed 15 percent.

State v. Lewis


No. 2002-KA-1924


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2002-1924 (La.App. 4 Cir. 11/26/02); 834 So. 2d 528; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 3705



November 26, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 30, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH NO. 416-829, SECTION "A" Honorable Charles L. Elloie, Judge.
State v. Lewis, 2002 La. App. LEXIS 2449 (La.App. 4 Cir., July 17, 2002)



DISPOSITION: VACATED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of three counts of armed robbery and sentenced to 30 years' imprisonment at hard labor as to each count. The convictions and sentences were affirmed. The State filed a multiple bill, charging him as a third felony offender and the Criminal District Court for Orleans Parish (Louisiana) resentenced him to 66 years at hard labor on count three under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1(A)(1)(b)(i) (2001). The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's third felony, armed robbery, was a crime of violence. His prior offenses were simple robbery, carrying a concealed weapon second offense, and first-degree robbery, which was a crime of violence. On the date that defendant was charged, former La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1(A)(1)(b) (2000) was in effect. The trial court deliberately sentenced the defendant to a lesser term under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1(A)(1)(b) (2001). The appellate court found that: (1) the trial court erred in sentencing defendant to the 66 year sentence rather than life imprisonment because the amendments to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1 (2001) became effective after defendant committed his most recent offense; (2) La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1, the habitual offender statute, was constitutional; and (3) imposition of a life sentence was not constitutionally excessive because nothing in the record or the facts suggested any mitigating circumstances.


OUTCOME: The sentenced imposed by the criminal district court was vacated and the matter was remanded for resentencing.

 

1530 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Hoag v. State


2001 CA 1076


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2001 1076 (La.App. 1 Cir. 11/20/02); 836 So. 2d 207; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 3649



November 20, 2002, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by Hoag v. State, 840 So. 2d 570, 2003 La. LEXIS 895 (La., Mar. 28, 2003)
Related proceeding at Hoag v. State, 872 So. 2d 1069, 2004 La. LEXIS 1587 (La., May 7, 2004)
Petition dismissed by Hoag v. State, 2004 La. LEXIS 3598 (La., Dec. 1, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 19th Judicial District Court. Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana. Docket No. 471,708. Honorable Jewel E. "Duke" Welch, Jr., Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a suit by plaintiffs, 35 coroners, against defendant, the State of Louisiana, seeking past due and future extra compensation allegedly owed them, the 19th Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), overruled the State's peremptory exception raising the objection of no cause of action, granted the coroners motion for summary judgment, and awarded each coroner the specific amount due him or her. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: Commencing with the 1986-1987 fiscal year, the legislative branch failed and/or refused to appropriate funds for the coroners' extra compensation. Further, the legislative branch failed, refused, and/or was unable to amend La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:1559 by which it created the State's obligation to pay the extra compensation to the coroners. La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:1559A and B imposed a mandatory obligation on the State to pay extra compensation to the coroners (1) until La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:1559 was repealed, (2) the money was paid, or (3) the terms for which the coroners were elected expire, whichever came later. Pursuant to La. Const. art. I, § 22 and the Louisiana Civil Code, substantive remedies available to the coroners were specific performance, La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 1986 et seq., or dissolution and damages, La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 2013 et seq. The coroners chose specific performance. The failure to pay the compensation owed to the coroners breached the contract between the State and the coroners. Thus, the trial court properly awarded the coroners the amounts due to them for past due compensation.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment. The State was cast for the costs of the appeal.

La. Electorate of Gays & Lesbians v. State


No. 2001-CA-1091


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2001-1091 (La.App. 4 Cir. 11/20/02); 833 So. 2d 1016; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 3689



November 20, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 17, 2003.
Related proceeding at La. Electorate of Gays & Lesbians, Inc. v. Connick, 2005 La. App. LEXIS 1065 (La.App. 5 Cir., Apr. 26, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 94-9260, DIVISION "A-5". Honorable Carolyn Gill-Jefferson, Judge.
812 So. 2d 626, 2002 La. LEXIS 726 (La., Mar. 28, 2002)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AS AMENDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The trial court declared La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:89(A)(1) and the remainder of the targeted statutes unconstitutional as they related to the prohibition of § 14:89(A)(1). Several times the case was appealed to the Louisiana Supreme Court and remanded to the trial court. Eventually, the supreme court vacated the trial court's judgments and transferred the appeal of the remaining constitutional issues to the appellate court.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, lesbian and gay civil organization and several lesbian and gay citizens, sued defendants, State of Louisiana, attorney general, and parish district attorney, the latter both individually and as the class representative of all of the Louisiana prosecutors. Plaintiffs sought a declaration that the Louisiana Crime Against Nature statute, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:89, and several statutes extending its effects, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 12:1041, 15:535, 15:536, 15:538, 15:540, 15:542, 15:542.1, 15:543, 15:544, 15:545, and 15:549 were unconstitutional. The appellate court held that the discriminatory purpose by the lawmaking body was not proven and no evidence was introduced that the entire legislative body enacted the statutes for the purpose of discriminating against gay men and lesbians. As such, the statutes were not unconstitutional on equal protection grounds. After considering the evidence and law, the appellate court found no error in the trial judge's ruling that there was insufficient evidence to hold that the targeted statutes provided for cruel, unusual, and excessive punishment. Also, the targeted statutes were not bills of attainder.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment as amended. The appellate court amended the original judgment to read that plaintiffs were dismissed with prejudice.

In re Medical Review Panel of Conerly


No. 02-CA-485


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


2002-485 (La.App. 5 Cir. 11/13/02); 833 So. 2d 384; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 3482



November 13, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 21, 2003.
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by In re Medical Review Panel of Conerly, 2003 La. App. LEXIS 3654 (La.App. 5 Cir., Dec. 30, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE 24TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 518-765, DIVISION "K". HONORABLE MARTHA E. SASSONE, JUDGE PRESIDING.
In re Med. Review Panel of Conerly, 793 So. 2d 574, 2001 La. App. LEXIS 901 (La.App. 5 Cir., Apr. 24, 2001)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED IN PART AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient challenged the judgment of the 24th Judicial District Court for the Parish of Jefferson, Division K, Louisiana, denying her motion to declare La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5628 unconstitutional, granting defendant hospital's exception of prescription, and denying the patient's motion for new trial, in the patient's action for medical malpractice involving two blood transfusions she received as an infant at the hospital.


OVERVIEW: Approximately 18 years after receiving the blood transfusions, the patient was diagnosed with the hepatitis C virus, and the patient was told by doctors that it was likely due to the blood transfused. The patient argued that an action in strict product liability arising out of a defective blood transfusion was not within the scope of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5628. The patient asserted that the action did not prescribe in three years from the date of the transfusion in cases where the harm from the transfusion was discovered beyond the three years. The appellate court ruled that the patient's claims of strict liability were not prescribed and the trial court was wrong in so ruling. All claims made against the hospital in strict product liability arising out of defective blood transfusions that arose before the blood shield statutes enacted in 1982 were governed by La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 3492 and not La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5628. However, the appellate court acknowledged that separate claims made by the patient on traditional medical malpractice grounds were prescribed.


OUTCOME: The judgment in so far as it granted the exception of prescription for strict liability claims was reversed, and the matter was remanded for further proceedings.

State v. Conner


02-KA-363


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


2002-363 (La.App. 5 Cir. 11/13/02); 833 So. 2d 396; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 3486



November 13, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 21, 2003.
Writ of error denied State v. Conner, 2003 La. LEXIS 1282 (La., Apr. 25, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE 24TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA, NUMBER 99-5804, DIVISION "P". HONORABLE MELVIN C. ZENO, PRESIDING.
State v. Conner, 771 So. 2d 641, 2000 La. LEXIS 2893 (La., Oct. 13, 2000)



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A bill of information was filed charging defendant with fifth-offense operating a vehicle while intoxicated (DWI), in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:98E. The 24th Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, Division "P" (Louisiana), found defendant guilty as charged. Defendant moved for a new trial, which the court denied. He was sentenced to 10 years at hard labor. Defendant filed a notice of intent to appeal, which was granted.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the State failed to prove his guilt beyond a reasonable doubt. Specifically, he asserted that the evidence was insufficient to show he was legally intoxicated and that the prosecution failed to prove he was the same person who was convicted of the prior DWI offenses. At trial, a police corporal testified that defendant was exceeding the speed limit, although he was not driving erratically, and that several factors, which were evident after he stopped defendant for speeding, led him to conclude that defendant was intoxicated. When defendant exited his car, he swayed and grabbed the side of the car to steady himself. When defendant walked toward the corporal after exiting his car he staggered. Defendant smelled strongly of alcohol, and his speech was slurred. The appellate court's review of the record supported the trial judge's determination that defendant was legally intoxicated and guilty beyond a reasonable doubt of operating a vehicle while intoxicated. And, when viewed in its entirety, the record supported the sentence imposed and that the entire term was to have been served without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence.


OUTCOME: The conviction and sentence were affirmed.

Wingfield v. State


NUMBER 2001 CA 2668 C/W NUMBER 2001 CA 2669


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2001 2668 (La.App. 1 Cir. 11/08/02); 835 So. 2d 785; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 3447



November 8, 2002, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Wingfield v. State, 2002 La. App. LEXIS 4040 (La.App. 1 Cir., Dec. 31, 2002)
Writ denied by Wingfield v. State, 845 So. 2d 1059, 2003 La. LEXIS 1772 (La., May 30, 2003)
Writ denied by Wingfield v. State, 845 So. 2d 1060, 2003 La. LEXIS 1773 (La., May 30, 2003)
Writ denied by Wingfield v. State, 845 So. 2d 1060, 2003 La. LEXIS 1774 (La., May 30, 2003)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Louisiana v. Wingfield, 157 L. Ed. 2d 282, 124 S. Ct. 419, 2003 U.S. LEXIS 7492 (U.S., 2003)
Remanded by Wingfield v. State, 2004 La. App. LEXIS 1255 (La.App. 1 Cir., May 14, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, State of Louisiana. Suit Number 418,074 c/w 418,842. Honorable Curtis A. Callaway and Honorable J. Michael McDonald, Judges Presiding.
Wingfield v. State ex rel. Department of Transp. & Dev., 716 So. 2d 164, 1998 La. App. LEXIS 2256 (La.App. 1 Cir., June 29, 1998)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED IN PART, AMENDED, AND AS AMENDED, AFFIRMED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: One truck driver was killed and his fellow driver was severely injured when their tractor trailer rolled over. Appellees, their wives, brought suit against appellant Department of Transportation and Development (DOTD). A jury in the 19th Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), awarded damages to the wives. Inter alia, the court granted the DOTD a judgment notwithstanding the verdict (JNOV). Both parties appealed.


OVERVIEW: One issue on appeal was whether the highway was an unreasonably dangerous one; defective by inadequate warnings and in design. The Federal Aid Highway Act (FAHA), 23 U.S.C.S. § 101 et seq., standards did not attempt to supersede the prohibition in state law against negligent acts of design, construction, or signage or imposition of strict liability. The appellate court saw no error in the trial court's denial of the summary judgment on the issue of preemption. Based on credibility determinations, the judge found that there was not sufficient evidence that the driver was impaired at the time of the accident. The court's conclusion served as the basis for the trial judge's grant of the motion to exclude the DOTD's experts' testimony regarding marijuana and grant of the partial summary judgment dismissing the affirmative defense of the driver's negligence in driving under the influence of marijuana. It was error for the judge to have based his ruling not on the evidentiary articles and law governing admissibility, but on his own credibility decisions and choice of expert opinions. However, the inclusion of the rejected evidence could not have permissibly changed the jury's verdict.


OUTCOME: The JNOV was reversed and the jury's award for the survival action was reinstated, the amount of damages awarded was amended, and as amended, the judgment was affirmed in part. The costs of the appeal were assessed as one-half to the wives and one-half to the DOTD.

Spooner v. E. Baton Rouge Parish Sheriff Dep't


No. 2001 CA 2663


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2001 2663 (La.App. 1 Cir. (11/08/02); 835 So. 2d 709; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 3460



November 8, 2002, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the 19th Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana. Civil Docket No. 477,617. The Honorable Timothy E. Kelley.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff prisoner filed suit against defendants, sheriff's department, deputy, and warden, for damages resulting from an alleged assault and battery committed by the deputy. The sheriff, deputy and warden filed an exception of failure to exhaust the administrative remedies, which was granted by the 19th Judicial District Court for the Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana). The prisoner's suit was dismissed and he appealed.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner asserted on appeal that the Corrections Administrative Remedy Procedure (CARP), La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 15:1171-1179, was unconstitutional as applied to tort suits, and thus the district court erred in dismissing his suit under an unconstitutional statute. The appellate court found that: (1) the prisoner was able to raise the unconstitutionality of the statute for the first time on appeal because the statute was declared unconstitutional in another case; (2) the sheriff's administrative procedure was not distinguishable from the department of corrections' administrative procedure; (3) the CARP administrative procedure was unconstitutional as applied to tort suits because it conflicted with La. Const. art. V, § 16(A), in that it attempted to divest the district courts of jurisdiction over prisoner's tort claims; and (4) it was error for the district court to dismiss the prisoner's tort suit for failure to follow the unconstitutional procedure set forth in CARP.


OUTCOME: The district court's judgment was reversed and remanded.

Allen v. Fireman's Fund Ins. Co.


No. 36,606-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


36,606 (La.App. 2 Cir. 11/06/02); 830 So. 2d 1120; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 3345



November 6, 2002, Judgment Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by Allen v. Fireman's Fund Ins. Co., 836 So. 2d 114, 2003 La. LEXIS 579 (La., Feb. 14, 2003)
Appeal after remand at Yarnell Ice Cream Co. v. Allen, 2004 La. App. LEXIS 425 (La.App. 2 Cir., Mar. 3, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 01-1771. Honorable J. N. Dimos, Judge.
Yarnell Ice Cream Co. v. Allen, 759 So. 2d 1066, 2000 La. App. LEXIS 1113 (La.App. 2 Cir., May 10, 2000)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Louisiana Office of Workers' Compensation (OWC) entered judgment against appellant employee, and in favor of appellee employer and the appellee insurer, and awarded damages. The employee filed another petition claiming the OWC had no jurisdiction to award money damages. The Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita, Louisiana, granted the employer's and the insurer's exceptions. The employee appealed.


OVERVIEW: The employee claimed to have injured his back on his first day of work for the employer, and obtained medical treatment paid for by workers' compensation. The employee reported no previous injuries, but it was discovered the employee had suffered a back injury in a department store. The current provisions of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1310.3(F) were not in effect at the time of the employee's initial claim for benefits or at the time he filed his petition in district court. Without regard to the retroactivity of these provisions, however, the employee did not attempt to litigate the constitutional issue in the proceedings that led to his first appeal. The gist of the argument in the appeal was that the OWC had no jurisdiction to award money damages except in awarding compensation benefits. The appellate court concluded, however, that the challenge to the OWC's jurisdiction and to the constitutionality of the statutes enabling the OWC to enter the awards, including his action challenging the subsequent award for damages for investigation and litigation, was barred by operation of La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 2005.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the district court was affirmed.

Sherman v. Touro Infirmary Hosp.


No. 2000-CA-1365 C/W No. 2000-CA-1366 C/W No. 2000-CA-2573 C/W No. 2000-CA-2574 C/W No. 2002-CA-1058 C/W No. 2002-CA-1059


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2000-1365 (La.App. 4 Cir. 10/30/02); 832 So. 2d 334; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 3349



October 30, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 3, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NOS. 91-14085 C/W 98-11028, DIVISION "N-8". Honorable Ethel Simms Julien, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant parents sued appellee doctors in the Civil District Court, Orleans Parish, Louisiana, alleging medical malpractice for the injuries their son received during his birthing procedure. The trial court granted the doctors' exception of prescription. The parents appealed.


OVERVIEW: In 1991, the parents sued the doctors and in 1996 filed a motion to prevent dismissal for abandonment of their action. The parents agreed to dismiss their lawsuit since they had not first filed the claim for a medical review panel. The parents then requested a medical review panel and filed a second lawsuit in 1998. The doctors pled the peremptory exception of prescription, which the trial court granted. The parents appealed, arguing the retroactive application of a holding that party who improperly filed a premature medical malpractice suit without first filing the claim with the board for a medical review panel, and whose suit was subsequently dismissed without prejudice, gained an additional year in prescription in addition to the suspended time provided by the Louisiana Medical Malpractice Act, within which to file suit anew violated their constitutionally protected interests. The appellate court held the parents failed to persuade it that the trial court's retroactive application of case law divested them of any constitutionally protected interest.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

1539 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. O'Neal


No. 36,431-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


36,431 (La.App. 2 Cir. 10/23/02); 830 So. 2d 408; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 3204



October 23, 2002, Judgment Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 198,597. Honorable Ramona L. Emanuel, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of vehicular homicide. The appellate court affirmed the conviction and defendant's adjudication as a third felony offender, but remanded for resentencing. The First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo (Louisiana) again imposed the mandatory sentence of life imprisonment. Defendant filed a motion to reconsider sentence, which was denied. Defendant appealed from the sentence imposed.


OVERVIEW: While defendant was intoxicated and had marijuana in his system, he drove a vehicle hitting two pedestrians who were attempting to cross the street. One of the victims died. Defendant had two prior non-violent felony convictions. At the resentencing hearing defendant presented testimony that he had shown remorse, helped his family, and made an effort to rehabilitate himself. The appellate court found that: (1) the amendment to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1 was to be applied prospectively, (2) defendant failed to show that the sentence imposed was excessive or that the sentence was not tailored to the defendant's culpability, the gravity of the offense, and the circumstances of the crime, and (3) the trial court considered all the circumstances in the case and properly found no reason to deviate from the mandatory sentence.


OUTCOME: The district court's sentencing order was affirmed.

 

1540 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Lee v. Pennington


No. 2002-CA-0381


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2002-0381 (La.App. 4 Cir. 10/16/02); 830 So. 2d 1037; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 3209; 31 Media L. Rep. 1267



October 16, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 11, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 2000-2867, DIVISION "L-15". Honorable Rosemary Ledet, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED AND REMANDED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff public servant filed a petition against defendants, mayor, city, police, district attorney, insurers, newspaper, and media, asking damages for defamation, malicious prosecution, racial profiling, and violations of abuse of rights doctrine and right to privacy. The Civil District Court, Orleans Parish, Louisiana, denied motions to consolidate and to declare La. Code Civ. Proc. Art. ann. 971 unconstitutional. The parties cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The public servant's arrest on the charges of aggravated rape was a matter of public record. The police department issued a news release detailing the public servant's arrest. Four television stations aired segments regarding the arrest that same evening, and the newspaper published an article regarding the arrest the next day. The first constitutional issue for the appellate court to consider was the constitutionality of the construction of La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 971. The appellate court found no constitutional flaw with the construction of the article. The second and most important constitutional issue before the appellate court was whether art. 971 violated the Equal Protection Clause. The appellate court found the constitutional challenges made were without merit. The abuse of rights doctrine could not be invoked. Malice was not proven because there was only conjecture presented that the articles and newscasts were published for the sole purpose of generating profits and to depict the public servant in a bad light. As to the public servant's argument regarding racial profiling, Louisiana law did not recognize a cause of action for racial profiling in the media.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the judgment in part, as to the trial court's denial of the motion to consolidate and the granting of the special motion to strike. The appellate court reversed, however, as to the trial court's failure to award reasonable attorney fees and costs. The matter was remanded.

 

1541 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Stewart


No. 2001-KA-2172


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2001-2172 (La.App. 4 Cir. 10/09/02); 830 So. 2d 350; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 3118



October 9, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication November 27, 2002.
Writ denied by State v. Stewart, 2003 La. LEXIS 2525 (La., Sept. 19, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 420-594, SECTION "C". Honorable Sharon K. Hunter, Judge.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AFFIRMED; SENTENCE VACATED; CASE REMANDED FOR RESENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Criminal District Court of Orleans Parish, Louisiana, convicted defendant of attempted possession of cocaine and sentenced defendant to 22 and 1/2 years at hard labor without the benefit of probation or suspension of sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: In its review for errors patent, the appellate court found that the trial court failed to observe the mandatory 24 hour delay between the denial of a motion for new trial and sentencing, and defendant did not waive the delay. Because defendant alleged the trial court imposed an excessive sentence, the sentence had to be vacated and the case remanded for resentencing. Defendant argued the trial court erred in permitting an officer to testify about the search performed by another officer, due to the original officer's unavailability. The testifying officer stated that he saw his partner search defendant's vehicle under the driver's seat and place the items he found on the roof of the vehicle. Additionally, defendant's counsel was made aware of the officer's absence prior to the commencement of the defendant's trial. Defendant's counsel did not object to proceeding to trial because of the officer's absence. The sentencing range for defendant as a fourth felony offender was 20 years to life. Defendant's 22 and 1/2 years sentence was within the lower range of the sentencing scale. The sentence imposed was not grossly out of proportion.


OUTCOME: The conviction was affirmed and the sentence vacated and remanded for resentencing.

State v. Suire


2002-411


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


2002-411 (La.App. 3 Cir. 10/02/02); 827 So. 2d 569; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 2969



October 2, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SIXTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF IBERIA, NO. 99-585. HONORABLE KEITH R. J. COMEAUX, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: SENTENCE VACATED AND SET ASIDE. CASE REMANDED TO THE TRIAL COURT FOR RESENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Sixteenth Judicial District Court, Iberia Parish (Louisiana), convicted defendant of communicating false information of planned arson and sentenced him to 10 years at hard labor. Defendant appealed. On remand for resentencing, the district court sentenced defendant to 8 years at hard labor. Defendant sought further review.


OVERVIEW: The office of community services removed defendant's daughter from his custody. The defendant made a bomb threat against community services. The building he threatened contained only a few persons, he presented no means of carrying out his threat, nor the intention to implement his threat, he expressed remorse, and he had no prior criminal record. In addition, there was testimony that defendant was not a threat to others and was not mentally ill. The appellate court found that: (1) a sentence of eight years was not warranted when considering the maximum penalties for aggravated assault and the degree of culpability of the defendant's actions; and (2) sentencing defendant to eight years was excessive, given the circumstances; the sentence shocked the appellate court's sense of justice and was grossly disproportionate to the severity of the crime.


OUTCOME: Defendant's sentence was vacated, and the matter was remanded to the district court for resentencing.
