State v. Sullivan


02-0360


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


2002-0360 (La.App. 3 Cir. 10/02/02);  827 So. 2d 1260; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 2985



October 2, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication.
Writ denied by State v. Sullivan, 841 So. 2d 790, 2003 La. LEXIS 1181 (La., Apr. 21, 2003)
Writ denied by State v. Sullivan, 2003 La. LEXIS 2387 (La., Sept. 5, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SIXTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF IBERIA, NO. 97-601, HONORABLE WILLIAM D. HUNTER, DISTRICT JUDGE.
State ex rel. Sullivan v. State, 810 So. 2d 1160, 2002 La. LEXIS 765 (La., Mar. 8, 2002)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction for first degree robbery several times. The 16th Judicial District Court, Parish of Iberia (Louisiana), sentenced defendant to 30 years at hard labor and denied his request for an out-of-time appeal, stating that he waived his right to an appeal by failing to timely file a motion to reconsider the sentence. On remand, the trial court granted leave to file an out-of-time appeal.


OVERVIEW: Inter alia, defendant claimed that the trial court erred, as the 30 year sentence imposed for first degree robbery was unconstitutionally excessive for a fourth felony offender who never committed a crime with a weapon. As a preliminary matter, the appellate court noted defendant failed to timely file a motion to reconsider his sentence, as required by La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 881.1(A), and, as a general rule, appellate courts were precluded from reviewing a sentence when a defendant failed to timely file such a motion. However, because defendant appeared to raise the issue of ineffective counsel in his pro se assignment of error, the appellate court reviewed the sentence. The 30-year sentence was clearly within the statutory limit. Before imposing sentence, the trial court received a pre-sentence investigation report that showed defendant was a fourth-felony offender and included a number of other charges that never became convictions. The appellate court found that the trial court did not abuse its wide discretion in sentencing defendant, and the trial court articulated the factors, both aggravating and mitigating, it considered before rendering the sentence.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

1544 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Lanthier v. Family Dollar Store


NUMBER 02-429


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


2002-0429 (La.App. 3 Cir. 10/02/02);  827 So. 2d 547; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 2986



October 2, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE OFFICE OF WORKERS' COMPENSATION, DISTRICT 02 PARISH OF RAPIDES, NO. 01-06757. ANTHONY PALERMO, WORKERS' COMPENSATION JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant injured worker appealed a judgment of the Office of Workers' Compensation, District 02, Parish of Rapides (Louisiana) (OWC). The worker claimed that her manager had falsely testified that the worker was a part-time employee. OWC dismissed, on its own motion, the worker's claim of employer fraud under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1208 on the basis of lack of subject matter jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: The issues on appeal were whether the OWC had subject matter jurisdiction to consider claims of misrepresentation under § 23:1208, and whether § 23:1208 was constitutional. The appellate court held that § 23:1208 was beyond the scope of the powers and authority granted to the OWC, an executive branch office. The appellate court declared § 23:1208 unconstitutional pursuant to La. Const. arts. 5, §§ 1, § 16; 2, § 2. In accordance with the constitutional provisions, the workers' compensation judge properly recognized that he lacked the authority to review a claim of fraudulent misrepresentation. La. Const. art. 5, § 16, limited the scope of the power and authority of an administrative tribunal like the OWC. If the employer had been found in violation of the statute, then the employer would also have been subject to criminal penalties under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1208(C). Imposition of such a penalty was clearly a judicial branch, not an executive branch, prerogative. Undertaking such action infringed upon powers specifically delegated to the judiciary and violated the Louisiana Constitution.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

1545 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Berry v. Dep't of Pub. Safety & Corr.


2001 CA 2186 C/W 2001 CA 2187


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2001 2186 (La.App. 1 Cir. 09/27/02); 835 So. 2d 606; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 2818



September 27, 2002, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from The State Police Commission. Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana. Docket No. 00-104-D c/w 01-106-O. Baxter W. Welch, Chairman. Joseph S. Cage, Jr., Gary M. Clark, Brooke Duncan, III, Patrick M. LaSalle and Theodore J. Newman, Members.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant demoted state police officer appealed a decision rendered by the State Police Commission, East Baton Rouge Parish (Louisiana), that upheld his demotion by the department of public safety and corrections, office of state police (SP), for, inter alia, failure to report off-duty traffic details. The demoted officer also appealed the commission's decision that it lacked jurisdiction to entertain his appeal of an annual performance rating.


OVERVIEW: The officer was demoted for violating SP Procedural Orders, as he failed to submit the paperwork for 30 off-duty traffic details he worked over a 2 year period. As a supervisor, the officer was expected to set an example. The commission found he had not done so, and, considering all of his violations, it concluded he should not have served in a supervisory position and upheld his demotion. The parties stipulated the officer had not reported the income he earned from the details on his income tax return. The appellate court held that all of the versions of Procedural Order 306 clearly and unambiguously covered off-duty personnel conducting "traffic control" at special events. The violation was established. The revision, which specifically added the words "traffic details" to the listing set out in Procedural Order 306, merely added another item to an illustrative list. Accordingly, the commission based its disciplinary decision on legal cause and did not abuse its discretion by imposing a punishment on the officer. The officer's "needs improvement" rating was not discriminatory, was not a removal or disciplinary claim, and the commission lacked jurisdiction over that issue.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

1546 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Wood v. Wood


NUMBER 2002 CU 0860


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


835 So. 2d 568; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 2819



September 27, 2002, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of error denied Wood v. Wood, 2003 La. LEXIS 880 (La., Mar. 28, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the 22nd Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of Washington, State of Louisiana. Suit Number 72, 441-"A". Honorable Raymond S. Childress, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a divorce, appellant mother was subsequently granted sole custody of her child, and appellees, the paternal grandparents, were granted limited visitation, with the requirement they not allow contact between the child and the incarcerated father. Later, the 22nd Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of Washington (Louisiana) granted the grandparents additional summer visitation. The mother appealed.


OVERVIEW: In post-divorce proceedings, the trial court had granted the mother sole custody of the child after the mother alleged that the father had a recent history of criminal sexual abuse and was incarcerated in Utah. After filing two rules for contempt against the mother for allegedly frustrating their visitation rights, the grandparents sought a modification, and obtained an additional one week of summer visitation. The appellate court cited a recent United States Supreme Court decision which rejected any visitation scheme that trampled upon the sacred and paramount rights of a fit parent to dictate the best interests of his or her children. When a parent was incarcerated, as here, the grandparents were relieved of showing extraordinary circumstance to obtain visitation, but they nevertheless had to show that the requested visitation was in the "best interest" of the child. The burden of proof was on the grandparents. Visitation that unduly burdened parental rights would be unconstitutional, regardless of the provisions of statutory law. The appellate court held that by improperly placing the burden on the mother and using the wrong analysis, the trial court fell into reversible error.


OUTCOME: judgment mandating summer visitation is reversed. The matter is remanded to the trial court for reevaluation of its decision in light of this opinion. Upon rendering a new judgment on the issue of additional, visitation to the grandparents, the court must provide an articulation of the court's analysis and reasons for its decision.

Bd. of Assessors v. City of New Orleans


No. 2002-CA-0691


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2002-0691 (La.App. 4 Cir. 09/25/02); 829 So. 2d 501; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 3060



September 25, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication November 14, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 99-17471, DIVISION "K-14". Honorable Louis A. DiRosa, Judge Pro Tempore.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the board, filed three petitions against appellee, the city, for payments in lieu of taxes (PILOT) collected and retained by the city. The board's third supplemental and amended petition added claims for damage relating to certain alleged PILOT projects. The city filed a motion for summary judgment. The Civil District Court, Orleans Parish, Louisiana, granted the motion and dismissed the proceedings. The board appealed.


OVERVIEW: The board sued the city in order to obtain a judgment awarding PILOT money collected and retained by the city in connection with a store's distribution center located in eastern New Orleans. The board also sought judgment declaring La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 51:1160, as amended, to be unconstitutional and ordering the city to distribute any and all future PILOT money under the store's agreement to the board and to all other tax recipient bodies of the city. Ultimately, the trial court entered judgment in favor of the city, and the board challenged the decision. The court of appeal held that: (1) the trial court did not err in granting the city's motion for summary judgment, since there existed no genuine issues of material fact concerning the lack of authorization of the amendment to the PILOT agreement; (2) the trial court did not err in failing to declare La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 51:1160, as amended in 1972, unconstitutional, since that statute did not violate the provisions of La. Const. art. VII, § 14(A); and (3) the trial court did not err in ruling that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2798.1 was applicable to the city's actions.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed. The costs of the appeal were assessed to the board.

 

1548 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Perritt v. Dona


No. 35,628-CW, No. 35,724-CW, No. 35,841-CW (Consolidated Cases)


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


35,628 (La.App. 2 Cir. 09/20/02); 827 So. 2d 1222; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 2775



September 20, 2002, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of error granted Perritt v. Dona, 836 So. 2d 74, 2003 La. LEXIS 392 (La., Jan. 31, 2003)
Writ of error granted Perritt v. Dona, 836 So. 2d 74, 936 So. 2d 74, 2003 La. LEXIS 393 (La., Jan. 31, 2003)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by Perritt v. Dona, 2003 La. LEXIS 1963 (La., July 2, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Remand from the Louisiana Supreme Court. Originally Appealed from the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita, Louisiana. Trial Court Nos. M412001, M352001, M612001. Honorable Alvin Rue Sharp, Judge, Honorable Benjamin Jones, Judge, Honorable Michael S. Ingram, Judge.
Richmond v. Brown, 812 So. 2d 624, 2002 La. LEXIS 953 (La., Mar. 15, 2002)
Arnold v. Dona, 812 So. 2d 623, 2002 La. LEXIS 955 (La., Mar. 15, 2002)
Perritt v. Dona, 812 So. 2d 624, 2002 La. LEXIS 954 (La., Mar. 15, 2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patients instituted medical malpractice actions against defendant health care providers, incidental to pending medical review panel inquiries. The parties sought supervisory review of the district court's ruling on discovery issues. The Louisiana Supreme Court effectively consolidated the separate cases, granted writ applications, and rendered an opinion directing that the issue be addressed in an opinion.


OVERVIEW: In two of the cases, the patients were served with interrogatories about the standard of care, which they refused to answer. In the first case, the patient gave a limited answer. In the second case, the patient answered that she was not an expert regarding the applicable medical standard. The patient refused to answer a second question. The common issue of the three cases concerned the sufficiency of the statement of material facts of the claim as presented to the medical review panel. In the third case, the claim did not list the particular injury or injuries suffered, or allege facts of causation linking injuries to the various unidentified actions of the physician. As such, the claim did not properly set forth a statement of the material facts. As to the first two cases, the process employed by the health care providers were faulty. First, there was no showing regarding any insufficiency in the claims to the Patient Compensation Fund. Further, the discovery in the non-judicial proceedings was not in keeping with the intended nature of the proceeding as described nor was discovery through written interrogatories expressly provided in the Medical Malpractice Act.


OUTCOME: The ruling of the district court was affirmed as to the third case. The trial court's ruling issuing a protective order and refusing to order answers to a written interrogatory was affirmed in the first case. In the second case, the trial court's ruling in ordering the patient to respond to written interrogatories was reversed.

 

1549 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Bernard v. La. Dep't of Pub. Safety & Corr.


2000 CA 1912


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2000 1912 (La.App. 1 Cir. 09/20/02); 843 So. 2d 413; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 4310



September 20, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by Bernard v. 862 So. 2d 975, 2004 La. LEXIS 37 (La., Jan. 9, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1]
Bernard v. La. Dep't of Pub. Safety & Corr., 2002 La. App. LEXIS 2832 (La.App. 1 Cir., Sept. 20, 2002)
Bernard v. La. Dep't of Pub. Safety & Corr., 835 So. 2d 470, 2001 La. App. LEXIS 2641 (La.App. 1 Cir., Nov. 9, 2001)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent, the Louisiana Department of Public Safety and Corrections (the Department), applied for a rehearing, alleging the appeals court's original opinion was in error regarding its interpretation of the screening provisions of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:1188 as applied by the Louisiana district court in this case to dismiss petitioner inmate's claims.


OVERVIEW: The inmate claimed habeas relief should be granted to him under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 362(2), which allowed relief if his original custody was lawful, but by some subsequent act, omission, or event, had become unlawful. He contended the application of an allegedly unconstitutional statute to return him to custody on a parole violation was the act that had made his current custody unlawful. The appeals court concluded the inmate's argument was not one that could properly be raised through post-conviction habeas under article 362(2). The statute that he claimed was unconstitutional had never been declared unconstitutional. The triggering event--application of an unconstitutional statute--for a habeas corpus claim under article 362(2) had not occurred. The inmate's claim was initiated as a civil action seeking redress from a governmental entity. Because an alleged violation of a constitutionally protected right could be raised in a separate suit invoking the district court's original jurisdiction, the screening provisions of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:1188 were correctly applied, and the district court's judgment of dismissal was appropriate for appellate review.


OUTCOME: On rehearing, the judgment of the district court dismissing defendant's claims was affirmed.

Peterson v. Toffton


No. 36,372-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


36,372 (La.App. 2 Cir. 09/18/02); 828 So. 2d 160; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 2747



September 18, 2002, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by Peterson v. Toffton, 2004 La. LEXIS 274 (La., Jan. 30, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Second Judicial District Court for the Parish of Claiborne, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 35285. Honorable Jenifer Ward Clason, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate filed suit against defendants, the prison warden, prison employees, and the department of corrections, seeking punitive and compensatory damages for injuries he allegedly suffered in connection with disciplinary proceedings. Prior to docketing, the Second Judicial District Court, Claiborne Parish, Louisiana, dismissed the inmate's suit. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The underlying action arose when one of the employees filed a disciplinary report against the inmate, allegedly in retaliation and out of anger after the inmate said he would bring charges against the employee for not allowing him to use the phone to report another employee. At a disciplinary proceeding, the inmate was found to have violated prison rules and was penalized and placed in isolation, which led to his initiating the instant action. In his petition, he alleged he suffered physical injuries from the time spent in isolation, as well as emotional distress and humiliation. On review, the appellate court found that since the inmate's complaint sought a remedy with respect to his conditions of confinement, he was required to seek judicial review of any administrative remedy decision in the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:1177(A). As he did not, the trial court properly utilized the judicial screening provisions of the Corrections Administrative Remedy Procedure, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 15:1171, 15:1178, of the Prisoner's Litigation Reform Act to dismiss his claim.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1551 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Stokes


No. 36,212-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


36,212 (La.App. 2 Cir. 09/18/02); 828 So. 2d 631; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 2762



September 18, 2002, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected November 6, 2002.
Writ of certiorari denied State v. Stokes, 2003 La. LEXIS 2383 (La., Sept. 5, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 99-F1160. Honorable Sharon Marchman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with aggravated rape, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:42A(1) or (2). He filed motions to quash the indictment. The State amended the indictment. Defendant filed a motion to suppress a photographic lineup, which was denied. Defendant dismissed the motions to quash. The jury found him guilty. The Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita, Louisiana sentenced defendant to life imprisonment. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a 24-year-old man, was charged with the aggravated rape of a 16-year-old girl, in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:42A(1) or (2). Defendant was sentenced to life in prison, without the benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence. Defendant challenged his conviction and sentence. The court of appeal held that: (1) the evidence was sufficient to support the conviction; (2) defendant's first set of motions to quash were voluntarily dismissed by defendant; (3) the trial court did not abuse its discretion by denying the motion to quash in the second set referring to the State's failure to timely produce evidence favorable to defendant; (4) the photographic lineup was not so unduly suggestive and conducive to mistaken identification as to deny defendant due process of law; and (5) the sentence was not excessive.


OUTCOME: The conviction and sentence were affirmed.

 

1552 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


City of Baker Sch. Bd. v. La. Dep't of Elections


No. 2002 CA 1905


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2002 1905 (La.App. 1 Cir. 09/13/02); 835 So. 2d 541; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 2707



September 11, 2002, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, State of Louisiana. Honorable Kay Bates, Judge Presiding. Trial Court No. 498,701.



DISPOSITION: Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff school board filed suit against defendant Louisiana Department of Elections and defendant Louisiana Secretary of State seeking a declaratory judgment that a reapportionment plan complied with state law. The 19th Judicial District Court, in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, State of Louisiana, found that the plan violated La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 17:71.3 and was thus invalid. The board appealed.


OVERVIEW: The school board reapportioned itself. The board had five single-member districts. The incumbents on the board in four of those districts qualified without opposition. The election to fill the fifth seat was contested. Those persons--the four incumbents who qualified without opposition and the contestants for the remaining district--were parties who would be affected. As such, they should have been joined in this lawsuit. In light of the failure of the board to join the parties needed for just adjudication, the appellate court noticed the lack of these parties on its own motion.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed and remanded the matter with instructions.

 

1553 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Malone v. Tubbs


No. 36,816-CA, No. 36,817-CA (Consolidated cases)


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


36,816 (La.App. 2 Cir. 09/06/02); 825 So. 2d 585; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 2703



September 6, 2002, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by Reeh v. Shyne, 824 So. 2d 1164, 2002 La. LEXIS 2601 (La., Sept. 11, 2002)
Writ dismissed by Reeh v. Shyne, 882 So. 2d 1147, 2004 La. LEXIS 2801 (La., Sept. 24, 2004)
Related proceeding at, Magistrate's recommendation at Simmons v. Malone, 2006 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 101468 (W.D. La., Mar. 6, 2006)
Related proceeding at Malone v. Shyne, 936 So. 2d 1279, 2006 La. App. LEXIS 1875 (La.App. 2 Cir., Aug. 29, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court Nos. 469,214 and 469,226. Honorable Frank H. Thaxton, III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, candidates for political office, had been convicted of crimes subjecting them to the disqualifying provisions of La. Const. art. I, § 10(B). Petitioner voter filed a petition challenging the qualifications of one of the candidates. The candidate argued that he had received an automatic first offender pardon. The First Judicial District Court, Parish of Caddo (Louisiana), held that the candidates were disqualified and they appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appeals raised the same basic issue: whether the provisions of art. I, § 10, as amended November 5, 1998, disqualified all candidates for elective office who had been convicted of a felony, who had exhausted all legal remedies and who had neither received a gubernatorial pardon, nor had 15 years elapse from the completion of their original sentence. The appellate court held that it did. The language of art. I, § 10, was clear and unambiguous. None of the three candidates was eligible to qualify for elective office unless art. I, § 10, could not have been applied to them: (1) because application would have been an illegal retroactive application under Louisiana law; (2) because the article's disqualifying language, effective November 5, 1998, amounted to an ex post facto law in violation of the U.S. Constitution; or (3) because the disqualifying language conflicted with other constitutional provisions so as to create ambiguity regarding its application. While the appellate court agreed that the amendment to art. I, § 10, was substantive, it clearly was intended to apply to all convicted felons attempting to qualify for public office after the effective date of the amendment.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed and costs were assessed to the candidates.

 

1554 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Melancon


No. 2001-KA-1656


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2001-1656 (La.App. 4 Cir. 08/21/02); 826 So. 2d 633; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 2664



August 21, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of error denied State v. Melancon, 2003 La. LEXIS 791 (La., Mar. 21, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 408-778, SECTION "L". Honorable Terry Alarcon, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged by bill of information with possession with the intent to distribute cocaine and entered a plea of not guilty at his arraignment. The Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish, Section "L" (Louisiana), denied defendant's motions to suppress evidence and for a new trial. Defendant was adjudicated to be a third felony offender. The trial court denied defendant's motion to reconsider sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court's failure to rule on the merits of a motion for new trial prior to sentencing constituted an error patent, however, because defendant's original sentence was vacated as a result of his multiple offender adjudication, the error was cured. Defendant argued that the prosecutor's actions during closing argument were prejudicial and influenced the jury's verdict. The prosecutor crumbled the affidavit of a witness during his closing argument. The appellate court held that the prosecutor's actions were not prejudicial. By crumbling the paper, he gave emphasis to his argument that the document was worthless. The prosecutor questioned the affiant's credibility and the fact that he did not appear to testify at trial. The jury was adequately instructed on actual and constructive possession. The requested instruction was not supported by any fact brought out at trial. To the contrary, the testimony of the police officer demonstrated that defendant was initially in actual possession of the drugs. He was not "merely present." Defendant did not produce any evidence to prove that he should have been sentenced to a sentence less than the mandatory sentence of life imprisonment.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

1555 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lee


No. 2001-KA-2082


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2001-2082 (La.App. 4 Cir. 08/21/02); 826 So. 2d 616; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 2665



August 21, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied State v. Lee, 852 So. 2d 1019, 2003 La. LEXIS 2371 (La., Sept. 5, 2003)
Writ of habeas corpus denied State ex rel. Lee v. State, 935 So. 2d 146, 2006 La. LEXIS 2289 (La., Aug. 18, 2006)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Lee v. Cain, 2007 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 103045 (E.D. La., June 20, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 414-094, SECTION "C". Honorable Sharon K. Hunter, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish, Section "C" (Louisiana), for aggravated battery and his sentence of life imprisonment, without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence as a third felony offender.


OVERVIEW: The district court denied defendant's motion for new trial and sentenced him that same day. La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 873 required a 24-hour delay between the denial of a motion for new trial and sentencing, unless defendant waived such delay. There was no indication defendant waived the delay, however, defendant showed no prejudice. Thus, the error was harmless. Defendant argued, inter alia, that the record failed to show that he made a knowing and intelligent waiver of his right to a jury trial. The appellate court held that the record contained the transcript of defendant's waiver of his right to a jury trial. The transcript indicated that the judge addressed and questioned defendant in the presence of his attorney as to whether he understood he had a right to trial by judge or jury. Defendant responded affirmatively. The judge then asked what type of trial he elected to proceed by. Defendant replied: "I would like to go with a judge." The record established defendant waived his right to a jury trial. Despite defendant's contention, the source of testimony was irrelevant to the establishment of the corpus delicti, so long as the statements were not those of the accused.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

1556 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Peterson v. Ward


No. 36,370-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


36,370 (La.App. 2 Cir. 08/16/02); 823 So. 2d 1146; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 2606



August 16, 2002, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State ex rel. Peterson v. State, 845 So. 2d 1069, 2003 La. LEXIS 1747 (La., May 30, 2003)
Writ denied by Peterson v. Ward, 2004 La. LEXIS 272 (La., Jan. 30, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Second Judicial District Court for the Parish of Claiborne, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 35,284. Honorable Jenifer Ward Clason, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate filed what he styled as a habeas corpus action against defendant prison officials in the Second Judicial District Court for the Parish of Claiborne (Louisiana). The inmate demanded to be transferred back to the prison where he was formerly housed and enrolled in its mental health program. The trial court summarily dismissed the action with prejudice.


OVERVIEW: The inmate alleged that he had been transferred from his former confinement to a new and harsher confinement as retaliation for exercising his rights to file complaints and lawsuits against prison officials. He did not allege that the complaints filed with the Department of Correction (DOC) had been resolved through its administrative remedy procedures. Thus, the trial and appellate courts found that his petition did not state a cognizable claim for habeas corpus relief as the inmate did not seek immediate or a speedier release from confinement. Rather, he alleged unconstitutional treatment while in confinement. He was challenging the conditions of his prison life, not the fact or length of his custody. The appellate court agreed with the trial court that the inmate's demand to be transferred back to the prison where he was formerly housed and enrolled in its mental health program must first be considered and disposed of through the administrative procedures of the DOC as required by the Corrections Administrative Remedy Procedure Act, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 15:1171-1180, and the Prison Litigation Reform Act, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 15:1181-1190.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

1557 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Poullard v. Hanson


No. 36,290-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


36,290 (La.App. 2 Cir. 08/14/02); 823 So. 2d 1130; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 2571



August 14, 2002, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Second Judicial District Court for the Parish of Claiborne, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 35147. Honorable Jenifer Ward Clason, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Second Judicial District Court for the Parish of Claiborne, Louisiana, granted judgment in favor of defendants, correctional institute employees, by sustaining their dilatory exceptions, in plaintiff prisoner's suit for damages and declaratory judgment. The prisoner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court had found that under Louisiana's Correction Administrative Remedy Procedure (CARP), La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 15:1171-1179, and Louisiana's Prison Litigation Reform Act (PLRA), La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 15:1181-1190, the prisoner was obligated to proceed with the administrative remedies available to him before he could file suit in the district court. The appellate court found that, after another case found that certain provisions of CARP were unconstitutional, the possibility existed for several sections of CARP to be saved from unconstitutionality vis-a-vis tort claims by the Department of Public Safety and Corrections adopting a new administrative remedy procedure and the legislature amending portions of CARP relating to judicial review. The new administrative remedy procedure rules simply informed the prisoner that he or she could file suit in district court. The legislature also amended provisions of CARP and PLRA. The trial court correctly found that the evidence presented indicated a failure by the prisoner to exhaust administrative remedies. The prisoner had 90 days to initiate administrative remedies for his action.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1558 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Felder


No. 36,228-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


36,228 (La.App. 2 Cir. 08/14/02);  823 So. 2d 1107; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 2584



August 14, 2002, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Felder v. Warden of David Wade Corr. Ctr., 2008 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 111395 (W.D. La., Sept. 24, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bossier, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 106,477. Honorable Bruce M. Bolin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was tried and convicted by a jury of possession of a firearm by a convicted felon. The Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bossier (Louisiana) sentenced defendant to 12 years at hard labor without the benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: En route to the scene of a fight, an officer pulled up behind defendant in a parking lot and called him over to the patrol vehicle. Defendant stopped briefly in front of the vehicle and then he ran down the street. While in pursuit, the officer stated that he saw defendant throw a gun down on the ground. After securing defendant, the officer retrieved the gun. Defendant also testified during trial. He stated that he ran from the officer because he was scared and denied possessing a firearm. However, defendant did admit that he had a prior simple burglary conviction. When viewed in the light most favorable to the State, the evidence was sufficient to support defendant's conviction for possession of a firearm by a convicted felon. The appellate court found that the officer's eyewitness account alone was sufficient to convict defendant. Considering defendant's prior criminal history, the fact that he was on probation when he committed the instant offense, and the fact that he lacked remorse and fled from the police, his sentence of 12 years at hard labor without benefits did not shock the conscience and was not unconstitutionally excessive.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Hudson v. City of Bossier


No. 36,213-CA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


36,213 (La.App. 2 Cir. 08/14/02); 823 So. 2d 1085; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 2587



August 14, 2002, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied Hudson v. City of Bossier, 831 So. 2d 279, 2002 La. LEXIS 3603 (La., Nov. 27, 2002)
Remanded by Hudson v. City of Bossier City, 2005 La. App. LEXIS 1 (La.App. 2 Cir., Jan. 6, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bossier, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 98,781. Honorable Bruce M. Bolin, Judge.
Horseshoe Entertainment v. Bossier Parish Police Jury, 714 So. 2d 920, 1998 La. App. LEXIS 1665 (La.App. 2 Cir., June 26, 1998)
Hudson v. City of Bossier, 766 So. 2d 738, 2000 La. App. LEXIS 2099 (La.App. 2 Cir., Aug. 25, 2000)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an appeal arising out of a taxpayer suit alleging that defendant city illegally contracted away its right to levy a per-person boarding tax on riverboat gaming operations within its jurisdiction, the Twenty-Sixth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Bossier (Louisiana) granted an exception of no right of action filed by all defendants except defendant parish police jury. Plaintiffs appealed.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs were an uncertified class of taxpayers and former members of the parish school board who challenged the legality of the contract between the city and the riverboat casinos. In the contracts, the city made a deal with the riverboats not to assess a boarding tax/fee in exchange for a fixed fee arrangement for a term of 10 years. In granting the exception of no right of action, the trial court found that plaintiffs had failed to show that the conduct complained of resulted in an increased tax burden and that they had no standing to challenge the legality of the contract at issue. The appellate court found that plaintiffs had at least a small and indeterminable interest in seeing that their elected representatives obeyed the laws and did not enter into illegal contracts in matters pertaining to the public fisc. The argument that the contract at issue represented a benefit and not a burden to the public fisc was without merit. The illegal surrender of the statutory right to tax the riverboats could not be considered a benefit to the public fisc. Thus, the trial court erred when it granted the exception of no right of action.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed and remanded the trial court's judgment.

State v. Juarbe


No. 2001-KA-2250


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2001-2250 (La.App. 4 Cir. 07/31/02); 824 So. 2d 1240; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 2531



July 31, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 18, 2002.
Writ denied by State ex rel. Juarbe v. State, 857 So. 2d 467, 2003 La. LEXIS 3153 (La., Oct. 31, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 369-910, SECTION "I". HONORABLE RAYMOND C. BIGELOW, JUDGE.
State v. Juarbe, 1999 La. App. LEXIS 3939 (La.App. 4 Cir., May 25, 1999)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish, Section "I" (Louisiana), which convicted defendant for second-degree murder and sentenced defendant to life imprisonment without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant's counsel argued that a mistrial should have been granted based on La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 770, due to the prosecutor's misconduct in introducing inadmissible evidence of other crimes during the questioning a witness. Defendant also raised several pro se issues on appeal. The appellate court agreed that the prosecutor's question should not have been asked and the answer should not have been admitted, however, the court held that the trial court did not err when it denied defendant's motion for a mistrial. Taken in totality with all other evidence, the court held that the comments did not likely contribute to the verdict. The trial court offered to admonish the jury, but defendant declined the trial court's offer. Moreover, the statement did not warrant reversal of defendant's conviction, as the testimony overwhelmingly established defendant's guilt. Thus, any error was harmless. The court also found that defendant's pro se assignments of error were without merit.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Creppel v. Dixon Corr. Inst.


2001 CA 2068


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2001 2068 (La.App. 1 Cir. 07/30/02); 822 So. 2d 760; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 2484



July 30, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1]
 Creppel v. Dixon Corr. Inst., 2002 La. App. LEXIS 2486 (La. App. 1st Cir. July 30, 2002).



DISPOSITION: Opinion clarified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prisoner sued appellee correctional facility in a Louisiana trial court in tort. The trial court sustained the correctional facility's exception of prematurity, holding the prisoner had not exhausted his administrative remedies. The prisoner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court had originally held that the administrative remedies that were the subject of the exception of prematurity because of failure to exhaust those remedies were an invalid attempt to alter the original jurisdiction of the trial court by legislative acts as they related to tort suits. The appellate court granted the correction facility's application for rehearing to further clarify its judgment. The appellate court noted the legislature was free to enact procedures for initial submission of tort claims by prisoners to administrative agency for review as long as the action of the administrative agency did not constitute the exercise of original jurisdiction. The appellate court concluded it did express an opinion on the exception of prematurity for failure to exhaust administrative remedies because those procedures were deemed unconstitutional as applied to tort suits.


OUTCOME: Th judgment of the trial court was reversed and remanded.

State v. Heard


No. 36,191-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


36,191 (La.App. 2 Cir. 07/17/02); 823 So. 2d 454; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 2374



July 17, 2002, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Appealed from the Second Judicial District Court for the Parish of Claiborne, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 19,877. Honorable Jennifer Clason, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Second Judicial District Court for the Parish of Claiborne, Louisiana, convicted defendant of purse snatching and adjudicated him a fourth-felony offender. Defendant was sentenced to life imprisonment without the possibility of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended the trial court erred in refusing to recuse the district attorney's office and in denying his motion to quash the habitual offender bill of information. He also complained that his sentence was excessive and unconstitutional. The appellate court found that defendant produced no evidence showing that the district attorney's bid for re-election created a personal interest in conflict with the fair and impartial administration of justice. Nor did defendant produce evidence to suggest that the State filed the habitual offender bill of information for the purpose of deterring or punishing the exercise of his legal rights; defendant failed to prove that a plea agreement existed or that he relinquished a fundamental right. Therefore, the trial court did not err in denying his motion to quash the habitual bill of information. As defendant was convicted of first degree robbery, purse snatching, and distribution of cocaine, his life sentence was proper under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1(A)(1(c)(ii). The record did not show that defendant's case was exceptional under the Johnson test.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1563 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Ceasar v. Barry


ADAM CEASAR, SR., ET AL. VERSUS DR. RICHARD J. BARRY, ET AL. 2002-0052


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


2002-0052 (La.App. 3 Cir. 07/17/02); 823 So. 2d 998; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 2376



July 17, 2002, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] APPEAL FROM THE FOURTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF CALCASIEU, NO. 89-6006, THE HONORABLE PATRICIA MINALDI, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: When appellee parents' medical malpractice suit was settled with defendant insurer, the Fourteenth Judicial District Court, Calcasieu Parish, Louisiana, found that liability was admitted, thereby precluding appellant patient's compensation fund from contesting the issue. The parents' motion for summary judgment was granted, awarding them damages and future medical care of their minor son. The compensation fund appealed.


OVERVIEW: The parents suit against defendants, a doctor, his insurer, and the hospital, alleged malpractice in the mother's prenatal care and in the delivery and birth of their son. On review, the compensation fund contended the trial court erred in implicitly ruling that the statutory admission of liability included an admission that the doctor was 100 percent responsible for the parents' damages. It further argued that because the parents' were still pursuing their claims against the hospital, the hospital could be found comparatively at fault for the son's injuries, and that the compensation fund would thereby be entitled to a pro rata reduction in the damages it could be required to pay. After reviewing the jurisprudence in this regard, the appellate court found that the compensation fund was correct in asserting that it was entitled to assert the comparative fault of the hospital. Accordingly, the parents were not entitled to summary judgment against the compensation fund based on the sole liability of the doctor.


OUTCOME: The summary judgment and the damages award were reversed and the case was remanded to determine the degree of comparative fault attributable to defendants, as well as for a determination of damages.

Flood v. Pendleton Mem'l Methodist Hosp.


No. 2002-CA-0440


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2002-0440 (La.App. 4 Cir. 07/17/02); 823 So. 2d 1002; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 2438



July 17, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 31, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 2001-8616, DIVISION "N-8". Honorable Ethel Simms Julien, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed..


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient filed a medical malpractice action against defendants, hospital and physicians, after the defendants' allegedly switched the patient's bone scan with another patient's bone scan. The Civil District Court, Orleans Parish, Louisiana, sustained the defendants' dilatory exception of prematurity. The patient appealed.


OVERVIEW: A nodule was found in the patient's lung. The patient underwent five courses of chemotherapy after the defendants' advised him that his bone scan indicated he had Stage IV cancer. When a second bone scan was conducted, it was learned that the patient's first bone scan had always been normal and the bone scan had been switched with another patient's bone scan. The patient claimed he did not need to submit his claim to a medical review panel as the misfiling of his bone scan was a clerical act and did not constitute malpractice as defined under the Private Medical Malpractice Act, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.41 et seq. The appellate court held that the misfiling of the bone scan was "treatment related" as the interpretation of the bone scan was a necessary step in the patient's cancer treatment program. The court also found the defendants were qualified health care providers within the meaning of § 40:1299.41 and were entitled to a medical review panel hearing before the patient filed suit. Finally, the patient failed to prove that § 40:1299.41 treated him differently from similarly situated patients under the State Medical Malpractice Act, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.39.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed and the patient's petition was dismissed without prejudice.

State v. Ricks


No. 2002-K-1126


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2002-1126 (La.App. 4 Cir. 07/10/02); 823 So. 2d 441; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 2378



July 10, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 23, 2003.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPLICATION FOR WRITS DIRECTED TO CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 426-731, SECTION "J". Honorable Leon Cannizzaro, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Writ granted. Sentence vacated. Case remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State filed a notice of intent to file for writs from the denial by the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish, Louisiana, to reconsider sentence against defendant.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was sentenced as a second offender to 10 years at hard labor with the first two years to be served without benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence. The State argued that the trial court erred by failing to impose the statutory minimum sentence under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 15:529.1, 40:967, 15 years at hard labor with the first two years to be served without benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence. The appellate court found that defense counsel did not argue for a lighter sentence. He did not rebut the presumption of constitutionality of the sentence under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1. Defendant had been arrested for battery, resisting an officer, and illegal uses of firearms during a crime. This was an indication of violent criminal activity; thus the trial court erred by sentencing defendant below the statutorily mandated guidelines.

1566 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Madison v. Ward


2000 CA 2842


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2000-2842, (La.App. 1 Cir. 07/03/02); 825 So. 2d 1245; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 2210



July 3, 2002, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] ON APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. (NUMBER 470,393 "H"), PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE. STATE OF LOUISIANA. HONORABLE J. MICHAEL MCDONALD, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: APPEAL DISMISSED IN PART; REMANDED IN PART WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The petitioner sought judicial review of a decision in an administrative remedy procedure. After a hearing, a commissioner for the 19th Judicial District Court, Louisiana, recommended dismissal of the petition. The district court agreed with the recommendation and signed a judgment dismissing the petition with prejudice. The petitioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The essence of petitioner's appeal was that the prohibition against good time in his sentence was illegal because the sentencing court failed to stipulate for the record that he was being sentenced under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 890.1, and that his equal protection rights were violated because a co-defendant received the same sentence but allegedly received good time and was released. This allegation of an illegal sentence was not, however, a proper subject for habeas relief, and was not subject to the appellate court's jurisdiction, pursuant to the Corrections Administrative Remedy Procedure, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 15:1171-79. The petitioner's claim as to the denial of good time release should have been raised either through timely motion for reconsideration of sentence directed to the sentencing court, timely direct appeal of that sentence to the appropriate court of appeal, or at any time by a motion to correct illegal sentence directed to the sentencing court. As to the purported constitutional claim, the appellate court instructed the district court to dismiss that claim without prejudice.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed, in part, for lack of jurisdiction, and the matter was remanded with instructions to dismiss the constitutional claim.

Vermilion Parish Police Jury v. Williams


2002-12


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


2002-12 (La.App. 3 Cir. 07/03/02); 824 So. 2d 466; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 2212



July 3, 2002, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1]  APPEAL FROM THE OFFICE OF WORKERS' COMPENSATION, DISTRICT 04, PARISH OF LAFAYETTE, NO. 99-8539. HONORABLE SHARON MORROW.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant parish employer appealed a decision of the Office of Workers' Compensation, District 04, Parish of Lafayette (Louisiana), which found in favor of appellee employee. The compensation court found, inter alia, that the parish was responsible to the employee for injuries he sustained in a fall sometime after his original injury and that the employee continued to be temporarily, totally disabled.


OVERVIEW: The parish argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred in finding that the employee was entitled to temporary total disability benefits as opposed to supplemental earnings benefits. It argued that it proved that there were jobs available and offered to the employee. The appellate court held that the workers' compensation judge found that the employee continued to be temporarily, totally disabled, and that the compensation judge based that finding upon the employee's doctor's testimony. The doctor testified that the employee was unable to work due to his many problems which included the palsy, headaches, back pain, neck pain, family history, social abilities, and education. And that the employee's back pain and psychological problems associated with his initial work-related accident would alone have been disabling. The parish also claimed that the trial court erred in finding that the ankle injury was related to the work accident. The appellate court held that the emergency room records supported the judge's finding that the ankle injury was related to the original back and leg injury. The employee was entitled to attorney fees pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1201.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the workers' compensation court was affirmed. Costs of the appeal were assessed to the employer.

 

1568 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Nelson


No. 2002-KA-65


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


2002-65 (La.App. 5 Cir. 06/26/02); 822 So. 2d 796; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 2167



June 26, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 21, 2002.
Writ of error denied State v. Nelson, 2003 La. LEXIS 1053 (La., Feb. 21, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 01-2820, DIVISION "P". HONORABLE MELVIN ZENO, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed her conviction for possession of cocaine and alleged, inter alia, that the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, Division "P" (Louisiana), erred in denying her motion to suppress evidence and to suppress her statements, as the Miranda warnings she was given were incomplete and could not have served as a basis for admission of the alleged statements.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended the detective failed to advise her that she could terminate questioning at any time. Defendant argued that she was not advised of her right to terminate questioning after she began making a statement. The right to terminate questioning was a right that had to be observed; but, it was not specifically included in the rights that had to be verbally advised. The detective testified that he told defendant about the narcotics investigation and advised her of her rights immediately after he removed her from the vehicle. Defendant stated that she understood those rights. The appellate court held that the detective advised defendant of all of her rights pursuant to Miranda. In addition, once defendant arrived at the police station, she refused to make any more statements. Thus, she exercised her right to terminate questioning, which the officer observed. The statements made by defendant to the detective occurred after she had been fully advised of her constitutional rights, and the trial judge did not err in denying the motion. The informant's tip was sufficient to establish reasonable suspicion to conduct a stop, and there was sufficient probable cause for an arrest.


OUTCOME: The trial court's denial of defendant's motion to suppress and defendant's conviction of possession of cocaine were affirmed.

 

1569 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Reed


2002-214


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


2002-214 (La.App. 3 Cir. 06/26/02); 2002 La. App. LEXIS 2564



June 26, 2002, Rendered


NOTICE:   [*1] DECISION WITHOUT PUBLISHED OPINION


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication.
Writ of error denied State v. Reed, 2003 La. LEXIS 672 (La., Mar. 14, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE THIRTY-THIRD JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF ALLEN, DOCKET NO. CR-00-0849. HONORABLE JOEL GERARD DAVIS, PRESIDING. Reported in Table Case Format at: 2002 La. App. LEXIS 2159.
 State v. Reed, 2002 La. App. LEXIS 2159 (La.App. 3 Cir., June 26, 2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed, as amended.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to the charge of possession of marijuana over 60 pounds after the Thirty-third Judicial District Court, Parish of Allen, Louisiana, denied his motion to suppress. Defendant was sentenced to 15 years at hard labor without benefit of parole, probation or suspension of sentence. The trial court also denied defendant's motion for reconsideration of his sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested after a confidential informant purchased drugs from him. The police executed a search warrant at defendant's home shortly after defendant had sold drugs to the informant, and the police recovered 120 pounds of marijuana from defendant's home. Defendant argued that the trial court should have granted his motion to suppress, as the trial court considered evidence at the evidentiary hearing that was outside the four corners of the affidavit, and that the affidavit was insufficient to establish probable cause. The appellate court held that while the language of the affidavit was imprecise, it was not so lacking in indicia of probable cause as to alert the issuing judge that its existence was entirely unreasonable. As there was no evidence that the police misled the issuing judge, or that the issuing judge was not a detached and neutral magistrate, exclusion of the evidence seized was not warranted. The legislature reduced the sentencing range for the crime that defendant pled guilty to after his conviction, but he was not entitled to be sentenced under the new sentencing range unless the legislature specifically stated the new statute was to be retroactive.


OUTCOME: The denial of the motion to suppress was affirmed, but defendant's sentence was amended to provide that he serve 15 years imprisonment at hard labor, with 10 years to be served without benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence.

ANR Pipeline Co. v. La. Tax Comm'n

COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2002 0576 (La.App. 1 Cir. 06/21/02); 822 So. 2d 758; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 2034



June 21, 2002, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 6, 2002.
Rehearing denied by ANR Pipeline Co. v. La. Tax Comm'n, 2002 La. App. LEXIS 2503 (La.App. 1 Cir., July 30, 2002)
Writ denied by ANR Pipeline Co. v. 854 So. 2d 343, 2003 La. LEXIS 2594 (La., Sept. 26, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, State of Louisiana. Trial Court No. 491,897. Honorable Timothy E. Kelley, Judge.
ANR Pipeline Co. v. 811 So. 2d 876, 2002 La. LEXIS 734 (La., Mar. 6, 2002)



DISPOSITION: REMANDED WITH ORDER.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant interstate pipeline companies paid ad valorem taxes under protest and protested valuation to appellee tax commission, then sued for a declaratory judgment and refund. The commission denied the companies' motion for a continuance of its evidentiary hearings. They petitioned for writs and an injunction against the hearings. The 19th Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana, denied their requests. They appealed.


OVERVIEW: The companies asserted that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:1851K, which provided for a 25 percent assessment, violated various provisions of the United States and Louisiana Constitutions in that interstate pipeline companies' properties were assessed at a higher rate than were companies engaged solely in intrastate transportation. While the companies appeal was pending, another panel of the appellate court addressed identical issues in another case involving the same companies in a different tax year. The appellate court in that case stayed proceedings before the commission until § 47:1851K's constitutionality was determined.


OUTCOME: All proceedings before the commission in the matter docketed herein were stayed until a final ruling was issued by the trial court on the constitutionality of a statute. Discussion of the issues raised in the appeal were pretermitted. The case was remanded to the trial court. Appeal costs were assessed to the commission.

 

1571 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Florida v. La. Dep't of Pub. Safety & Corr.


NUMBER 2001 CA 1145


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


201 1145 (La.App. 1 Cir. 06/21/02); 822 So. 2d 712; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 2061



June 21, 2002, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 6, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana. Trial Court Number 462,873. Honorable John Perry, Judge Pro Tempore Presiding.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant former inmates filed a petition for damages from a denial of due process and loss of liberty interest by reason of an illegal forfeiture of good time and concomitant increase in the number of days incarcerated. The 19th Judicial District Court, East Baton Rouge Parish (Louisiana), dismissed the suit without prejudice for the former inmates failure to show that all administrative remedies were exhausted. The former inmates appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the former inmates argued that the district court erred in maintaining the agency's exceptions of vagueness and improper cumulation based on the erroneous finding that the former inmates were required to submit to an unconstitutional administrative review process prior to filing suit for damages. The appellate court held that, in light of a recent Louisiana Supreme Court decision holding the provisions of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:1171-1179 unconstitutional as applied to inmate tort actions, the district court erred in dismissing the former inmates' claims. To the extent that § 15:1171-1179 allowed the agency to exercise original jurisdiction in tort actions, the statute violated La. Const. art. V, § 16(A), as it divested the district courts of original jurisdiction over a tort action. The claims asserted by the former inmates were claims to recover damages for injury while incarcerated in prison. Thus, to the extent they asserted a tort action, the former inmates were entitled to have the district court adjudicate their tort claims under its original jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded.

 

1572 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Armand v. La. Dep't of Health & Human Res.


NUMBER 2000 CA 1457


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2000 1457 (La.App. 1 Cir. 06/21/02); 822 So. 2d 671; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 2068



June 21, 2002, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 6, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge. Suit Number 367,062. Honorable Bob Downing, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Nineteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana, dismissed plaintiffs', mother and son, motion for summary judgment and granted defendants', hospital and state, motion for summary judgment on the issue of constitutionality of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.39. Plaintiffs appealed.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs sued defendants in a medical malpractice action. La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.39 limited the liability of state health-care providers in a medical malpractice action for general damages and lost wages to a $ 500,000 statutory cap. The appellate court found that the prior judgment adjudicating liability and awarding quantum was not res judicata as to the issue of constitutionality. Prior caselaw dictated that the resolution of the issue of the constitutionality of $ 500,000 statutory caps on medical malpractice judgments were constitutional. Nothing in the law permitted a court to depart from traditional notions of constitutional law to conclude that the statute violated the constitution. No Louisiana court had held that after analyzing due process, adequate remedy, original jurisdiction, sovereign immunity, and separation of powers issues presented in similar cases involving claims against both private and public health-care providers. If the cap was to be changed, it had to be by the power of the legislature.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Creppel v. Dixon Corr. Inst.

COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2001 2068 (La.App. 1 Cir. 06/21/02); 822 So. 2d 760; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 2093



June 21, 2002, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 6, 2002.Review or Rehearing granted, Clarified: Creppel v. Dixon Corr. Inst., La. App. 2001-2068, 2002 La. App. LEXIS 2486 (La. Ct. App. 1 Cir. July 30, 2002).

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate appealed an administrative ruling in the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana, holding his claim of negligence against a prison nurse was premature, as he failed to exhaust his administrative remedies. The trial court affirmed the decision. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate sued the correctional facility in the trial court, alleging an on-duty nurse committed an act of negligence. V, § 16(A), as trial courts had original jurisdiction over all civil and criminal matters.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed and remanded.

State v. Williams


2002 KA 0065


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2000 0065 (La.App. 1 Cir. 06/21/02); 822 So. 2d 764; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 2032



June 21, 2002, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 6, 2002.
Writ denied by State ex rel. Williams v. State, 870 So. 2d 263, 2004 La. LEXIS 1270 (La., Apr. 8, 2004)
Post-conviction relief denied at State ex rel. Williams v. State, 924 So. 2d 148, 2006 La. LEXIS 540 (La., Feb. 10, 2006)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Williams v. State, 118 So. 3d 392, 2013 La. LEXIS 1508 (La., 2013)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Remanded by State v. Williams, 2015 La. App. LEXIS 393 (La.App. 1 Cir., Feb. 27, 2015)
Post-conviction relief denied at State ex rel. Williams v. State, 177 So. 3d 1054, 2015 La. LEXIS 2264 (La., 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FIRST JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. (NUMBER 97243 "B"), PARISH OF TANGIPAHOA, STATE OF LOUISIANA. HONORABLE BRUCE C. BENNETT, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCED AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury convicted defendant for three counts of armed robbery. Defendant filed motions for post verdict judgment of acquittal and new trial, which were denied. The Twenty-First Judicial District Court, Parish of Tangipahoa, Louisiana, sentenced defendant to 99 years at hard labor, without benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence, on each count, to run consecutive with each other. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: This matter involved three armed robberies committed in the same town. On appeal, defendant argued there was insufficient evidence to prove his identity as the perpetrator. He contended the eyewitnesses' identifications were unreliable because each eyewitness failed to see or mention tattoos on his face and arms. The State argued the uncontradicted identification by the witness in each robbery was sufficient to negate any reasonable probability of misidentification. The appeals court concluded that a rational trier of fact, viewing the evidence in the light most favorable to the prosecution, could have concluded that the State proved beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant was the perpetrator in each of the three robberies. During the trial, the victims of the three armed robberies each identified defendant as the man who robbed him or her at gunpoint. Each of these three victims also viewed an out-of-court photographic lineup and identified defendant as the armed robber. In addition to the victims' identifications, the State introduced evidence of similarities in the three crimes. The trial court's decision to allow the jury to take notes was harmless error.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Nash


No. 36,038-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


36,038 (La.App. 2 Cir. 06/14/02); 821 So. 2d 678; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 1928



June 14, 2002, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of error denied State v. Nash, 2003 La. LEXIS 2150 (La., June 27, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Appealed from the Third Judicial District Court for the Parish of Lincoln, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 45,328. Honorable Cynthia T. Woodard, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a jury trial, defendant was convicted of second degree murder. The Third Judicial District Court for the Parish of Lincoln, Louisiana, imposed the mandatory sentence of life imprisonment without benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence. Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence.


OVERVIEW: The victim was found in her trailer. She had been killed by a slash wound to the neck. Forensic examination revealed defendant's bloody fingerprints on items inside the trailer. Defendant denied knowing the victim. He later stated he and the victim had sexual relations in the trailer two weeks before the murder and that it was the last time he was in the residence. Subsequently, he admitted he was in the victim's trailer the night of the murder. At trial, defendant's wife testified against him. On appeal, defendant argued the evidence was circumstantial regarding his identity as the murderer and did not exclude every reasonable hypothesis of innocence. The appeals court disagreed. Defendant's statement to the police offered no explanation as to why his blood would have commingled with that of the victim if he merely discovered the body. Defendant's identity as the perpetrator of the offense was clearly proven. Further, defendant's right to spousal privilege pertaining to confidential communications was upheld. However, when defendant's wife chose to waive her spousal privilege to not testify against her husband, she was allowed to testify as to non-privileged matters.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Woodberry


No. 2002-K-0994


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2002-0994 (La.App. 4 Cir. 06/05/02); 820 So. 2d 638; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 1876

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 24, 2002.
Writ of error denied State v. Woodberry, 2003 La. LEXIS 780 (La., Mar. 21, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPLICATION FOR WRITS DIRECTED TO CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 371-742, SECTION "C". Honorable Sharon K. Hunter, Judge.
State ex rel. Woodberry v. State, 721 So. 2d 908, 1998 La. LEXIS 2317 (La., July 2, 1998)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was found guilty of sexual battery, crime against nature, second-degree kidnapping, simple robbery, and first degree robbery. The Criminal District Court for the Orleans Parish (Louisiana) denied defendant's post conviction relief application, and defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant asserted five claims in his relief application. First, defendant argued there was no probable cause for the indictment on aggravated rape and second degree kidnapping. The court ruled that the claim obviously could have been raised prior to trial, during the appeal or defendant's first relief application, and as it was not, should have been barred under La. Second, defendant asserted the selection of the grand jury foreperson violated the constitution because of the exclusion of African-Americans. Defendant's fourth claim was that the evidence was insufficient to convict him on the charge of second degree kidnapping, a claim that was barred under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 930.4. Defendant's fifth claim was based on ineffective assistance of counsel, which the court determined was without merit.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Gaspard


No. 2001-KA-1042 C/W No. 2002-KA-172


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


2001-1042 (La.App. 5 Cir. 05/30/02) 820 So. 2d 1095; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 1728



May 29, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 17, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 00-1211, DIVISION "M" AND NO. 00-1210, DIVISION "M". HONORABLE HENRY G. SULLIVAN, JR., JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After defendant pleaded guilty to all charges, the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Jefferson Parish, Louisiana, convicted defendant of misdemeanor hit-and-run driving, misdemeanor battery of a police officer, and felony battery of a police officer. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court ordered defendant's appeals be consolidated. On review, the appellate court found defendant only briefed the conviction for felony battery of a police officer. Therefore, defendant's issues regarding the misdemeanor convictions were considered abandoned. Defendant argued that when she entered her guilty plea, the State failed to articulate sufficient facts to establish a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. 14:34.cB(3), and thus, did not meet its burden. In its brief, the State pointed out that, at the time of her guilty plea, defendant stated the police officer threw her on the ground and that she got up and kicked him twice. The prosecutor stated that the factual basis for the plea was that defendant kicked the officer several times in the groin which caused and required medical attention. The appellate court ruled that this was a sufficient factual basis to establish strong evidence of actual guilt. Thus, defendant's guilty plea to the charge of battery on a police officer requiring medical attention was valid.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Johnson


No. 2001-KA-1455, CONSOLIDATED WITH: No. 2001-KA-1457


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT

May 29, 2002, Decided

PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] APPEAL FROM PLAQUEMINES 25TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. NOS. 99-4439 C/W 2000-1866, DIVISION "B". Honorable William A. Roe, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Plaquemines 25th Judicial District Court, Louisiana, convicted defendant for the distribution of cocaine, pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967(A). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967(A) and sentenced to 30 years at hard labor. Defendant argued that the district court erred in failing to grant his request to include jury instructions on alibi witnesses. Defendant argued that the use of an alibi was more than a defense, but rather it was evidence used to rebut the State's case. Defendant's sentence was not unconstitutionally excessive as the district court articulated specific reasons for the 30-year sentence, and why the statutory minimum sentence was not constitutionally justifiable.

State v. Broussard


No. 99-KA-1054


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


1999-1054 (La.App. 4 Cir. 05/29/02); 819 So. 2d 1141; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 1841



May 22, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 10, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 400-200, SECTION "F". HONORABLE DENNIS J. WALDRON, JUDGE.
 State v. Broussard, 806 So. 2d 663, 2002 La. LEXIS 383 (La. 2002)



DISPOSITION: Vacated and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After denying defendant's motion to suppress, the Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish, Louisiana, convicted defendant of being a felon in possession of a firearm in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:95.1. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress and that the evidence was insufficient to convict him. The evidence showed that the officers stopped defendant and his friends because they were in violation of a curfew. A computer check revealed that defendant had outstanding arrest warrants. Defendant ran away and an officer saw that defendant had a gun. Defendant was arrested and searched. The appellate court found that once the officers found that there was an outstanding warrant, they had probable cause to arrest. The trial court therefore correctly denied the motion to suppress. The appellate court also found the State presented no evidence that defendant was convicted of a prior felony. The officers in fact did not know of what crime defendant had been convicted. The only testimony was hearsay evidence of an unknown police operator that defendant had a record. No proof existed in the record that defendant was the same named person who was convicted of armed robbery in a different parish. Accordingly, defendant's conviction was amended to reflect a conviction for the lesser-included offense of illegal carrying of weapons.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence were vacated and the matter was remanded with instructions that defendant be convicted of illegal carrying of weapons, and sentenced accordingly.
