Medford v. State ex rel. Charity Hosp.


2002 CW 0750


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2002 0750 (La.App. 1 Cir. 05/15/02); 825 So. 2d 1213; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 1416



May 15, 2002, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] ON APPLICATION FOR SUPERVISORY WRIT OF REVIEW TO THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. NUMBER: UNASSIGNED. PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE. STATE OF LOUISIANA. HONORABLE JUDGE: UNASSIGNED.



DISPOSITION: Petitioner's application for supervisory writ of review granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner prisoner sought a supervisory writ of review to the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana, contending that defendants, Clerk of Court, judges, and commissioners, had no legal authority to compel him to file his civil tort suit as a Petition for Judicial Review.


OVERVIEW: A petition for judicial review filed pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:1171 et seq., sought review of a ruling by the Department of Public Safety and Corrections, a state agency. Such review was limited to a review of the administrative record and had to be filed within 30 days of the last administrative decision. The appellate court found that, by using Nineteenth Jud. Dist. Ct., La., Ct. R. XII, the Clerk of Court's office was improperly requiring tort suits to be filed on the forms developed for appellate review of administrative rulings. The forms had to be sufficiently different from the judicial review forms in order to avoid confusion between the two totally separate and distinct types of filings.


OUTCOME: The writ was granted.

Ackel v. Acad. La. Co.


No. 2001-CA-1188


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


2001-1188 (La.App. 5 Cir. 05/15/02); 821 So. 2d 109; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 1452



May 15, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 17, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA. NO. 520-152, DIVISION "F". HONORABLE PATRICK McCABE, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff lessor sued defendant lessee for breach of a lease agreement, and the lessor added Jefferson Parish, alleging an ordinance regulating commercial traffic on residential streets was unconstitutional and or unconstitutionally enforced. The Twenty Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana) granted summary judgment in favor of the lessee and Jefferson Parish, and the lessor appealed.


OVERVIEW: The lessor and lessee entered into a lease for commercial retail space. The lease required the lessor to perform certain improvements to the space and required the lessee to provide other improvements. The lessee informed the lessor it was seeking to cancel the lease, as required improvements were not completed. The appellate court ruled the trial court erred in its finding that the mere fact that building permits were not issued gave the lessee the right to cancel, without consideration of the good faith and diligence of the lessee in attempting to procure the permits. The appellate court further ruled the lessor failed to satisfy her burden of proof that the ordinance was enforced at all against the property. The record did not support the lessor's assertion that the ordinance affected a taking of the property by prohibiting the collection of rent from the space. The lessor did not present any evidence that Jefferson Parish enforced the ordinance or that enforcement as to the property prevented any actual merchandise deliveries at any time.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment in favor of the lessee was reversed and summary judgment in favor of Jefferson Parish was affirmed, and the matter was remanded for further proceedings.

 

1582 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Esteve v. U.S. Agencies Cas. Ins. Co.


NUMBER 2001 CA 1009


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2001 1009 (La.App. 1 Cir. 05/10/02); 818 So. 2d 998; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 1344



May 10, 2002, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 10, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the 17th Judicial District Court In and for the Parish of Lafourche State of Louisiana. Trial Court Number 88266 Division "D". Honorable Ashly Bruce Simpson, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insureds sued appellees, insurer and agent, for underinsured/uninsured (UM) benefits. The 17th Judicial District Court, in and for the Parish of Lafourche, State of Louisiana, granted the insurer's and the agent's summary judgment motion. The insureds appealed.


OVERVIEW: The insureds, who were both retired, made a claim for damages under the underinsured/uninsured (UM) provisions of their automobile policy after a car crashed into their home. The insurer prevailed on a summary judgment motion on the grounds that the insureds selected "economic-only" UM coverage. The insureds' claimed that, because they did not understand the meaning of "non-economic" loss only, they did not have a "meaningful selection." If the insureds did not have a meaningful selection in choosing the UM coverage, the policy form violated case law. The appellate court noted that the insurer's form met all the necessary requirements, as it explained the difference between economic and non-economic coverage. The court also held that the agent was not negligent, as he had no duty to explain to the insureds that the coverage they selected was of little benefit to them. Moreover, the evidence provided indicated that the agent answered all the insureds' questions.


OUTCOME: The grant of summary judgment was affirmed.

 

1583 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Brown v. Grabert


2001 CA 0064


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2001 0064 (La.App. 1 Cir. 05/10/02); 818 So. 2d 872; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 1347



May 10, 2002, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 10, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 32nd Judicial District Court Parish of Terrebonne, Louisiana. Docket No. 114,695. Honorable David Arceneaux, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurer for employer challenged the judgment of the 32nd Judicial District Court for the Parish of Terrebonne (Louisiana) dismissing the claims against the injured employee's attorney and the insurer for the other driver and awarding Moody fees for the attorney.


OVERVIEW: The employee was injured while driving in the course and scope of his employment. When the injured employee failed to make payment to the employer's insurer, pursuant to a settlement agreement, it sought reimbursement from the injured employee, his attorney, and the other driver's insurer, by filing motions to enforce a prior judgment. The attorney's motion to withdraw as counsel based on a conflict of interest was granted, and the injured employee was ordered to deposit money into the court's registry. After withdrawing as counsel, the attorney filed a motion for Moody fees. The court ruled as follows: (1) there was not fair notice that the employer's insurer was attempting to pursue a separate action for damages; (2) if the employer's insurer wished to pursue an action for damages, it had to file suit with the required factual allegations to support its causes of action and effect proper service against the true targets of its action; and (3) the attorney did not provide a sufficient basis for an award of fees.


OUTCOME: The dismissal of the claims was affirmed, and the award of Moody fees was reversed and remanded.

State v. Canada


2001 KA 2674


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2001 2674 (La.App. 1 Cir. 05/10/02); 838 So. 2d 784; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 1356



May 10, 2002, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 10, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 19th Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana. Honorable Todd Hernandez, Judge Presiding. Docket No. 01-01-31.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to carjacking in violation of LA. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:64.2 with the understanding that he would receive a sentence in the range of 3 to 40 years and the other 3 charges against him would be dismissed. The 19th Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana, sentenced defendant to 15 years of imprisonment at hard labor. Defendant filed a motion for reconsideration, which was denied, and he appealed.


OVERVIEW: The record showed that the parties to the plea agreement performed their obligations in good faith. The defendant pled guilty to one count of carjacking; the State dismissed the three other charges against the defendant; and the trial judge imposed a sentence within the range agreed upon by the parties and within the legal sentencing range for carjacking. The appellate court found that: (1) the plea bargain was a contract between the defendant and the State, and the court would not modify the plea agreement; and (2) the defendant could not appeal or seek review of a sentence imposed in conformity with a plea agreement, which was set forth in the record at the time of the plea, pursuant to the provisions of LA. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 881.2(A)(2).


OUTCOME: The judgment of the judicial district court was affirmed.

 

1585 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Womens's Health Clinic v. State


NUMBER 2002 CA 0016


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2002 0016 (La.App. 1 Cir. 05/10/02); 825 So. 2d 1208; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 1358



May 10, 2002, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Appealed from the 19th Judicial District Court In and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana Trial Court Number 482,386 Division "D" Honorable Janice Clark, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED. REMANDED WITH ORDER.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The 19th Judicial District Court In and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana, granted judgment in favor of plaintiffs, women's health clinics, in their suit against defendant State seeking temporary and permanent injunctive relief barring the State from enforcing the provisions of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2800.12. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The State argued that the trial court erred in overruling the State's declinatory exception, raising the objection of lack of subject matter jurisdiction. The appellate court found that it was without jurisdiction to issue or review advisory opinions and could only review matters that were justiciable. The clinics sought to enjoin the State from enforcing La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 2800.12. The statute, however, created a private right of action in favor of women who suffered damage while undergoing an abortion. The statute contained no provision authorizing the State or any of its agencies or officers to enforce, or take any action on, the provisions of the statute. The statute created no apparent dispute between the clinics and the State. The clinics would have the opportunity to present their defenses and seek adequate remedy, if and when private actions were brought against them. It was the private plaintiff, bringing a private lawsuit under the statute, who caused the injury of which the clinics complained. No justiciable controversy existed between the clinics and the State.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

 

1586 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Town of Mamou v. Fontenot


2001-1622


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


01-1622 (La.App. 3 Cir. 05/08/02); 816 So. 2d 958; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 1268



May 8, 2002, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE THIRTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF EVANGELINE, NUMBER 59970-A PRESTON N. AUCOIN, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff town sued defendant town attorney over some property. Third party lawyer, through reconventional demands and other means, became part of the suit, which came to focus on attorney fees. The lawyer settled with the town. On remand, the 13th Judicial District Court, Parish of Evangeline (Louisiana), found the parties' contingent fee contract invalid and awarded attorney fees on the basis of quantum meruit. The town attorney appealed.


OVERVIEW: The town was governed by a mayor and board of aldermen. The lawyer worked for a hospital or nursing home, management over which was transferred from non-profits to a company. The mayor approached the town attorney and lawyer regarding representing the town in accounting and collection efforts as to money due the town from the non-profits. They entered into a contingent fee contract for 25 and 33.3 percent of all collections before and after litigation respectively. The sums involved turned out to be large. External criticism led the mayor to choose not to honor the agreement. The attorney asserted that he should have been paid for the collection of some funds already in the town's possession, as he had to defend against the non-profits' claim for reimbursement. The appellate court found that the attorney was not entitled to a contingent fee over funds he merely transferred from one town account to another. The contingent fee was to be based on amounts recovered, not on accounts receivable assigned to the town in settlement. The contingent fees were reasonable under La. St. Bar. Art. X, R. 1.5(a) for the difficult job. The mayor and board understood the contract.


OUTCOME: The determination that the contingent fee contract was invalid was reversed. Judgment was rendered increasing the attorney fee award from $ 60,875 to $ 159,265, giving the town credit for $ 125,000 previously retained by the town attorney, and awarding him legal interest on that portion of the award not already in his possession from the date of judicial demand until paid in full.

Lucas v. Tenet Health Sys. Hosps., Inc.


No. 2001-CA-2219


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2001-2219 (La.App. 4 Cir. 05/01/02); 818 So. 2d 269; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 1696



May 1, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 2000-832, DIVISION "D-16". Honorable Lloyd J. Medley, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED FOR TRIAL.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, husband and wife, sued defendant blood center and defendant hospital alleging that a blood transfusion which the wife received on March 28, 1986 caused her to contract the hepatitis C virus. The Civil District Court, Orleans Parish, Division D-16, Louisiana, granted an exception of prescription and dismissed the husband and wife's claims against the blood center. The husband and wife appealed.


OVERVIEW: The husband and wife filed their lawsuit on January 24, 2000 alleging that the first time the wife was told she had hepatitis C was on February 5, 1999. At the time of the wife's transfusion LA. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5628 did not apply to blood centers, but in 1990 it was amended to include community blood centers. In 1999 the legislature enacted La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5628.1 (1999) which was a remedial, retroactive statute for pending claims. The appellate court found that: (1) the district court erred in granting the exception of prescription because LA. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5628 was not applicable to claims against a blood center before September 7, 1990, and the husband and wife's claim against the blood center was timely under LA. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5628.1 (1999) because the claim fell within the window of opportunity identified in the statute; and (2) the issue of the constitutionality of the statute was moot.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the civil district court was reversed and remanded.

In re Fleming Applying for Intra Family Adoption of K.D.R.

1590 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Ventress


01-KA-1165


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


01-1165 (La.App. 5 Cir. 04/30/02); 817 So. 2d 377; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 1160



April 30, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA, NUMBER 00-6304, DIVISION "C," HONORABLE ALAN J. GREEN, PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Sentence vacated, remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson, Louisiana, convicted defendant of aggravated flight from an officer, pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. § 14:108.1, and he was resentenced as a third-felony offender to 16 months' imprisonment at hard labor, with credit for time served. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The State contended that the sentence imposed on defendant as a third-felony offender was illegally lenient. The State argued that whether the trial judge erroneously imposed sentence under the multiple offender statute, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1(A)(2)(b)(ii), as amended, or made a downward departure from the mandatory sentence required for third felony offenders, who had a prior conviction for a crime of violence, the trial court erred. The appellate court found that the multiple offender statute was inapplicable. In the enactment of 2001 La. Acts 403, the legislature was cognizant that it was amending a number of criminal statutes, with the intent to prospectively lessen prison overcrowding. The legislature did not intend that the old and new versions of the statute should apply at the same time. Thus, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1, as amended, applied to crimes committed after the effective date of the amendment. Defendant presented no evidence to rebut the presumption that the mandatory sentence of life, without benefits of parole, probation or suspension of sentence, was unconstitutional. A downward departure was unwarranted.


OUTCOME: The sentence was vacated and remanded.

State v. Houston


No. 2002-KA-0255


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2002-0255 (La.App. 4 Cir. 05/17/02); 818 So. 2d 253; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 1524



April 24, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at, Remanded by State v. Houston, 2003 La. App. LEXIS 2864 (La.App. 4 Cir., Oct. 1, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 417-430, SECTION "I". HONORABLE RAYMOND C. BIGELOW, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Conviction affirmed, sentence vacated, remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Criminal District Court, Orleans Parish (Louisiana), denied defendant's motion to suppress a confession and entered a final judgment of conviction after a jury found defendant guilty of attempted possession of cocaine. Both defendant and the State challenged imposition of the sentence.


OVERVIEW: Police were on patrol when they noticed defendant. He was walking in the same direction the officers were driving, and after he glanced over his shoulder and saw them, he seemed to become nervous. He stopped, put his right hand in his pants pocket, removed a bag, dropped it to the sidewalk, and began to walk fast. The bag contained a glass tube. Two conclusive testing procedures on the residue in the tube indicated the substance in the tube was crack cocaine. After defendant was convicted, he was sentenced. The trial court applied the version of a sentencing statute that was not amended until after defendant committed his offense. After a 30-year sentence was imposed, the appellate court found the trial court applied the wrong version of the statute. The appellate court agreed with the State that the trial court was obligated to apply the sentencing statute in effect at the time the offense was committed, especially since the amended statute stated that it applied only prospectively. Since the proper statute required that defendant be sentenced to life in prison because he had been adjudicated to be a fourth felony offender, the case had to be remanded for resentencing.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed, but the sentence was vacated and the case was remanded for resentencing.

State v. Robinson


No. 2001-KA-1458

Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Robinson v. Leblanc, 2007 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 103678 (E.D. La., July 24, 2007)
Related proceeding at Robinson v. Stalder, 21 So. 3d 318, 2008 La. App. LEXIS 1232 (La.App. 1 Cir., 2008)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Robinson v. State, 42 So. 3d 397, 2010 La. LEXIS 1750 (La., 2010)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Robinson v. Rader, 2013 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 92048 (E.D. La., June 10, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] APPEAL FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 344-417, SECTION "B". HONORABLE PATRICK G. QUINLAN, JUDGE.
State ex rel. Robinson v. State, 720 So. 2d 338, 1998 La. LEXIS 1618 (La., May 29, 1998)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of aggravated burglary and attempted simple burglary. The Criminal District Court for the Parish of Orleans (Louisiana) re-sentenced defendant to serve 50 years at hard labor under the Habitual Offender Law, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1. The defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered an elderly woman's home to rob her. Defendant asked for the woman's money and wedding ring. The victim begged defendant not to take her ring, but he forced it off her finger. Defendant was initially sentenced to 25 years and then re-sentenced as a habitual offender to 50 years at hard labor. A different judicial district court granted defendant's motion and ordered that the record be amended to show that he was serving a 25 year term. The court who presided over defendant's trial and original sentencing then granted the State's motion to correct an illegal sentence and re-instated the sentence for 50 years at hard labor. The appellate court dismissed defendant's claim that he was deprived the right to counsel of his choice as defendant failed to show how he was prejudiced by his appointed counsel's representation or that the appointed counsel was incompetent. It was proper for the trial court to re-instate the 50 year sentence as the judicial district that had vacated it had no authority to do so. Defendant's sentence was within the range suggested for his crime as the acts of violence toward the elderly victim justified a sentence at the higher range.


OUTCOME: The re-instatement of the sentence of 50 years at hard labor was affirmed.

Allain v. Martco P'ship


No. 2001 CA 0614


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2001 0614 (La.App. 1 Cir. 04/17/02); 828 So. 2d 587; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 1131



April 17, 2002, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied May 29, 2002, Reported at: 2002 La. App. LEXIS 1937.
Rehearing denied by Allain v. Martco P'ship, 2002 La. App. LEXIS 1937 (La.App. 1 Cir., May 29, 2002)
Appeal granted by Allain v. Martco P'ship, 826 So. 2d 1132, 2002 La. LEXIS 2895 (La., Oct. 4, 2002)
Reversed by Allain v. Martco P'ship on Appeal, 2003 La. LEXIS 1616 (La., May 23, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the Eighteenth Judicial District Court, in and for the Parish of Iberville, State of Louisiana. Trial Court No. 44,321. Honorable J. Robin Free, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Motion denied in part and granted in part; reversed and rendered; LSA-R.S. 3:4278.2 declared unconstitutional.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff minority timber land co-owners sued defendant timber partnership in the Eighteenth Judicial District Court, in and for the Parish of Iberville (Louisiana), to annul the sale of timber by the majority owners to the partnership. The majority owners were not parties to the lawsuit. The trial court rendered judgment in favor of the partnership. The minority owners appealed.


OVERVIEW: The minority landowners contended that the sale was invalid for three reasons: (1) the consideration for the sale was so inadequate as to constitute lesion beyond moiety; (2) the partnership did not strictly comply with the provisions of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 3:4278.2; and (3) La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 3:4278.2 was unconstitutional. The trial court chose to reject the minority landowners' expert testimony regarding the value of the timber and to accept the testimony of the other foresters. The appellate court found no manifest error in the trial court's decision that the price paid by the partnership was not less than 50 percent of the fair market value and thus was not lesionary. The appellate court rejected the minority landowners' second argument finding that the partnership offered the same terms and conditions to them as to the majority owners and thus the partnership complied fully with the provisions of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 3:4278.2. The appellate court held the statute was unconstitutional in that it denied the minority landowners procedural due process protections because the majority owners could always foreclose any meaningful challenge to their decision to sell timber.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed. The appellate court rendered judgment declaring the statute unconstitutional, and rendered judgment in favor of the minority owners against the partnership in the sum of $ 218,295.

Civil Serv. Comm'n v. City of New Orleans


No. 2001-CA-0635


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2001-0635 (La.App. 4 Cir. 04/10/02); 826 So. 2d 23; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 1532



April 10, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ granted by Civil Serv. Comm'n of New Orleans v. City of New Orleans, 828 So. 2d 581, 2002 La. LEXIS 3177 (La., Nov. 1, 2002)
Writ granted by Civil Serv. Comm'n of New Orleans v. City of New Orleans, 828 So. 2d 581, 2002 La. LEXIS 3178 (La., Nov. 1, 2002)
Affirmed in part and remanded in part by Civil Serv. Comm'n v. City of New Orleans, 2003 La. LEXIS 2334 (La., Sept. 9, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] APPEAL FROM CIVIL DISTRICT COURT, ORLEANS PARISH. NO. 2000-16933, DIVISION "G-11". Honorable Robin M. Giarrusso, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff civil service commission (commission) sued defendant city, seeking to enjoin the effect of a management agreement entered into between the city and a management company. The agreement privatized operation of the city-owned cultural center. The Civil District Court, Orleans Parish, Division G-11, rendered judgment in favor of the commission. The city and the management company appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court enjoined the city and the management company, inter alia, from discharging any management company employee formerly employed by the city without the approval of the commission until the commission approved the privatization contract. The appellate court held that both the civil service system and the New Orleans Home Rule government system were creatures of the Louisiana Constitution. The commission's rules on privatization contracts related immediately to the selection, hiring, promotion, and demotion of public employees. The employees covered by the rules were classified civil service employees, working for the city's department of property management. The rules protected those classified employees from an administration that would use privatization as a means of eliminating civil service protection of the employees and defeating the objectives of providing for selection, hiring, promotion, and demotion on the basis of merit. The privatization rules were squarely within the constitutional authority granted to the commission and to the authority granted to the commission by the New Orleans Home Rule Charter, and the commission's rules had the effect of law.


OUTCOME: The district court was affirmed.

State v. Hicks


No. 01-KA-1064


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIFTH CIRCUIT


01-1064 (La.App. 5 Cir. 04/10/02); 817 So. 2d 192; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 986



April 10, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. Hicks, 845 So. 2d 1068, 2003 La. LEXIS 1741 (La., May 30, 2003)
Related proceeding at State v. Mills, 2005 La. App. LEXIS 714 (La.App. 5 Cir., Mar. 29, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON, STATE OF LOUISIANA, NO. 99-7491 - DIVISION "P". HONORABLE MELVIN C. ZENO, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was found guilty of manslaughter by a Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), jury and sentenced to 40 years at hard labor. The State filed a multiple offender bill of information alleging defendant to be a third felony offender. The trial court vacated defendant's original sentence and imposed an enhanced sentence of life imprisonment without parole. Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended the evidence was insufficient to convict him of manslaughter, as he did not have the requisite intent to kill the victim. He argued the shooter twisted his hand and then ripped the gun from it. Defendant was present when the shooter and the victim began arguing. Defendant then left the room and retrieved a gun from the shooter's car. The jury concluded that defendant willingly and knowingly provided the shooter with the weapon that he used to kill the victim, a conclusion the appellate court found was supported by the record. Defendant did nothing to assist the victim after the shooting. He did not call the police and left immediately after the crime with the shooter. Defendant argued his life sentence as a third felony offender was constitutionally excessive. Because his underlying felony was a crime of violence, the multiple offender statute mandated a life sentence. Defendant made no showing of exceptional circumstances to justify a downward departure from the required minimum sentence. He presented no evidence or argument at the time of sentencing regarding a downward departure. The appellate court concluded defendant's life sentence was not excessive.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence were affirmed.

Plaquemines Parish Gov't v. State


No. 2001-CA-1027, No. 2001-CA-1028


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FOURTH CIRCUIT


2001-1027 (La.App. 4 Cir. 04/10/02); 826 So. 2d 14; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 1539; 155 Oil & Gas Rep. 259



April 10, 2002, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] APPEAL FROM PLAQUEMINES 25TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT. NOS. 33-953 C/W 34-211, DIVISION "A". HONORABLE ANTHONY RAGUSA, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The 25th Judicial Court, Plaquemines Parish, Louisiana, granted judgment in favor of appellee parish government in its petition for declaratory judgment asking the trial court to declare it to be owner of certain property over appellant state. The state appealed.


OVERVIEW: The state argued that the trial court erred in its denial of the state's peremptory exception raising the objection of no right of action and in its ruling that the government obtained ownership of certain minerals affecting the property when the board of commissioners merged into the parish government. The appellate court found that the state conveyed the tract to the board in 1938, which granted a mineral lease, including the disputed tract. The board was later consolidated into the parish government. Thus, the government had obtained ownership of certain mineral rights affecting the tract when the board merged. There was a genuine factual issue as to causation of the land loss, because there was no evidence as to exactly how the tract came to be covered by the open waters of the Gulf of Mexico. La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:1152 applied because a mineral lease was granted on the land that became water bottoms, which were retained by the government. The state could not challenge the constitutionality of the statute. The trial court did not have to describe the boundaries of the tract as it was not one that affected title to immovable property.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1598 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Jordan


No. 35,643-KA


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, SECOND CIRCUIT


35,643 (La.App. 2 Cir. 04/03/02); 813 So. 2d 1123; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 930



April 3, 2002, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. Jordan, 845 So. 2d 1067, 2003 La. LEXIS 1740 (La., May 30, 2003)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Jordan v. Cain, 2006 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 78508 (W.D. La., Aug. 29, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Appealed from the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo, Louisiana. Trial Court No. 204712. Honorable Ramona L. Emanuel, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was found guilty of armed robbery. The First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo (Louisiana) denied defendant's motions for a new trial and for post-verdict judgment of acquittal and sentenced him to serve 58 years at hard labor without the benefit of parole, probation, or suspension of sentence, and it denied his motion to reconsider sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: At gunpoint, two assailants demanded the victim's car keys, billfold, and money. While the assailants were having difficulty unlocking the victim's vehicle, he escaped and witnessed his vehicle being driven away from the scene. The court ruled that, based upon the record, the jury could have reasonably found that the State negated any reasonable probability of misidentification. Viewing the evidence in a light most favorable to the State, rational jurors could have found the essential elements of armed robbery proven beyond a reasonable doubt. There was sufficient evidence to support the jury's finding that defendant was the individual who took the victim's property by the use of force or intimidation while armed with a handgun. There was no err in denying defendant's motion in limine to exclude the in-court identification. A review of the testimony showed defendant did not satisfy his burden of proving that the in-court identification was suggestive and that there was a substantial likelihood of misidentification. Furthermore, the sentence imposed was neither grossly disproportionate to the severity of the offense nor shocking to the sense of justice.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1599 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Allien


01-1509


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, THIRD CIRCUIT


01-1509 (La.App. 3 Cir. 04/03/02); 814 So. 2d 743; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 944



April 3, 2002, Rendered


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-EIGHTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT, PARISH OF LASALLE, NO. 65806. HONORABLE JOHN PHILLIP MAUFFRAY, JR., DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by the 28th Judicial District Court, Parish of La Salle, Louisiana, of operating a vehicle while intoxicated, third offense, and sentenced to a 5-year prison sentence at hard labor with 30 months suspended, in-patient treatment for alcohol abuse, and supervised probation. Defendant appealed that his sentence was excessive in light of a change to the statutory sentencing provisions effective after the date of his offense.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued on appeal that a change made subsequent to his offense in the sentencing provisions of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:98, to require that only 30 days of a prison sentence be imposed without the benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence, instead of the 6 months previously required, required the trial court to reconsider his sentence. The appellate court held that because the trial court sentenced the defendant pursuant to the statute in effect at the time of his offense, it did not commit a manifest abuse of discretion by denying his motion for reconsideration. In considering the constitutional excessiveness of defendant's sentence, the appellate court noted, as had the trial court, that the defendant's record contained nine alcohol-related arrests and that because of his alcohol abuse, the defendant did not contemplate the serious threat that his behavior was to others. Defendant's sentence was within the sentencing guidelines of § 14:98 at the time of the offense. Although defendant contended in mitigation of his sentence that he was not involved in an accident at the time of the stop, the sentence was neither excessive, nor unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed defendant's convictions.

 

1600 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Weller v. Brown


NUMBER 2001 CA 0314


COURT OF APPEAL OF LOUISIANA, FIRST CIRCUIT


2001 0314 (La.App. 1 Cir. 03/28/02); 813 So. 2d 635; 2002 La. App. LEXIS 904



March 28, 2002, Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Later proceeding at La. Ins. Guar. Ass'n v. Weller, 2007 La. App. LEXIS 2047 (La.App. 1 Cir., Nov. 2, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] Appealed from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court In and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge. Suit Number 200,984. Honorable Jewel E. "Duke" Welch, Jr., Judge.
Weller v. Brown, 724 So. 2d 230, 1998 La. App. LEXIS 3451 (La.App. 1 Cir., Nov. 6, 1998)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Nineteenth Judicial District Court in and for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana, nullified and vacated its previous judgment in favor of appellants, insurer and employer, for lack of subject matter jurisdiction in favor of appellee employee. The insurer and employer appealed.


OVERVIEW: Appellants contended that the trial court erred in holding that the Nineteenth Judicial District Court did not have subject matter jurisdiction to hear the insurer's petition to terminate and/or modify workers' compensation benefits. Appellants asserted that the ground for nullity appeared in the record, that the date of injury was in 1976, and therefore La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 2005 applied and precluded the employee from seeking annulment of the 1997 judgment. The appellate court found, however, that appellants failed to recognize that the codal provision suggested that the restrictions listed were disjunctive. Therefore, even though the ground for nullity appeared in the record of appeal, so long as the appellate court did not consider the ground, an action of nullity could be sought. A petition filed after January 1, 1990, seeking modification of a prior district court judgment had to be heard by the Louisiana Office of Workers' Compensation Administration (OWC). The insurer filed a petition after the date seeking termination of the employee's benefits; therefore the OWC had exclusive jurisdiction to hear the petition for modification.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.
